1201 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thompson


C8-92-222


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


486 N.W.2d 163; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 601



June 3, 1992, Decided  
June 9, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court. Hennepin County. Hon. Charles A. Porter, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) that revoked his probation, and his sentence imposed by the trial court upon his conviction of first-degree sale of crack cocaine in violation of Minn. Stat. § 152.021, subd. 1(1) (Supp. 1989).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to concurrent prison terms for his conviction of one count of first-degree controlled substance crime and one count of second-degree controlled substance crime. The trial court stayed execution of sentence and placed defendant on probation for 15 years. Two probation revocation hearings were held, and on both occasions when defendant admitted to violating his probation, the trial court ordered additional days of incarceration and reinstated probation. The trial court also ordered defendant to attend a specific drug treatment program. After defendant enrolled in the program, the county decided to have no more contact with the program. The trial court revoked defendant's probation and found that defendant's previous violations justified imprisonment for 86 months. The court held that the trial court properly revoked defendant's probation not because of his inability to attend a treatment program, but rather because the sentencing alternative was no longer available. The court found that the distinction between crack and powder cocaine no longer existed, and defendant could only be sentenced for one second-degree penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for resentencing.

 

1202 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Mitchell v. Steffen


C3-92-239


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


487 N.W.2d 896; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 597



June 2, 1992, Decided  
June 9, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Mitchell v. Steffen, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 575 (Minn., Aug. 4, 1992)
Affirmed by Mitchell v. Steffen, 504 N.W.2d 198, 1993 Minn. LEXIS 517 (Minn., 1993)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court. Ramsey County. Hon. Michael T. DeCourcy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant department of human services and respondents both sought review of a decision of the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which ruled that the case should proceed as a class action suit and granted summary judgment to respondents on the claim that the statute was unconstitutional under the Equal Protection Clause of the United States Constitution, but denied their claim for retroactive benefits.


OVERVIEW: Respondents' challenged the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 256D.065 (1991), on the grounds that it implicated the right to travel and violated the Equal Protection Clause of the United States Constitution. Respondents alleged that the statute violated the equal protection clause of the Minnesota Constitution, and the Privileges and Immunities Clause of the United States Constitution. Respondents sought injunctive and declaratory relief and an award of retroactive benefits for class members. The court held that where a state law unequally distributes benefits among otherwise qualified bona fide residents, it not only raised equal protection concerns, but also impermissibly infringed on the constitutionally protected right to travel. Respondents sought enforcement of the prior statute, and requested that the department reimburse them the amount mandated by law to pay under that prior statute. The court held that the relief requested was equitable relief in the form of specific performance, not money damages, and was not barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The court reversed the district court's refusal to award retroactive benefits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment, but reversed the trial court's refusal to award retroactive benefits, and remanded.

 

1203 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Simon


C0-90-2705


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


485 N.W.2d 719; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 489



May 13, 1992, Decided  
May 19, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, Affirmed in part and modified in part by State v. Simon, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 647 (Minn., July 16, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Aitkin County; Hon. Clinton W. Wyant, Judge. District Court #K9-89-433



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction after a jury trial, by the District Court, Aitkin County (Minnesota). Defendant was convicted of driving while under the influence in violation of Minn. Stat. § 169.121, subd. 1(a) and subd. 3(b) (1989) and refusal to submit to testing in violation of Minn. Stat. § 169.121, subd. 1a and subd. 3(c) (1989).


OVERVIEW: An officer placed defendant under arrest for driving while under the influence of alcohol and read him an implied consent advisory. Defendant was given a choice of a blood or urine test, but he refused to submit to either test. Defendant moved to suppress the evidence of his refusal. The trial court found some statements were obtained in violation of defendant's right to have counsel present during questioning. However, the statements made during the implied consent advisory were ruled admissible. The court disagreed with defendant's arguments on appeal and affirmed. The court held that the trial court did not err in admitting the evidence of refusal or the tape of the implied consent advisory because defendant failed to assert in the trial court that the request for a test was a critical stage under Minn. Const. art. I, § 6. In addition, the request to undergo testing did not constitute interrogation and a Miranda warning was not required. The trial court did not err in sentencing defendant to consecutive terms because driving under the influence and refusing testing were not part of a single behavioral incident and did not arise out of a continuous course of conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

 

1204 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Midwest Family Mut. Ins. Co. v. Bleick


C9-91-1921


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


486 N.W.2d 435; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 480



May 12, 1992, Decided  
May 19, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition Granted in Part and Denied in Part July 27, 1992, Reported at 1992 Minn. LEXIS 194.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Renville County; Hon. John J. Weyrens, Judge. District Court File No. C190631



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer challenged an order of the District Court, Renville County (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment to respondent insured, after determining that the insurer was obligated to provide an additional sum of money in "add-on" to its underinsured motorist coverage as a result of an accident in which the insured was killed.


OVERVIEW: The personal representative of the deceased contended that the insurer should pay the heirs of the deceased an additional sum of money as "add-on" to the underinsured motorist (UIM) coverage because of a change in the law that occurred when Minn. Stat. § 65B.49(4a) was amended. These amendments changed UIM coverage from "difference of limits" coverage to "add-on" coverage. The insurer contended that the insurance policy should be governed by the statutes in effect on the date of the issuance of the policy, not the date of the accident. The court held on appeal that the statutory amendment applied because the fact that a pre-existing insurance contract was affected did not make application of the statute to the accident and death occurring after the statute's effective date a retroactive application of the statute. Applying the three-part test used to determine whether a contractual impairment was unconstitutional, the court also held that there was no impairment of contract under the contracts clause of the United States Constitution and the Minnesota Constitution. The legislation was reasonably and appropriately tailored to meet its stated goals.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court and the insurer's obligation to pay the additional sum as "add-on" to the insured's underinsured motorist coverage.

 

1205 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Amdahl v. Stonewall Ins. Co.


CX-91-2074


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


484 N.W.2d 811; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 474



May 4, 1992, Decided  
May 12, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Amdahl v. Stonewall Ins. Co., 1992 Minn. LEXIS 440 (Minn., July 16, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Dakota County; Hon. Harvey A. Holtan, Judge. District Court #C3907244



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance company sought review of a District Court, Dakota County (Minnesota) that denied its motion to dismiss the suit as untimely and for insufficient service of process. The action was brought by respondent receiver asserting the insured's claim against appellant for failure to settle claims within the limits of the insured's policy.


OVERVIEW: Respondent receiver brought an action asserting the insured's claim against appellant insurance company for failure to settle claims within the limits of the insured's policy. Appellant sought review of the decision that denied its motion to dismiss the suit as untimely and for insufficient service of process. In affirming the decision, the court ruled that because the final outcome of the original action was probative of the reasonableness of appellant's refusal to settle, the insured did not know if it had a viable claim until the appellate process was complete. The court agreed that the limitations period on a bad-faith failure to settle a claim did not begin to run until the appellate process was complete and final judgment was entered. The court stated that the failure to stay entry of the underlying judgment on appeal did not determine finality for purposes of limitation of actions. The court held the executive secretary to appellant's president had implied, if not express, authority to accept service because her written job description charged her with the duty of controlling suits and legal paper flow within the company.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court because statute of limitations did not begin to run on the claim against appellant for bad-faith failure to settle until the appellate process was complete. The court ruled service of process of appellant's secretary was proper because she had routinely accepted service of process for appellant.

 

1206 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Minnesota Fed'n of Teachers v. Mammenga


C0-91-2357


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


485 N.W.2d 305; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 421



April 21, 1992, Decided  
April 28, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.
Review denied by, Request denied by Minn. Fed'n of Teachers v. Mammenga, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 497 (Minn., June 30, 1992)
Appeal after remand at Minnesota Fed'n of Teachers v. Mammenga, 500 N.W.2d 136, 1993 Minn. App. LEXIS 530 (Minn. Ct. App., 1993)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. Michael M. Monahan, Judge. Dist. Ct. File No. C3913272



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as to respondents other than Bethel College. Reversed and remanded as to respondent Bethel College.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of an order from the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent colleges in appellants' action challenging the constitutionality of the Post-Secondary Enrollment Options Act (PSEOA), Minn. Stat. § 123.3514 (1990), under the establishment of religion clauses, Minn. Const. art. 1, § 16, and art. 13, § 2.


OVERVIEW: The PSEOA allowed 11th and 12th grade high school students in the public schools to take courses at eligible colleges or universities for credit while the state paid the costs. Appellants contended that PSEOA violated the establishment of religion clauses of the Minnesota Constitution. A federal action filed by appellants on the basis of the federal Constitution's Establishment Clause was disposed of on summary judgment. Appellants then sued the colleges in state court, alleging that the PSEOA violated the Minnesota Constitution. One count of appellants' complaint was dismissed voluntarily. The trial court granted summary judgment as to the other counts. Appellants challenged the grant of summary judgment. The court held that the trial court did not err in holding that the PSEOA did not violate the establishment of religion clauses of the Minnesota Constitution. The PSEOA was neutral in defining the institutions that could participate in the program. Any potential benefits to the colleges were indirect and incidental.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment as to all except one of the colleges. As to that college, the court reversed and remanded.

 

1207 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Thomas v. St. Paul Fire Dep't Relief Ass'n


C9-91-2163


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 406



April 10, 1992, Decided  
April 21, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Thomas v. St. Paul Fire Dep't Relief Ass'n, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 434 (Minn., June 16, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. Mary L. Klas, Judge. District Court File #C2914087



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, three municipal firefighters who served for less than 10 years, sought review of an order of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which, relying on Minn. Stat. § 69.45 (1990), granted summary judgment to appellee, the fire department relief association (association), in the firefighters' declaratory judgment action to recover their mandatory pension contributions.


OVERVIEW: Three city firefighters with under 10 years service brought a declaratory judgment action to recover their mandatory pension contributions. The trial court, which relied on Minn. Stat. § 69.45, granted the association summary judgment despite the claim that the statute was unconstitutional and that promissory estoppel required the association to make the refund. The court disagreed, reasoning that the legislature's 1953 repeal of Minn. Stat. § 69.12, which allowed for a refund of pension contributions when an association member ceased for any reason being a member of the fire department, evidenced an intention to bar such refunds. The court, applying the rational basis test to the firefighters' challenge of § 69.45 on equal protection grounds, ruled that there was a legitimate state interest in preserving existing contract rights. Moreover, the statute's 20-year service requirement was not unconstitutional under the contract clause as it did not impair the firefighters' contractual right to pension benefits, only conditioned it. The argument that promissory estoppel required the association to make a refund lacked merit, as it made no promise to do so before 20 years expired.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order granting the fire department relief association summary judgment in the firefighters' declaratory relief action to recover their mandatory pension contributions.

 

1208 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gonzales


C8-91-1991


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


483 N.W.2d 736; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 365



April 6, 1992, Decided  
April 14, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Request denied by State v. Gonzales, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 858 (Minn., June 10, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. Charles A. Flinn, Jr., Judge. District Court File 9100358, 9100432



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered in the negative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged forfeiture of his truck, approved by the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which found valid and constitutional St. Paul, Minn., Legislative Code § 279 (1990), which required the forfeiture of motor vehicles driven by the customers of prostitutes. The trial court also rejected defendant's motion to suppress the handgun and the cocaine found when his truck was searched.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested during a St. Paul vice unit prostitution sting operation. His truck was seized under the city's forfeiture ordinance, St. Paul, Minn., Legislative Code § 279. Defendant moved to suppress the handgun and the cocaine found when his truck was searched on the ground that the forfeiture ordinance was void as preempted by state law. The trial court, and the State on appeal, defined the subject matter as forfeitures arising from prostitution convictions. Because the legislature provided forfeitures for some but not for all prostitution offenses, the State asserted the subject matter had not been preempted. The court disagreed. The legislature had the power to exercise its judgment and exclude some offenses from the statute without leaving them open to municipal enactment. The subject matter to be regulated was the forfeiture of property used in, or associated with, criminal offenses. The court agreed with defendant that the listing of forfeitures for a wide variety of criminal offenses, including murder, promotion of prostitution, bribery, and receiving stolen property, was so comprehensive as to indicate a legislative intention to preempt the field.


OUTCOME: The court held that the forfeiture ordinance was unconstitutional; it was preempted by state law and was not a valid enactment.

 

1209 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Blilie


C6-91-2444


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


484 N.W.2d 34; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 370



April 6, 1992, Decided  
April 14, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by In re Blilie, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 485 (Minn., June 16, 1992)
Affirmed by In re Blilie, 494 N.W.2d 877, 1993 Minn. LEXIS 9 (Minn., 1993)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon J. Jerome Plunkett, Judge. District Court File 169489



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ward sought review of a judgment of commitment of the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which denied her petition, pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 252A.19, subd. 2 (1990), for a declaratory judgment, an injunction, and an order to show cause. She challenged her public guardianship, which was created under Minn. Stat. § 525.753 (1949), and the administration of neuroleptic medication upon her guardian's consent without court review.


OVERVIEW: The ward was committed in 1952 as a mentally deficient person. She urged that her public guardianship was terminated when the statute, which created her guardianship, was repealed. At the time of the instant proceeding, she was subject to the guardianship of the Commissioner of Human Services (Minnesota) under Minn. Stat. ch. 252A (1990). She also argued that Minn. Stat. § 253B.03, subd. 6a (Supp. 1991) violated her constitutional right to privacy by authorizing her treatment with neuroleptic medication upon the consent of Commissioner, as her guardian, absent a court order or appointment of a guardian ad litem. She claimed that the Commissioner was in a position of conflict of interest, since it would be authorizing its own employees to administer the medication. The court affirmed the decisions of the district court. Her public guardianship had not expired. Further, because § 253B.03, subd. 6a allowed consent to treatment to be given either by the ward or the guardian, there was no concern about the unrestrained discretion of medical personnel. Nor was there any indication that a conflict of interest, in fact, existed on the part of the Commissioner.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the district court, denying the ward's petition for a declaratory judgment that her public guardianship terminated upon repeal of the statute under which the guardianship was created. The court affirmed the district court's decision that the statute permitting administration of neuroleptic medication to her upon her consent or that of her guardian was not unconstitutional. A placement issue was found to be moot.

 

1210 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Ritter v. Abbey-Etna Machine Co.


C2-91-1940


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


483 N.W.2d 91; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 340; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P13,175



March 31, 1992, Decided  
April 7, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Ritter v. Abbey-Etna Mach. Co., 1992 Minn. LEXIS 835 (Minn., June 10, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Eugene Minenko, Judge. DC File #91-007190



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mill manufacturer challenged the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota)order denying its summary judgment motion based on Minn. Stat. § 541.051, subd. 1 (1986), the statute of repose, in respondent employee's action to recover for injuries on theories of negligence, strict liability and breach of warranties, and failure to warn against the manufacturer and defendants, mill distributor and mill components manufacturer.


OVERVIEW: The employee sued the manufacturer, distributor, and component manufacturer of the steel mill in which he got his hand caught and had his hand and arm injured. The court affirmed denial of the manufacturer's motion for summary judgment based on the statute of repose. The statute had to be strictly construed, using a common sense analysis utilizing no technical legal construction. The court agreed that the mill was not an improvement to real property that subjected the action to the 10 year repose limitation. Reviewing other cases that determined what improvements were, the court found the steel tube mill was unlike an overhead crane, sewer system, light fixture, or an electrical system. The mill was essentially production machinery and was not an integral part of the employer's building. The court found legislative history of § 541.051 buttressed the conclusion. After the statute was found unconstitutional, it was amended to include parties that furnished materials, but the intent was still to only protect a limited class of parties that helped complete the work and then abandoned and turned over control to the property owner, and the manufacturer did not fit in that class.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the manufacturer's motion for summary judgment that alleged that the employee's claims were barred by the 10 year statute of repose for improvements to real property.

 

1211 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Perillo v. Brooklyn Park


C3-91-1817


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 252



March 18, 1992, Decided  
March 24, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Philip D. Bush, Judge. DC File No. 8918993



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant arrestees, who claimed to have been beaten as they were arrested by respondent police officers who were employed by respondent city, complained of a grant by the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), of a final partial summary judgment in favor of the city on arrestees' 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims, which alleged that the city unconstitutionally authorized its police officers to use excessive force.


OVERVIEW: The arrestees alleged nine incidents of excessive force occurred in the city over a period of seven years. The record showed five of the incidents resulted in investigation and action by the city and the possibility of four uninvestigated incidents over seven years. The record clearly did not support the theory that the police officers had persistent and widespread practices of excessive force. The arrestees presented no evidence that the training was inadequate or that any lack of training was the "moving force" behind the alleged constitutional violation. There was also no evidence that the city was deliberately indifferent to allegations of constitutional violation; the evidence showed to the contrary. Specifically, the city's police chief confirmed that complaints had been filed, but he also indicated that the complaints had been handled in a proper manner. This assertion was unrebutted, and instead of showing indifference, it established that the complaints were investigated. There was no conflicting evidence of a violation of constitutional rights by the city; consequently, summary judgment in favor of the city was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1212 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Mrozka v. Archdiocese of St. Paul & Minneapolis


C6-91-1441, C9-91-1515, C0-91-1516


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


482 N.W.2d 806; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 298



March 18, 1992, Decided  
March 24, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Request denied by Mroska v. Archdiocese of St. Paul & Minneapolis, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 744 (Minn., May 15, 1992)
Related proceeding at Diocese of Winona v. Interstate Fire & Cas. Co., 858 F. Supp. 1407, 1994 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 8555 (D. Minn., 1994)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Anoka County; Hon. Phyllis G. Jones, Judge. District Court File #C68912659



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court, Anoka County (Minnesota) remitted the punitive damage award against respondent religious organization to appellant child abuse victim. Appellant challenged the remittitur of damages and respondent challenged the punitive damage award as contrary to public policy and both the Minn. Const. and U.S. Const. Appellant's parents challenged the trial court's dismissal of their claim for intentional infliction of emotional distress.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was awarded punitive damages against respondent, which challenged the award as contrary to the evidence, Minnesota public policy, and both state and federal constitutional provisions. Appellant challenged the award reduction resulting from the district court's remittitur. Appellant's parents challenged the district court's dismissal of their intentional infliction of emotional distress claim. The court affirmed the district court's decision imposing the punitive damage award and determined that there was no religious organization exemption from the punitive damage award, that the award regarded a secular matter, and that it caused no excessive government entanglement with religion under either the Free Exercise or Establishment Clauses of the U.S. Const. While Minn. Const. art. I, § 16 precluded religious infringement, it excluded licentious acts as protected conduct. The court found the district court did not abuse its discretion in remitting the damage award which was based on respondent's ability to pay and the likelihood of deterrence, and also held that dismissal of the emotional distress claim was proper due to lack of evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the punitive damage award against respondent based on the court's determination that it was not violative of Minnesota public policy or either the Minnesota or U.S. Constitutions. The court also upheld the circuit court's remittitur of appellant's award and its dismissal of the claim made by appellant's parents for intentional infliction of emotional distress based on lack of evidence.

 

1213 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Salo v. Hansen


C9-91-2034, C0-91-2035


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 251



March 13, 1992, Decided  
March 24, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Daniel R. Hart, Judge. District Court File #898700. District Court File #898701



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, individually and as parent and guardian of a minor, sought review of a decision of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment to respondents, police officer, the police department, and the city, and dismissed their claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and the equal protection clause. Appellant minor argued error in granting summary judgment on her claim of negligent infliction of emotional distress.


OVERVIEW: Appellants argued the trial court erred in granting summary judgment to the police officer and the city on their claims of excessive force under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. One of the appellants also sought recovery for property damage she incurred as a result of allegedly excessive police force. The court stated that there was no record evidence that the appellant's property was intentionally damaged by the police officers and therefore she did not have a viable § 1983 claim. The minor alleged that she experienced bad dreams and emotional trauma as a result of seeing her father beaten by the officer. The court stated that the was no U.S. Const. amend. XIV liberty interest in being free of emotional trauma caused by observing allegedly excessive police force directed at a parent. The court noted that appellants failed to name the unidentified officers and that without an identification of the officers int was not possible to hold the city responsible for the unidentified officers' conduct. With respect to appellants' equal protection claims, the court stated that there was no evidence that the alleged assaults were racially motivated and therefore summary judgment was properly granted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision.

 

1214 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Peltier v. Maplewood Police Civil Service Com.


C7-91-1500


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 259



March 12, 1992, Decided  
March 24, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Request denied by Peltier v. Maplewood Police Civ. Serv. Comm'n, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 781 (Minn., June 10, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to Maplewood Police Civil Service Commission



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator police sergeant sought review of an order from respondent city police civil service commission (Minnesota), affirming an order of the city chief of police, which suspended the police sergeant for five days based on a finding that he left his supervisory post during a critical situation.


OVERVIEW: When the police sergeant left early while a shooting incident was under investigation, the city police captain suspended the sergeant for five days without pay even though the sergeant claimed that he was justified in leaving early because he was very tired, had a migraine headache, and the situation was under the control of other officers. The sergeant appealed to the city police civil service commission, which affirmed the suspension. The sergeant appealed, arguing that he was denied substantive due process because the standards, which he was accused of violating, were unconstitutionally vague and ambiguous. The court held that there was substantial evidence supporting the commission's finding that the situation was anything but quiet when the sergeant left his post. The court determined that the early leave policy was not vague in that there were numerous references in police manuals and regulations requiring police sergeants to "guide, train, direct and motivate" junior officers, and to "use sound judgment in emergency situations. Thus, the court found no fault in the procedure followed by the commission.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the commission.

 

1215 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Pahlen v. Commissioner of Public Safety


CX-91-1345


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


482 N.W.2d 493; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 231



March 11, 1992, Decided  
March 17, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Polk County; Hon. Michael J. Kraker, Judge. District Court #C3-91-323



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant appealed an order from the District Court, Polk County (Minnesota), denying his motion for a new trial in an implied consent matter involving the decision of respondent, the commissioner of public safety, in revoking the claimant's driver's license.


OVERVIEW: The claimant's driver's license was revoked, pursuant to the implied consent law, and he petitioned for judicial review. The trial court sustained the revocation and the claimant unsuccessfully moved for a new trial, and he appealed denial of the motion for a new trial. The commissioner moved to dismiss the appeal, contending that it was improper. The claimant moved for temporary reinstatement of his license pending resolution and later moved to expedite the decision and waive a required out-patient program. The court held that an appeal could be taken from an order denying a new trial motion in an implied consent proceeding. Yet where the claimant did not raise the state constitutional right to counsel issue in his petition for judicial review or at the hearing, the claimant did not claim that he made a request for counsel at the time of the test request. The court denied the claimant's motion for reinstatement of his driver's license pending disposition of the appeal, and the issue as to whether the claimant should be required to complete an out-patient treatment program was raised for the first time on appeal. Thus, it was not properly before the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order, sustaining the revoking of the claimant's driver's license.

 

1216 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State, Department of Human Rights v. Hibbing Taconite Co.


C3-91-1798, C1-91-1816


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


482 N.W.2d 504; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 227; 58 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P41,526



March 10, 1992, Decided  
March 17, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Hibbing Taconite Co., 1992 Minn. LEXIS 852 (Minn., May 15, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari to Department of Human Rights. File Nos. HR-81-017-PE and 4-1700-455-2



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator employer sought review of the decision of respondent, Department of Human Rights (Minnesota), that found that it had unlawfully discriminated against the claimants, individuals who had been denied employment, on the basis of disability and that ordered compensatory damages in the form of back pay.


OVERVIEW: The employer argued that its decisions not to hire the claimants were justified as a "serious threat" as permitted by Minn. Stat. § 363.03, subd. 5 (1982). The court agreed and reversed the judgment. The court explained that to prove a condition constituted a serious threat, an employer had to show that it relied upon competent medical advice that there existed a reasonably probable risk of serious harm. The court opined that an employer who had relied upon competent medical advice that there existed a reasonably probable risk of serious harm should be allowed some discretion in determining whether an individual should be disqualified from employment. The court found that an employer need not establish to a certainty that its decision was sound. The court stated that if an employer erred at all, it should be allowed to err on the side of safety. As such, because the employer provided competent medical advice that individuals with certain back problems posed a serious threat to themselves and other workers, the court opined that the employer met its burden under the "serious threat" defense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

1217 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Nicholson v. Independent School Dist. #363


C0-91-1404


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 246



March 10, 1992, Decided  
March 17, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Nicholson v. Indep. Sch. Dist. No. 363, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 806 (Minn., May 15, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to Independent School District No. 363



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator teacher appealed a decision from respondent school board (Minnesota), which terminated his teaching contract pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 125.12, subd. 8 (1990). The teacher sought review by writ of certiorari and alleged numerous errors.


OVERVIEW: Prior to being terminated, the teacher had a continuing contract to teach at a high school. After a student came forward and reported that the teacher had repeatedly made sexual advances toward him, the school board initiated an investigation. Subsequently, the school board terminated the teacher's contract after finding immoral conduct unbecoming a teacher and willful neglect of duty. The court affirmed. Specifically, the court held that the fact that the teacher's sexual advances did not occur in the classroom did not place the conduct outside of his teaching role. Furthermore, the court found that the school board's refusal to permit the teacher to conduct discovery was not a denial of his due process rights or his statutory right to a hearing because there was no right to discovery under Minn. Stat. § 125.12, subd. 9 (1990). Finally, the court held that the teacher's knowing use of his position to engage in sexual misconduct with a minor was so obviously inappropriate that he should have known, without warning, that it was unacceptable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the school board's decision.

 

1218 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Way v. Foley Dental Office


C8-91-1506


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 222



March 4, 1992, Decided  
March 10, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, Review denied by Way v. Foley Dental Office, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 753 (Minn., May 15, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Anoka County; Hon. Michael J. Roith, Judge. District Court File C9911350



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Anoka County (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment for respondent dentist. The patient had alleged breach of warranty and torture. The trial court found that the action stated a claim for malpractice and that the patient failed to serve an affidavit of expert review as required under Minn. Stat. § 145.682 (1990). The patient denied that the claim was for malpractice.


OVERVIEW: The patient visited the dentist complaining of severe tooth pain. The dentist diagnosed him as having an abscess. The patient claimed that the dentist inflicted unnecessary pain during the course of the examination. Nevertheless, he made an appointment to return for treatment, at which time the dentist informed him that he would not perform a root canal but offered to remove the nerve in the offending tooth and apply an occlusal splint. The patient agreed to the treatment. The patient claimed that the dentist again inflicted unnecessary pain during the course of treatment, which continued to worsen. He returned to the dental office and demanded help but refused the medications offered him and eventually sought treatment from another dentist. On appeal, the court held that the true crux of the patient's claim was that the dentist's decision to remove the nerve and apply a splint was not a proper course of treatment for his tooth pain. Such a claim alleged malpractice, error, mistake, or failure to cure. Therefore, § 145.682 applied to his claim, despite the fact he did not denominate his action as one for malpractice.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1219 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Benson v. Hackbarth


C3-91-1607


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


481 N.W.2d 375; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 156



February 19, 1992, Decided  
February 25, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Benson v. Hackbarth, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 762 (Minn., Apr. 27, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Chisago County; Hon. James E. Dehn, Judge. District Court File F691536



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review from an order for child support of the Chisago County District Court (Minnesota), despite his prior stipulated admission of paternity and payment of an agreed upon lump-sum. The father contended that the district court erred in ordering him to pay child support.


OVERVIEW: Shortly after the mother and the county welfare board commenced an action against the father alleging that he was the father of the child, the father entered into a stipulation under which he admitted paternity and agreed to pay the mother an agreed upon lump sum in complete satisfaction of all past, present, or future liability for support of the child. More than 10 years later, an action was filed on behalf of the child seeking a child support order against the father. The district court entered a child support order against the father. The court reversed. Specifically, the court held that the child was barred from bringing a separate action for support where the father paid a lump sum settlement and the child's interests were adequately represented in the settlement negotiations under Minn. Stat. § 257.28 (1978) (repealed 1980). The court found that the child's basic right to establish parental relations would not be barred by finding that the child had privity with the mother in the original settlement with the father. Furthermore, the court noted that the county welfare board had been directed to insure that the interests of the child were safeguarded during the settlement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's judgment.

 

1220 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Chamberlain v. State


C1-91-1489


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 140



February 10, 1992, Decided  
February 18, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Chamberlain v. State, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 765 (Minn., Apr. 13, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. William S. Posten, Judge. Hennepin County District Court File 72114



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted by a jury in the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota) of one count of first degree criminal sexual conduct and four counts of fourth degree criminal sexual conduct and was sentenced. Petitioner's convictions were affirmed on all but one count and petitioner sought post-conviction relief, which was denied. Petitioner claimed that he should be resentenced in accordance with the Minnesota Sentencing Guidelines.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was sentenced before the sentencing guidelines took effect but his conviction was made final by the Supreme Court after they took effect. The State contended that petitioner could not raise the resentencing issue through the postconviction petition since he had not raised it on direct appeal. The court held that petitioner did not deliberately or inexcusably fail to raise the resentencing issue on direct appeal, so that substantive review was warranted. The court affirmed the denial of post conviction relief and held that the promulgation of sentencing guidelines prior to the final judgment was not the same as legislative reduction of a statutory maximum punishment. The court further held that the legislative reduction of a statutory maximum sentence effected a substantive right, but that enactment of sentencing guidelines did not. Further, the court held that the presumptive sentence under the guidelines could have been departed from on the same grounds relied on by the trial court in imposing the original sentence to reach a similar or longer sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of postconviction relief.

 

1221 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Ginsberg v. Minnesota Dep't of Jobs & Training


C8-91-1540


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


481 N.W.2d 138; 1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 146



February 10, 1992, Decided  
February 18, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Ginsberg v. Minn. Dep't of Jobs & Training, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 760 (Minn., Apr. 9, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari to Department of Jobs and Training



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a decision of the Commissioner of Jobs and Training (Minnesota), which found that as Assistant to the Commissioner and Economic Opportunity Director in the Department of Jobs and Training, the employee was ineligible for unemployment benefits because he had not been "employed" by the Department of Jobs and Training but had worked in a major nontenured policymaking or advisory position in unclassified service.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked as Assistant to the Commissioner in an unclassified position. He thereafter was appointed to the unclassified position of Economic Opportunity Director. After a new governor appointed a new Commissioner, the employee was fired. The employee and the former Commissioner testified that neither of the employee's positions required him to make or establish policy. His claim for unemployment benefits was denied on the basis that he had not earned wages in covered employment because his services were performed in major nontenured policymaking and/or advisory positions in the unclassified service. The court affirmed finding that under the rule of necessity, the Commissioner had to participate in the proceedings because she was the only official authorized by law to determine the employee's entitlement to unemployment benefits. The court held that there was evidence to support the Commissioner's conclusion that the employee was in a major policymaking or advisory position. The court held the legislature, in enacting Minn. Stat. § 268.04, subd. 12(10)(f)(v)(a) did not evidence an intent that the duties of the position were more important that the position itself.


OUTCOME: The decision of the Commissioner determining that the employee was ineligible for unemployment compensation benefits because his positions were policymaking or advisory positions was affirmed.

 

1222 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Evans v. Commissioner of Public Safety


C3-90-2116


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 71



January 28, 1992, Decided  
February 4, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. James D. Rogers, Judge. District Court No. IC469183



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver challenged the judgment of the District Court of Hennepin County (Minnesota), which affirmed revocation of his driver's license by respondent Commissioner of Public Safety pursuant to the implied consent law, Minn. Stat. § 169.123, subd. 2(b) (Supp. 1989).


OVERVIEW: Police advised underage people to leave a party. The driver parked around the corner, intending to return. The police, suspecting as much and that alcohol violations were involved, illuminated the car's interior and recognized the driver. He was read the implied consent advisory under § 169.123, subd. 2(b) (Supp. 1989) and given a breath test. His driver's license was revoked. The driver challenged his "seizure" and the implied consent advisory. The court found the objective evidence available to the police was sufficient to justify a seizure. Caselaw held that an advisory that informed a driver that refusing testing could subject him to criminal penalties unconstitutionally violated due process if the driver who took the test did not have the prior license revocations needed to make refusal a crime. The court found no merit in the Commissioner's claim that the driver did not raise an "identical due process" argument below and that he failed to show he would have refused testing but for the advisory. The trial court had found the advisory language constitutional, and the driver did not have to show actual prejudice. He was entitled to rescission of his license revocation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and found that the driver was entitled to rescission of his driver's license revocation.

State v. Marshall


C2-91-1517


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1992 Minn. App. LEXIS 64



January 15, 1992, Decided  
January 28, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Marshall, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 764 (Minn., Mar. 26, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, St. Louis County; Hon. Charles T. Barnes, Judge. District Court File 9080687



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the District Court, St. Louis County (Minnesota), which sentenced him to 88 months' imprisonment following the entry of his guilty plea to second-degree possession of cocaine in violation of Minn. Stat. § 152.022, subd. 2(2) (1990).


OVERVIEW: Defendant obtained an order for the withdrawal of his original guilty plea after a co-defendant pleaded guilty to a reduced charge of controlled substance in the third degree and admitted during her plea that the drugs, which were found in a hotel room, belonged to her. The trial court, however, denied defendant's request for a dismissal of the charges. On the day set for trial, defendant again pleaded guilty as charged, but the State no longer agreed that only one of his prior convictions would be included in calculating his criminal history score. The court affirmed the judgment, finding that the trial court properly considered two prior drug convictions for purposes of calculating defendant's criminal history score because the drug convictions did not constitute a single behavioral incident. Further, the court found it neither unfair nor unconstitutional that defendant received a longer sentence than his co-defendant. The court found that the sentence was fair in comparison to others convicted of the same crime who possessed the same criminal history score. The court rejected defendant's allegation of prosecutorial vindictiveness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Wilde v. Dorow


C5-91-605


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 1249



December 27, 1991, Decided  
January 7, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Wilde v. Dorow, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 723 (Minn., Mar. 19, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Brown County; Hon. Warren E. Litynski, Judge. District Court File C090484



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a putative heir, challenged the judgment from the Brown County District Court (Minnesota) that dismissed her claim to the statutory share of respondent estate by way of summary judgment. The putative heir claimed that the trial court erroneously denied her claim of paternity as barred by the limitation in Minn. Stat. § 257.58, subd. 1 (1990).


OVERVIEW: The decedent died intestate. The putative heir brought a claim against the estate for her statutory share of the estate claiming that she was the decedent's illegitimate daughter. The trial court dismissed the claim, holding that in the absence of a presumption of paternity, the putative heir's clam was barred because she had not brought a paternity action within one year of reaching the age of majority pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 257.58, subd. 1 (1990). On review, the putative heir argued that she was denied a remedy, that the time limit should be waived due to equity, and that limitation applied only to support and custody cases. The court rejected the arguments and affirmed the decision. The court reasoned that the time limitation under the statute was reasonable, that Minn. Stat. §524.2-109 (1990) specifically provided that the paternity statute applied to intestate succession, and that there was no evidence that the putative heir was disabled or otherwise prevented from timely filing her paternity action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

In re D.L.


C7-91-1173


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


479 N.W.2d 408; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 1236



December 23, 1991, Decided  
December 31, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, Motion to strike denied by, Request granted In re Welfare of D.L., 1992 Minn. LEXIS 758 (Minn., Feb. 27, 1992)
Affirmed by In re D.L., 486 N.W.2d 375, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 156 (Minn., 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Isabel Gomez, Judge. District Court File AD170884



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant foster parents sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which ruled in favor of respondent grandparents. The foster parents brought a claim to challenge the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 259.28, subd. 2.


OVERVIEW: The foster parents appealed from the trial court's ruling granting the grandparents' petition to adopt the minor child. They claimed that Minn. Stat. § 259.28, subd. 2, impermissibly classified adoptive children based upon their race, thereby violating the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Section 259.28, subd. 2, required the trial court, in the absence of good cause to the contrary, to follow certain placement preferences in the adoption of a child of minority racial or minority ethnic heritage. The grandparents were African-American and the foster parents were not. The court held that by imposing different criteria for adoptive placement of children of minority racial or ethnic backgrounds, as opposed to non-minority children, § 259.28, subd. 2, violated the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court however, held that the record supported the trial court's findings of significant benefits to the child from placement with her grandparents.


OUTCOME: The court ruled against the foster parents and affirmed the judgment of the trial court placing the child with the grandparents.

State v. Regitschnig


CX-91-1023


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 1229



December 20, 1991, Decided  
December 31, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Steele County; Hon. Casey J. Christian, Judge. District Court File # T1-91-50



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the District Court, Steele County (Minnesota), which convicted defendant of a misdemeanor violation of a city zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant purchased a mobile home park with knowledge of a zoning ordinance that permitted the continuance of the park as a nonconforming use but prohibited expansion beyond the 14 units then existing. Defendant then placed 15 units on the property. Defendant was convicted of a misdemeanor violation of the city zoning ordinance. On appeal, the court held that defendant could not challenge the constitutionality of the zoning ordinance because defendant, as an aggrieved party, did not first exhaust all available remedies. The court noted that, for defendant to have exhausted his available remedies, he must have applied for and been denied a variance from the regulations restricting development of his property. The court held that the addition of the 15th unit was a prohibited expansion of an otherwise legal nonconforming use of the property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Rooney v. Rooney


C7-91-945


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


478 N.W.2d 545; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 1225



December 17, 1991, Decided  
December 24, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Rooney v. Rooney, 669 N.W.2d 362, 2003 Minn. App. LEXIS 1161 (2003)
Related proceeding at Christ's Household of Faith v. Ramsey County, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 42117 (D. Minn., May 17, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. Lawrence D. Cohen, Judge. District Court #DM-F1-87-23807



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), rendered against it as an ex-spouse's employer for payment of maintenance and child support obligations under Minn. Stat. §§ 518.611, 518.613. Respondent former wife sought an award of attorney fees and costs incurred in defending the appeal pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 518.14.


OVERVIEW: The employer alleged that it was not a proper party to the action and that it should not be subject to the judgment. The employer disputed that it was an employer and that the ex-spouse was an employee. The employer also contended that Minn. Stat. §§ 518.611, 518.613 (1990) were unconstitutional as applied because they denied it an opportunity to appear and present evidence and, thus, denied due process. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the cause, finding that the trial court could not ignore the employer's request for an evidentiary hearing because ordinary rules of due process mandated a hearing. Thus, the court concluded that the employer had a right to an evidentiary hearing unless it waived its right by its conduct. The court remanded for the trial court to clearly enunciate whether the employer waived an evidentiary hearing by its conduct, to determine whether the employer was in fact the ex-spouse's employer, and if in fact it was an employer, to determine the amount of the ex-spouse's maintenance and child support obligation. The court denied the ex-wife's motion for attorney fees and appellate costs pursuant to its discretion under Minn. Stat. § 518.14.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the cause.

Golden Valley Lutheran College v. Golden Valley


C0-91-1189


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 1174



December 10, 1991, Decided  
December 17, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Golden Valley Lutheran College v. City of Golden Valley, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 821 (Minn., Feb. 10, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Ann D. Montgomery, Judge. District Court File 899790



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant college sought review of the decision of the District Court, Hennepin County(Minnesota), which dismissed its taking of property claim against respondent city, required the college to provide a more definite statement for the tortious interference claim, and denied the college's motion to disqualify counsel for the city. Further, the trial court denied the college's motion to disqualify the trial judge and motion for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: The college filed an action against the city and the state higher education authority for unconstitutional taking of property and tortious interference with prospective business advantage. The trial court dismissed the taking claim, required the college to provide a more definite statement for the tortious interference claim, and denied the college's motion to disqualify counsel for the city. The trial court also dismissed the college's motions to disqualify the trial judge and for reconsideration. The court reversed the dismissal of the tortious interference claim and the taking claim. The trial court stated that the college failed to allege the existence of a contract. The court held that the trial court confused interference with prospective relationship, which did not require the existence of a contract, with an interference with contract claim. However, the trial court properly denied the motion to disqualify because it was brought more than a year after the trial court had issued its order. The trial judge's relationship to the alleged potential witness could not have affected her previous orders because she was not made aware of the purported conflict until long afterward.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the motion to disqualify and motion for reconsideration, reversed the dismissal of the taking and interference claims, and remanded for further proceedings.

In re Monson

478 N.W.2d 785; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 1185

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which committed him as a psychopathic personality to the Minnesota Security Hospital for an indeterminate period.


OVERVIEW: Shortly after appellant pleaded guilty to two counts of second-degree criminal sexual conduct for incidents involving young boys, the district court committed him as a psychopathic personality to a security hospital. Appellant sought review of the commitment on the basis that the evidence was insufficient to support the determination that he is a psychopathic personality. The court affirmed. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision committing appellant as a psychopathic personality for an indeterminate period.

 

1230 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Hahn v. Tri-Line Farmers Co-op


C4-90-2738, C3-91-5


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


478 N.W.2d 515; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 1123



November 25, 1991, Decided  
December 3, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.
Review denied by Hahn v. Hutchinson Wil-Rich, Inc., 1992 Minn. LEXIS 644 (Minn., Jan. 27, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Lac Qui Parle County; Hon. Bruce W. Christopherson, Judge. District Court #C9-88-23



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent worker filed an action against appellant auger manufacturer after he was injured while towing an auger. The auger manufacturer brought a third-party action against the worker's employer, appellant agricultural cooperative. The District Court, Lac Qui Parle County (Minnesota) entered judgment for the worker, and the manufacturer and cooperative appealed. The manufacturer also challenged the denial of its motion to reallocate damages.


OVERVIEW: In a worker's action following his injury while towing an auger, the jury returned a verdict finding his employer, an agricultural co-operative, 95 percent at fault, the manufacturer of the auger three percent at fault, and the worker two percent at fault, awarding the worker $ 2,197,918. The trial court held that the maximum contribution the manufacturer could obtain from the cooperative was the total workers' compensation benefits the cooperative was required to pay the worker, $ 543,445, on account of Minn. Stat. § 176.061 (1986). There was no common law liability involving the employer and the third party, and the manufacturer was therefore responsible for $ 1,610,515 of the damages award. The court affirmed, finding no constitutional violation. The court ruled that Minn. Stat. § 604.02, subd. 2 (1986), which governed the reapportionment of uncollectible judgments, was not applicable to an employer's contribution in a workers' compensation third-party liability action because to find the statute applicable in such circumstances would defy legislative intent. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the jury to view an edited videotape of the paraplegic worker.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the worker and determined that the trial court's refusal to grant the manufacturer's motion to reallocate damages uncollectible from the employer was properly denied.

 

1231 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. New Mexico v. Chappell


C2-91-1159


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 1135



November 25, 1991, Decided  
December 3, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State ex rel. N.M. v. Chappell, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 775 (Minn., Jan. 17, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Pine County; Hon. James R. Clifford, Judge. File K591474



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Pine County (Minnesota), which denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus and extradited him to New Mexico to serve a sentence there.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was serving time on a federal charge in Minnesota when he was indicted in New Mexico for securities violations. He was transferred to New Mexico to stand trial and, upon his conviction, he was returned to Minnesota to complete his sentence there. At the end of his federal sentence, the Minnesota governor issued a warrant for the inmate's delivery to New Mexico. When he did not waive extradition, the inmate was taken into custody by a county sheriff. The inmate filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The trial court denied the petition and extradited the inmate. The court affirmed, holding that it deferred to New Mexico for consideration of the constitutional defects raised by the inmate in the underlying extradition action. The court further held that the trial court properly denied the petition for habeas corpus because it found that the extradition documents were in order, the inmate was actually charged with and convicted of a crime in New Mexico, he had been identified by a New Mexico prosecutor as defendant in the New Mexico proceedings, and he was outside New Mexico and had not yet served time for the offenses committed there and, thus, he was a fugitive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

Wschola v. Snyder


C0-91-690


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


478 N.W.2d 225; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 1140; 60 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1492; 58 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P41,417



November 25, 1991, Decided

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Wschola v. Snyder, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 707 (Minn., Feb. 10, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Dakota County; Hon. Gerald W. Kalina, Judge. District Court #C9906826



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a decision of the District Court, Dakota County (Minnesota), which held that the employee's action against appellee employer based upon the Minnesota Human Rights Act was filed after the allowable period under the statute of limitations in effect when the employee's cause of action accrued in violation of Minn. Stat. § 363.06, subd. 3 (1986) and granted the employer's motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The employer terminated the employee from her employment as a bartender. 308 days after she was fired, the employee filed a complaint alleging she was terminated because of her pregnancy, in violation of the Minnesota Human Rights Act (MHRA). After the date of the employee's termination, the state legislature increased the limitations period for the MHRA from 300 days to one year, but did not specify whether it would be applied to causes of action not yet time barred under the old statute of limitations. Applying the 300-day limitations period, the trial court granted a motion to dismiss the employee's action. On appeal, the court held that the newer, one-year statute of limitations applied to the employee's complaint. The court noted that the legislature subsequently passed a bill that further expanded the statute of limitations of the MHRA to two years and specifically allowed the limitations statute to be applied retroactively.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision to grant the motion to dismiss.

 

1233 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Grussing v. Kvam Implement Co.


C0-91-947


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


478 N.W.2d 200; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 1121



November 21, 1991, Decided  
December 3, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Swift County; Hon. Keith C. Davison, Judge. District Court File #C8-90-134



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state agency sought review of an order of the District Court Swift County (Minnesota) denying its motion to quash defendant manufacturer's subpoena for the testimony of an occupational safety and health (OSHA) investigator who had cited third-party defendant employer for certain violations in connection with a wrongful death products liability action brought by plaintiff trustee after a work-related accident at the employer's facility.


OVERVIEW: The trustee's decedent was working at the employer's facility when he was killed. The trustee sued the manufacturer of the product that was involved in the accident and the manufacturer brought a third-party claim against the employer. Meanwhile, an OSHA investigation was performed, resulting in fines being assessed against the employer. Consequently, the manufacturer subpoenaed the OSHA records and the testimony of the investigator. The agency produced the records, but moved to quash with respect to the testimony, invoking the statutory privilege in Minn. Stat. § 182.659, subd. 8 (1990). The district court upheld the subpoena, ruling that the statute violated due process and the separation of powers doctrine. The agency appealed. In reversing, the appellate court ruled that that statute was consistent with both substantive and procedural due process. The statutory privilege had a rational basis and legitimate goal in furthering timely and impartial investigations. Moreover, the manufacturer had access to the desired information through the reports that were produced. The privilege did not infringe upon the separation of powers.


OUTCOME: The order refusing the quash the witness subpoena for the investigator's testimony was reversed.

State v. Hart


C8-91-517


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


477 N.W.2d 732; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 1094



November 20, 1991, Decided  
November 26, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Hart, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 657 (Minn., Jan. 16, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Beltrami County; Hon. James E. Preece, Judge. Dist. Ct. File No. K790933



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court, Beltrami County (Minnesota), which convicted him of first degree criminal sexual conduct and first degree burglary, in violation of Minn. Stat. §§ 609.342, subds. 1(c), (e)(i), subds. 1(a), (c) (1990), and sentenced him to concurrent terms of 244 months for the criminal sexual conduct conviction and 34 months for the burglary conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction was based on his unlawful entry into the victim's home, where he raped her while her children slept in the house. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the trial court did not err by deleting "intentionally" from the standard jury instructions for first degree criminal sexual conduct because the offense was a general intent crime; (2) the trial court acted within its discretion when it refused to give an instruction on third degree criminal sexual conduct as a lesser included offense; (3) the trial court did err by not specifying separate essential elements and a separate verdict form for each of the two counts of first degree criminal sexual conduct; and (4) the trial court acted within its discretion in giving a double upward durational departure sentence for the criminal sexual conduct conviction because the crime was particularly cruel and was committed in the presence of children.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

1235 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Investment Co. Inst. v. Hatch


C4-91-904


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


477 N.W.2d 747; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 1100



November 19, 1991, Decided  
November 26, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. George O. Peterson, Judge. District Court File #C887494109.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant investment company appealed a judgment from the District Court, Ramsey County (Wisconsin) that granted respondent commerce commissioner summary judgment on the company's claim that the statutory registration fee scheme embodied in Minn. Stat. § 80A.28, subd. 1(b) (1990) violated both the Due Process and the Equal Protection Clauses of the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Section 80A.28, subd. 1(b) (1990) authorized the collection of fees from the registration of redeemable securities. The statute specifically stated that there "shall be no maximum fee for securities registered pursuant to this clause." However, fees collected for all other types of securities were capped at $ 300 pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 80A.28, subd. 1(a) (1990). The trial court concluded that the language and legislative history of § 80A.28, subd. 1(b) permitted collection of fees to raise revenues in excess of the cost of regulation. The court affirmed relying heavily upon its standard of review concerning the constitutionality of a statute. Thus, the court interpreted the absence of a fee cap in subdivision 1(b) to clearly permit generation of excess revenues, particularly when in other subdivisions of the same statute the legislature placed fee caps on other different types of securities. The origination of the Securities Act in the senate did not preclude raising revenue under subdivision 1(b) because at the time of its enactment it was primarily a regulatory act that incidentally produced excess revenues.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment granted to the commissioner on the company's claim that statutory language authorizing collection of registration fees to raise revenue violated both the Due Process and the Equal Protection Clauses.

Lloyd F. Smith Co. v. Den-Tal-Ez


C6-91-841


COURT OF APPEALS OF MINNESOTA


478 N.W.2d 510; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 1109; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P13,071; 16 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. 2d (Callaghan) 18



November 19, 1991, Decided  
November 26, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. Joanne M. Smith, Judge. District Court File C1893089



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, tenants and owner of a building, sought review of a decision of the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), that appellants failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted in their action against respondents, dental chair manufacturer and motor manufacturer, for strict liability and negligence. The trial court also granted respondents' motions for summary judgment on appellants' breach of warranty claims.


OVERVIEW: Appellants contended that a defective dental chair located in the office of one of the tenants, a dentist, caused a fire in the building. The dentist purchased the chair from another dentist. The trial court determined that the Uniform Commercial Code (UCC) provided the exclusive remedy for the property damage caused by the fire and that the breach of warranty claims were time barred under Minn. Stat. § 336.2-725. Appellants contended that it could not be determined whether the original purchase of the chair was a commercial transaction and there was no commercial transaction in the case because the dentist purchased the chair used. The court found that the UCC provided the exclusive remedy for the property damage. Appellants failed to present any genuine issue of material fact regarding the identity of the original purchaser of the chair. The secondary purchase was a commercial transaction because it was between businesspersons for use in income generating activities. The breach of warranty claim was time barred under § 336.2-725. The cause of action arose when the manufacturer delivered the chair and the action was not brought before the four year statute of limitation expired.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to respondents.

In re Application of Jobe


No. C1-91-424


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


477 N.W.2d 723; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 1072



November 13, 1991  
November 19, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; No. 88903565; Hon. Michael J. Davis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Remanded. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted on two counts of first degree murder in the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota). Before the court was an appeal from a trial court's order for payment of expert fees and services. The issue before the court was whether the trial court erred in awarding only part of the expert witness fees that were claimed under Minn. Stat. § 611.21 (Supp. 1989).


OVERVIEW: The state offered evidence to prove defendant committed the murders by using a DNA analysis of blood found at the murder scene. The trial court granted permission for defense to hire an expert witness. The order limited expert witness fees to $ 5000. The pretrial hearing took 12 days. The state called seven experts; five employed by the FBI and two private consultants. The defense called three experts who were all private consultants. The trial judge found that the DNA evidence admissible. Only one defense expert testified at trial. After the trial, defendant's attorney submitted the bill for expert witness fees to the trial judge. The trial judge ordered payment of expert witness fees and disallowed 38 hours billed by the expert. The judge explained that 10 hours of consultation were necessary but the additional 38 only benefitted defendant's attorney and were not necessary for an adequate defense. The court remanded for further proceedings on why the expert fees incurred were unreasonable and for recalculation, if any, of a reasonable amount was ordered. The court noted that § 611.21 mandated the trial court to pay reasonable fees that were necessary for an adequate defense.


OUTCOME: The court's order on the payment of expert witness fees was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Glover


Nos. C2-91-1064, C2-91-1243


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 1059



November 12, 1991  
November 19, 1991, Filed
