DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two separate reviews, appellant, the State of Minnesota, challenged two rulings from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota) that suppressed cocaine obtained during the warrantless search of two defendants and their car.


OVERVIEW: In response to a shots fired radio dispatch, police stopped a car with both defendants inside. After conducting a pat down search, the car was searched and a pouch containing cocaine was found. At the suppression hearing, the officers testified that the dispatch told them the suspects were black males driving a light-colored car. The actual dispatch made no mention of race and described the car as silver. In separate rulings for each defendant, the first trial court judge suppressed the evidence, ruling that the officers lacked the particular and objective basis to stop the car. The second trial court judge ruled the stop was legal but that the search of the pouch was illegal because it could not have been a weapon. The court affirmed both rulings, holding that that the determination of credibility was solely a matter for the trial court. The court declined to address the apparent contrast in each trial court's analysis, and the State's contention that the passenger did not have any expectation of privacy because that issue was not raised at trial.


OUTCOME: The rulings of the trial courts were affirmed.

Housing & Redevelopment Auth. v. Agassiz Constr.


No. C6-91-600


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


476 N.W.2d 781; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 1031; 16 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. 2d (Callaghan) 132



October 29, 1991  
November 5, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Polk County; No. C861456; Hon. Russell A. Anderson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On appeal from summary judgment from District Court, Polk County (Minnesota), appellants alleged the trial court erred when it applied the Uniform Commercial Code statute of limitations to this case, and barred third party indemnification actions.


OVERVIEW: Respondent contracted with appellant engineers to remodel building, with appellant general contractor. Third party defendant delivered lumber to general contractor, but during inspection, respondent learned that lumber was meant for interior use, not exterior use. Respondent sued general contractor, and amended its complaint to include appellant engineers. Lower court granted respondent's second motion for summary judgment, and dismissed appellants' complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed, and found that appellants' cause of action for breach of warranty accrued when third party defendant tendered delivery of lumber, and appellants brought their third party claim well beyond statutory four year limit. The Uniform Commercial Code statute of limitations governed. Respondent could not recover from third party defendant because it commenced this action five years after tender of delivery.


OUTCOME: Where action accrued outside the statute of limitations provided by the Uniform Commercial Code, respondent could not recover from third party defendant, and the judgment was affirmed.

State by Humphrey v. Casino Mktg. Group


No. C1-91-598


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


475 N.W.2d 505; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 976



September 25, 1991  
October 8, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Casino Mktg. Group, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 833 (Minn., Dec. 4, 1991)
Affirmed by State v. Casino Mktg. Group, 491 N.W.2d 882, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 295 (Minn., 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Nos. C6-90-12442, C6-90-12443; Hon. George O. Petersen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant marketing agent sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Ramsey County (Minnesota), which granted the State's motion for a temporary injunction prohibiting him from using automatic-dialing announcing devices to solicit customers at home pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 325E.26(4) (1990).


OVERVIEW: The State commenced two actions against appellant seeking to enjoin him from using automatic-dialing announcing devices to solicit people by telephone on the basis that use of the devices violated Minn. Stat. § 325E.26(4) (1990). The trial court granted the State's motion for a temporary injunction. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court found that the restrictions placed on commercial speech under § 325E.26(4) were lawful where the asserted governmental interests in restricting the use of such devices was substantial, the requirement of a live operator advanced the state's interests in privacy and preventing fraud, and the restrictions were not more extensive than necessary. The court determined the trial court did not error by applying a presumption the statute was valid even though first amendment rights were involved where commercial speech was not granted the high standard of protection other first amendment rights received. U.S. Const. amend. I. The court concluded the statute was not an illegal prior restraint on speech where the statute merely regulated the manner by which certain telephone solicitations could be presented to consumers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that granted the State's motion for a temporary injunction prohibiting appellant from using automatic-dialing announcing devices to solicit customers at home.

In re Welfare of Z.P.B.


No. C0-90-2736


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


474 N.W.2d 651; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 925



September 4, 1991  
September 10, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; File No. 16674997; Hon. Allen Oleisky, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a minor, sought review of the order from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which ordered the minor to submit a blood sample for DNA analysis pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 609.3461 (1990).


OVERVIEW: After a minor admitted committing sexual conduct, the juvenile court ordered to submit a biological specimen for DNA analysis under Minn. Stat. § 609.3461 (1990). When the order was issued, the Bureau of Criminal Apprehension (BCA) had not yet adopted uniform procedures and protocols for collecting and maintaining such evidence. The court affirmed the juvenile court's order. The court held that the order did not violate the minor's constitutional right to due process of law even though the procedures and protocols had not yet been adopted. The minor did not have a justiciable controversy in that there had been no attempt to use the minor's DNA sample. The only intrusion was the drawing of the blood sample. Neither did the order impermissibly conflict with the juvenile court confidentiality statutes. The legislature had the power to choose when such information would not be confidential, and it so chose in its enactment of § 609.3461.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the juvenile court's order that the minor provide a blood sample for DNA analysis.

St. Paul v. Various Items of Drug Paraphernalia


No. C9-90-2735


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


474 N.W.2d 413; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 879



August 20, 1991, Decided  
August 27, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; District Court File No. C587482494; Hon. Edward S. Wilson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner challenged an order of the District Court of Ramsey County (Minnesota), which found that items sold in the owner's shop were subject to forfeiture as drug paraphernalia. He challenged the trial court's findings that the drug paraphernalia statutes were constitutional as applied and that the various items were drug paraphernalia. The owner also alleged that the trial court erred in allowing a police officer to testify as an expert.


OVERVIEW: Undercover police bought items having the physical characteristics of drug paraphernalia from the owner's store. A search warrant was obtained and the items seized. A civil forfeiture action was filed. The trial court found that most of the items were drug paraphernalia subject to forfeiture. The trial court, holding that Minn. Stat. § 152.01, subd. 18 was constitutional as applied and that there was sufficient evidence to support determinations that the items were drug paraphernalia, denied a request for a new trial. The court reversed and remanded, holding that items found to have the physical characteristics necessary to meet the statutory definition of drug paraphernalia must also have been intended for use as such, that is, with controlled substances; thus, a finding of the intent for use was necessary. The court found Minn. Stat. § 152.02, subd. 18 (1982), and Minn. Stat. § 152.093 (1982), as applied, did not infringe on the owner's constitutional rights to free association nor equal protection. The court held that items marketed specifically for cutting other substances were drug paraphernalia even though they could also be purchased at drug stores and health food stores.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court finding that the items were drug paraphernalia subject to forfeiture was reversed and the matter was remanded with instructions to the trial court to determine the intent of the owner as to ultimate use, and to make specific findings and conclusions regarding that intent.

Krmpotich v. Duluth


Nos. C5-90-2036, C7-90-2037, C8-90-2354


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


474 N.W.2d 392; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 850



August 14, 1991, Decided  
August 20, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, St. Louis County; District Court File No. 9020115; Hon. David S. Bouschor, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, two citizen groups, appealed decisions of the District Court for St. Louis County (Minnesota), which found in favor of respondents, a city and a developer, on the suits by the groups to prevent the building of a shopping mall. The trial court found that the mall would not impact any natural resources or wetlands under the Minnesota Environmental Rights Act (MERA).


OVERVIEW: The developer bought a 35-acre site for a 267,000 square foot strip retail mall and parking lot in the Miller Hill Corridor Area of Duluth, Minnesota. The site was characterized by wetlands, a creek, steep slopes, and flood hazard areas. The developer proposed to blast out the slopes, using the material to fill in the wetlands. A corporation was already discharging waste into the wetlands. The court reversed the judgment that the development would not violate MERA. The court so held because the wetlands would be eliminated. This was an impact on a natural resource under Minn. Stat. § 116B.02(4) (1988), even though the wetlands were not currently in their pristine state. The developer's proposed holding ponds would not have mitigated this adverse impact. The court affirmed the judgment holding that the city had followed its own ordinances in approving certain variances for the developer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment below in favor of the city regarding its actions granting variances, rezoning, and vacating an easement. The court modified the judgment by severing an invalid reversionary clause from the city's ordinance, which was otherwise valid. The court reversed the judgment in favor of the developer and found that the proposed construction would violate the Minnesota Environmental Rights Act.

DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a grant of summary judgment from the District Court, Rock County (Minnesota) in favor of respondent city in the employee's action for wrongful termination in violation of the collective bargaining agreement's residency requirement. The city asserted that the appeal should be dismissed for lack of a justiciable controversy.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked in the electrical line distribution department and was subject to a residency requirement set forth in the collective bargaining agreement and required by Minn. Stat. § 415.16 (1984). The employee filed a grievance under the collective bargaining agreement regarding the residency requirement. The court held that the employee's appeal lacked a justiciable controversy. The court explained that the employee had failed to exhaust his administrative remedies under the collective bargaining agreement. The court stated that a mere allegation by the employee that the residency requirement was unconstitutionally applied to him did not relieve the employee of the obligation to exhaust his administrative remedies.

State v. Reha


No. CX-90-2372


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


474 N.W.2d 360; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 795



August 6, 1991, Decided  
August 13, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Reha, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 626 (Minn., Oct. 7, 1991)
Reversed by State v. Reha, 483 N.W.2d 688, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 122 (Minn., 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; District Court No. 90021721; Hon. William B. Christensen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the District Court of Hennepin County (Minnesota), which found her guilty of violating Minneapolis, Minn. Code of Ordinances § 244.690 which required dwellings to be kept in a clean and sanitary condition. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the ordinance alleging it was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The Minneapolis Health Department inspected defendant's home. One inspector testified to clutter and garbage that constituted unclean and unsanitary conditions. The inspector's supervisor testified defendant's home contained garbage, rubbish, empty food containers, clothing, and food lying about the house. Defendant testified the clutter was due to extensive renovations and the fact that she collected clothes for charity that she washed and dried prior to delivering them. She also testified as to special usage of some items such as plastic bottles that were to be used as individual greenhouses for her tomato plants. The testimony was corroborated by her daughter. Defendant was convicted of violating Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 244.690 (1985). The court reversed and remanded finding that the term "clean and sanitary" as used in the statute was so vague and discretionary in its application to defendant's conduct that it violated the minimum standards of due process. The court noted the phrase "clean and "sanitary" was not defined in the housing chapter, was not a term of art with established meanings, and it had no settled usage or tradition of interpretation in law.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for violating a local ordinance requiring occupants to keep their dwellings in clean and sanitary conditions was reversed.

 

1246 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Murphy v. Bloomington


No. CX-91-387


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 733



July 15, 1991, Decided  
July 23, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Murphy v. City of Bloomington, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 781 (Minn., Sept. 13, 1991)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; No. 8819320; Hon. Dolores Orey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner sought review of a summary judgment from the District Court, Hennepin County, Minnesota, that refused to reach the issue of the constitutionality of two zoning ordinances. The ordinances limited the number of unrelated persons who could live in a single family dwelling. Respondent city had brought criminal charges against the owner because he constructed and operated a duplex without obtaining the necessary permits and licenses.


OVERVIEW: The owner argued that the definition of "family" and the limitation of roomers in single-family dwellings under Bloomington, Minn., City Code §§ 19.03, 19.27(c)(4), respectively, were unconstitutional on their face and as applied to him. The court found that the record supported the trial court's findings. The owner converted the lower level of his house into a separate dwelling unit and rented it to a tenant who, in turn, sublet a room to another person. The owner never alleged that he intended to live with these tenants as a "family" in a single-family unit. The city never applied the definition of "family" against the owner or charged him with having too many roomers in violation of the code sections. The city brought criminal charges because the owner constructed and operated a duplex without obtaining required permits and licenses. The owner's damages, the loss of his property through foreclosure, arose only because of his operation of a duplex in a single-family residential area without a conditional use permit. Because the owner suffered no direct harm through application of the code sections, the trial court did not err in refusing to reach the constitutional issues raised.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment against the owner was affirmed.

 

1247 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Welfare of M.R.M.


No. CX-90-2582


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 641



June 19, 1991, Decided  
June 25, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Lindsay G. Arthur, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A delinquency petition filed in the District Court of Hennepin County, Juvenile Division (Minnesota) charged appellant juvenile with theft. Following a bench trial, the trial court found that the prosecution proved the petition. The issues on appeal centered on pretrial identifications, an in-court identification, and the failure to bifurcate the pretrial hearing from the trial.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile claims that evidence of a pretrial identification was inadmissible. The victim showed a high level of certainty at a showup. Only a week elapsed between the last offense and the identification. The victim's description was sufficient in context for a police officer and an assistant principal to think of the juvenile on the basis of the description. The court concluded that there was an adequate basis for the victim's school office identification independent of the suggestive procedure, and there was no substantial likelihood that the victim misidentified the juvenile as the offender at the showup. The factors considered in determining the admissibility of the out-of-court identification had essentially the same weight for determining the admissibility of the in-court identification. Based on the victim's opportunity to see the offender, the degree of the victim' attention, the accuracy of description, and the certainty demonstrated, there was no substantial likelihood of irreparable misidentification from either pretrial identification. Finally, the trial judge denied the motion to suppress so there was no harm in having that same judge hear the case on the merits.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Kwasek


No. C8-90-2239


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 649



June 14, 1991, Decided  
June 25, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by State v. Kwasek, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 575 (Minn., Aug. 1, 1991)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Winona County; Hon. Margaret Shaw Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was an officer of a corporation that held a license to sell intoxicating liquor at a bar, sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Winona County (Minnesota), which convicted him of violating a city ordinance by permitting a nonemployee to remain in a bar after 1:30 a.m.


OVERVIEW: Shortly before 3:00 a.m., defendant and a friend went into the bar for about 15 minutes. City police officers conducting surveillance in the area noticed their activity, entered the bar, and determined that defendant's friend was not an employee. Defendant was convicted of permitting a nonemployee to remain in a bar after 1:30 a.m. He sought review. On appeal, the court upheld the conviction. The court rejected defendant's argument that the ordinance, Winona City Code § 55.07(k) (1989), did not prohibit a licensee from allowing non-employees to be on the premises after 1:30 a.m. provided they arrived after 1:30 a.m. The court held that ordinance terms should be construed in accordance with their common and approved usage. The court ruled that the common meaning of "remain" was to stay or linger on the premises for any length of time after 1:30 a.m., regardless of the time of arrival. The court found that the ordinance was sufficiently clear to give licensees notice that they could not permit non-employees to stay or linger on the licensed premises after 1:30 a.m. no matter what time they arrived.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1249 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sybrant


No. C9-90-1908


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 626



June 12, 1991, Decided  
June 18, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Sybrant, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 505 (Minn., Aug. 1, 1991)
Review denied by State v. Sybrant, 472 N.W.2d 639, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 258 (Minn., 1991)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Michael J. Davis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota). A jury convicted defendant of both first- and second-degree criminal sexual conduct, and defendant received a mandatory 37-year sentence and a $ 40,000 fine as a repeat sex offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was released from imprisonment as a child molester, was placed on parole with the condition that he have no contact with children. The grandchild of a woman he subsequently married reported that defendant sexually abused her. The child testified at defendant's sex abuse trial, and out-of-court statements of the child's mother and others were admitted. The trial court also admitted testimony of four witnesses whom defendant had previously sexually abused. The court modified the judgment and affirmed. The trial court did not err in admitting hearsay statements; the statements were reliable because they were descriptive, detailed, and consistent. Moreover, the child's mother had no motive to lie. Corroboration of the statements was provided by testimony of the four previous child victims, which established a pattern of sex abuse of children and which was admissible under an exception to the rules of evidence. Although the State's allusions to defendant in closing argument as a liar, pervert, and sexual deviant were improper, they did not warrant a reversal. The statute under which defendant received a mandatory sentence as a repeat sex offender was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment by vacating the lesser-included second-degree offense of criminal sexual conduct. As modified, the court affirmed.

Black v. Snyder


No. C5-91-71


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


471 N.W.2d 715; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 635; 56 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 539; 58 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P41,365



June 11, 1991, Decided  
June 18, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Black v. Snyder, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 706 (Minn., Aug. 29, 1991)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Andrew W. Danielson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant associate pastor challenged the decision of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which dismissed, on First Amendment grounds, her breach of contract, sexual harassment, reprisal, retaliation, and defamation claims against her former employer, appellee church.


OVERVIEW: The associate pastor filed a discrimination charge alleging sexual harassment against defendant supervising pastor with the Department of Human Rights. Subsequently, the church voted to discharge her for her inability to conduct the pastoral office efficiently. She filed an action against the church, supervisor, and defendant national church for sexual harassment and retaliation under the Minnesota Human Rights Act, Minn. Stat. ch. 363; breach of contract; defamation; and wrongful termination. The church and supervisor moved to dismiss for lack of subject-matter jurisdiction and for failure to state a cognizable defamation claim. The trial court granted the church dismissal. The associate appealed. The court reversed in part and affirmed in part. The First Amendment did not bar the associate from litigating her sexual harassment claim. Her harassment claim did not involve scrutiny of church doctrine, interfere in matters of an inherently ecclesiastical nature, or infringe upon the church's religious practice. However, federal constitutional prohibitions on excessive entanglement with internal church affairs prohibited judicial review of her discharge-related claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part as to dismissal on First Amendment grounds of the breach of contract, reprisal, retaliation, and defamation claims against the church, and reversed in part as to sexual harassment.

 

1251 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Patton v. Yarrington


Nos. C5-90-2506, C7-90-2507


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


472 N.W.2d 157; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 634; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P12,995



June 7, 1991, Decided  
June 18, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Patton v. Yarrington, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 574 (Minn., Aug. 29, 1991)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. James H. Johnston, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a personal injury claimant and a wrongful death claimant, challenged the decision of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment to defendant manufacturer, dismissing their claims as untimely under the statutes of limitations for each of their respective actions.


OVERVIEW: A fire occurred in a duplex. Two smoke detectors installed in the duplex and made by the manufacturer allegedly failed to work during the fire. The personal injury claimant was injured in the fire. Seven members of the wrongful death claimant's family also died in the fire. The claimants brought their respective actions against the manufacturer of the detectors. The trial court found that both actions were barred by the statute of limitations. On appeal, the court affirmed as to the personal injury claimant. Minn. Stat. § 541.051, dealing with wrongful death or personal injury actions arising out of defective improvements to real property, applied to bar his action. It was not unconstitutionally vague, it did not violate equal protection, and his chronic alcoholism was not a form of insanity that would toll the statute. In addition, the smoke detectors were improvements. The court found that the wrongful death claimant's action was not barred under § 541.051, which applied to her because it was more specific and more recent than the general catchall provision of § 573.02. The wrongful death claimant's action was timely because she brought her action within two years of the fire.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed as to the personal injury claimant, finding that his claim was properly barred by the statute of limitations for improvements to real property. The court reversed as to the wrongful death claimant, finding that her claim was improperly barred by the general statute of limitations for wrongful death actions. The court remanded her claim for a trial on the merits.

 

1252 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Davidson


No. CX-90-1304


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


471 N.W.2d 691; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 596



June 5, 1991, Decided  
June 11, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by State v. Davidson, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 445 (Minn., Nov. 15, 1991)
Reversed by State v. Davidson, 481 N.W.2d 51, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 56 (Minn., 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Winona County; Hon. Dennis A. Challeen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court of Winona County (Minnesota), which convicted defendant of one count of sale or distribution of obscene material in violation of Minn. Stat. § 617.241, subd. 2(a).


OVERVIEW: Section 617.241, subd. 2(a) provided that in order to determine that a work was obscene, the trier of fact had to find that the average person, applying contemporary community standards, would find that it appealed to a prurient interest in sex, depicted specified sexual conduct in a patently offensive manner, and lacked serious literary, artistic, political, or scientific value. Defendant argued that § 617.241, subd. 2(a) violated the federal and state constitutions and that he was deprived of a fair trial by evidentiary and jury instruction errors. The court reversed the conviction and held that § 617.241, subd. 2(a) was void for vagueness.The void for vagueness analysis rendered consideration of state constitutional issues or privacy rights unnecessary. The "community standard" in the statute did not require a community to first set a definable standard if they wanted to keep obscenity out. Communities got to prosecute first and establish the standard by the after-the-fact jury verdict. "Community standard" did not guide law enforcement and did not provide fair notice to citizens that they needed and that the constitution mandated before conduct could be prosecuted.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and vacated the conviction.

Bradley v. Hubbard Broadcasting

1254 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jinkerson


No. C8-90-1964


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


469 N.W.2d 723; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 474



May 7, 1991, Decided  
May 14, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Blue Earth County; Hon. Charles C. Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court, Blue Earth County (Minnesota), which convicted him of conspiracy to possess more than 10 grams of cocaine, a third degree controlled substance crime, and sentenced him to 58 months, the presumptive sentence. Defendant claimed that the evidence was insufficient to prove that he knew the substance he was purchasing was cocaine, and that his sentence violated equal protection.


OVERVIEW: An undercover officer testified to conversations and circumstances leading up to his sale of cocaine to defendant and two accomplices. Accomplice testimony provided the only direct evidence that defendant knew he was buying cocaine, rather than marijuana. On appeal from a conviction for conspiracy to possess more than 10 grams of cocaine, a third degree controlled substance crime, defendant claimed that the uncorroborated accomplice testimony was insufficient to prove the essential element of knowledge that the substance being purchased was cocaine. The officer's testimony and a videotape of the sale connected defendant to the crime and showed him examining the cocaine, and defendant's own testimony corroborated the accomplices' testimony except on the issue of whether he intended to purchase cocaine or marijuana. This was sufficient corroboration under Minn. Stat. § 634.04 (1988), and it was a matter for the jury to determine the weight and credibility given to the accomplices' testimony. Imposition of the presumptive sentence, which was the same severity as a permissible sentence upon conviction of a second degree controlled substance crime, did not violate equal protection.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. White


No. C4-90-1430


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


468 N.W.2d 556; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 350



April 16, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. White, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 397 (Minn., June 19, 1991)
Reversed by State v. White, 489 N.W.2d 792, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 248 (Minn., 1992)



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the trial court (Minnesota), which convicted him of possessing more than 10 grams of cocaine in violation of Minn. Stat. § 152.013, subd. 2(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that his conviction warranted reversal because the trial court gave an erroneous jury instruction, and because the trial court admitted into evidence items seized in an unconstitutional search of a car. On appeal, the court reversed his conviction and remanded the case. The court found that the trial court had based the jury instruction on § 152.028, subd. 2, which permitted the jury to infer knowing possession of the controlled substance by defendant who was driving the car at the time the controlled substance was found in it. Defendant did not demonstrate that the inference was irrational in the case. The trial court properly cautioned the jury on use of the inference and the burden of proof. The court ruled that a police officer's warrantless search of the car for defendant's identification violated the fourth amendment to the United States Constitution or Minn. Const. art. I, § 10. There was no need for an immediate search of the car under the circumstances. The warrantless search could not have been a valid search incident to arrest. The state did not prove that the evidence would inevitably have been discovered without the police misconduct.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the case.

Minnesota Chamber of Commerce v. Minnesota Pollution Control Agency


No. C1-90-1904


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


469 N.W.2d 100; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 388



April 16, 1991, Decided  
April 23, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Minn. Chamber of Commerce v. Minn. Pollution Control Agency, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 486 (Minn., July 24, 1991)
Summary judgment granted by, Injunction denied by, Partial summary judgment denied by, Dismissed by Minn. Chamber of Commerce v. Minn. Pollution Control Agency, 2012 Minn. Dist. LEXIS 194 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari to Minnesota Pollution Control Agency.



DISPOSITION: Petition for declaratory judgment denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Chamber or Commerce sought a declaratory judgment under Minn. Stat. § 14.44 (1990) declaring that respondent Minnesota Pollution Control Agency exceeded its statutory authority, adopted rules without complying with rulemaking requirements, and violated constitutional provisions when it adopted Minn. R. 7050 (1990), which amended the water quality rules.


OVERVIEW: After the MPCA's Citizen Board authorized a hearing process on proposed amendments to the water quality rules, the MPCA published both the proposed amendments and the requisite notice of hearings. An administrative law judge concluded that the proposed changes to Minn. R. 7050.0218 did not constitute substantial change. The MPCA adopted Minn. R. 7050. The Chamber then petitioned the court for a pre-enforcement declaratory judgment. The court denied the petition. The MPCA adequately considered social and economic factors when adopting the rule, as the rulemaking record established that it considered the requisite factors under Minn. Stat. §§ 115.43, subd. 1, and 116.07, subd. 6. Accordingly, the MPCA did not exceed its statutory authority.Minn. R. 7050.0218 did not allow the MPCA to engage in unpromulgated rulemaking. Thus, the rule did not violate due process. The change to Minn. R. 7050.0218 did not raise a new subject matter but, rather, restored part of the procedure followed before the proposed amendments. The standards promulgated in Minn. R. 7050 bore a rational relation to the accomplishment of the legitimate public purpose of maintaining water quality.


OUTCOME: The court denied the Chamber's petition for a declaration that MPCA exceeded, in adopting amendments to its water quality rules, exceeded its statutory authority, adopted rules without complying with rulemaking requirements, and violated constitutional provisions.

McGraw v. Battle Lake


No. C8-90-2127


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 381



April 15, 1991, Decided  
April 23, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Ottertail County; Hon. Homer A. Saetre, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed the adverse judgment of the Ottertail County District Court (Minnesota) in their declaratory action against defendant city, arguing that the trial court erred in interpreting the city's zoning code.


OVERVIEW: The landowners applied for a building permit to construct improvements on their lakeshore property, and the city clerk issued a permit for the purpose of repairing existing buildings. After neighbors reported to city authorities that the improvements appeared to violate the city zoning code, the landowners applied for a variance. After the city denied their variance request, the landowners began a declaratory action. The trial court denied the requested relief, concluding that the city zoning code prohibited the proposed improvements and that the city did not abuse its discretion in denying the variance request. The landowners appealed. In affirming, the court concluded that the trial court properly interpreted the zoning ordinance at issue. The side yard setback for the lot was seven and one-half feet. While the landowners argued that the proper point of measurement was the structure's wall and not the overhang, this would permit an overhang that extended all the way to the lot line, potentially causing damage to adjacent lots. The trial court properly concluded that the setback was measured from whatever part of the structure was nearest to the lot line.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Kedzior v. County of Hennepin


No. C5-90-2277


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 358



April 8, 1991, Decided

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual sought review of a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which granted motions for summary judgment filed by respondents, city, county, and police officers, in the individual's action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and for assault and battery.


OVERVIEW: The individual stopped while jogging to look in display windows of stores. It was after midnight and the area had been subject to smash and grab robberies. An officer stopped the individual and demanded identification. The individual said he didn't have any and walked away. The officer grabbed the individual, threw him against the patrol car several times, and told the individual he was in trouble. Backup officers arrived and arrested the individual, who requested an attorney. At the station he continued to request an attorney. The individual was allowed to call an attorney but still refused to identify himself. He was released 16 hours after his arrest. The individual filed a § 1983 action and assault claims against respondents. Respondents moved for summary judgment, which was granted by the trial court. The individual appealed. The court held that the officers were entitled to qualified immunity on the § 1983 claim, and that the claim against the city failed because the individual was not deprived of a federal constitutional right. The court held that the officers were not immune to the assault claims. The court held that a question of fact existed regarding the assault.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to respondents on the individual's claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The court reversed the grant of summary judgment to respondents on the individual's assault and battery claims.

Jurkovich v. Independent School Dist. No. 708


No. C7-90-2006


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


467 N.W.2d 360; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 269



 March 18, 1991, Decided  
 March 26, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari to Independent School District No. 708.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator superintendent appealed from a decision from respondent the Independent School District No. 708 (district) terminating his continuing employment contract.


OVERVIEW: The superintendent's contract was up for renewal when the legislature changed the tenure status of superintendents to be equal with that of a teacher. A new contract was drafted for the superintendent that incorporated this change, and the superintendent refused to sign the contract, instead choosing to continue under the old contract. The district elected to terminate the superintendent's employment, and the superintendent sought judicial review of this decision. The court noted that a contract for public school educators was subject to legislative enactments on continuing contract law. If the legislature intended to exempt from the amendment teachers who previously acquired continuing contract rights, it should have included a savings clause in the amending act. Since no clause was included, and the effective date of the legislation was specifically postponed, the court concluded that the amendments removing superintendents from continuing contract laws did not apply to him. In addition, the superintendent had the freedom to continue under the existing contract so long as he made no demands. Therefore, the decision of the district was improper.


OUTCOME: The termination decision of the district was reversed.

Evenson v. St. Paul Bd. of Appeals


No. C3-90-2262


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


467 N.W.2d 363; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 268



 March 18, 1991, Decided  
 March 26, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Evenson v. City of St. Paul Bd. of Appeals, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 651 (Minn., May 10, 1991)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. Roland C. Faricy Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the personal representative of the estate of his father, the owner of a vacant building, sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota). The trial court, by a writ of certiorari, affirmed a decision by respondents, a city's board of appeals and others, which denied the owner's request to waive a vacant building fee.


OVERVIEW: The house purchased by the owner was subject to a condemnation order, and the house had remained vacant ever since. The owner never rehabilitated the property. The Board of Appeals granted his first request to have a vacant building fee suspended. The fee was reinstated 10 years later, and the owner was informed the fee might be waived if he presented a rehabilitation plan. When he did not submit a plan, his request for a waiver of the fee was denied. He requested a waiver again on the basis of financial hardship, which was also denied. The trial court affirmed. The court did as well. The court rejected appellant's argument that the vacant building ordinance was an unconstitutional taking. The ordinance did not deny all reasonable uses of the property; the city simply refused to allow the owner to continue an unreasonable use. The fee was not unreasonable or confiscatory, and the fee could have been waived had the owner submitted a rehabilitation plan. He had not done so in 24 years. Appellant had not shown that performance would have been impractical, and a further extension of time would have been inconsistent with the goal of securing the public health, safety, and welfare.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the judgment.

Minnesota League of Credit Unions v. Minnesota Dep't of Commerce


No. C7-90-2054


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


467 N.W.2d 42; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 252



 March 13, 1991, Decided  
 March 19, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Minn. League of Credit Unions v. Minn. DOC, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 545 (Minn., Sept. 6, 1991)
Affirmed by Minnesota League of Credit Unions v. Minnesota Dep't of Commerce, 486 N.W.2d 399, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 174 (Minn., 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari to Department of Commerce.



DISPOSITION: Rule declared valid. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Minnesota League of Credit Unions sought a declaratory judgment pursuant to Minn. Stat. §§ 14.44 and 14.45 (1988) to determine the validity of Minn. R. 2675.6400, subpt. 6.B, a rule that had been proposed by respondent Minnesota Department of Commerce.


OVERVIEW: The rule implemented a statutory procedure by which groups too small to support a credit union of their own could be certified to become members of an existing credit union. It provided that when an existing credit union sought to include a smaller group, the existing credit union was not permitted to solicit individuals to join the select group as a condition for membership in the credit union. The court held that the rule did not violate free speech guarantees. Although it regulated commercial speech, based on the court's application of the four-part test established by the U.S. Supreme Court, it was a permissible regulation. The prohibited solicitation was lawful and not misleading; the government had a valid interest in the limitation of membership in credit unions to groups having a common bond of occupation, association, or residence; and the restriction advanced the governmental interest and went no further than necessary to advance that interest. The rule was not unconstitutionally vague or unconstitutionally arbitrary, did not go beyond the Department's statutory authority, and was adopted in compliance with statutory rulemaking procedures. The rule was declared valid.


OUTCOME: The court declared the proposed rule to be valid.

 

1262 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Holte v. State


No. C2-90-1538


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


467 N.W.2d 346; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 266



 March 13, 1991, Decided  
 March 19, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Holte v. State, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 443 (Minn., May 16, 1991)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Clay County; Hon. Homer A. Saetre, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, landowners who were ordered to spray their land to eradicate grasshoppers, sought review of a summary judgment granted by the District Court, Clay County (Minnesota), in favor of respondents, a county agricultural inspector, the county, and the State, which ruled that the Minnesota Grasshopper Control Act (MGCA) did not conflict with the Minnesota Environmental Rights Act (MERA) and did not deny the landowners due process of law.


OVERVIEW: Under the MGCA, if an owner who was ordered to spray land refused, the land was sprayed by the county, the cost assessed against the land, and the owner possibly charged with a misdemeanor. The owner could challenge the spray order at a post-spray hearing. Alleging that the chemicals sprayed to kill grasshoppers would harm the environment, the landowners argued that the trial court erred in concluding that they did not have a civil cause of action under the MERA. The court disagreed. After reviewing the legislative history of both acts, the court concluded that the legislature did not intend to subject the MGCA to the MERA. Furthermore, pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 645.26, subd. 4 (1988), because the MGCA was the later enactment, it was not subject to the MERA. The court also held that, although the owners had standing to challenge the constitutionality of the MGCA, the statute did not unconstitutionally deprive the landowners of their due process rights. Even though the MGCA permitted the imposition of misdemeanor penalties without a prior hearing, because it provided a post-spray hearing, it did not violate the owners' rights to procedural due process.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Thomas

Court of Appeals of Minnesota


467 N.W.2d 324; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 236

 March 12, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Morrison County; Hon. Thomas Godzala, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the District Court, Morrison County (Minnesota), which upheld a jury verdict that found defendant guilty of driving with an alcohol concentration of .10 in violation of Minn. Stat. § 169.121, subd. 1(e) (1988); and driving after revocation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by state troopers because he was driving erratically. Based on his driving and performance of field sobriety tests, the troopers arrested defendant. Blood samples tested about four days after they were taken from defendant showed a blood alcohol concentration of .15. Defendant was charged with driving with an alcohol concentration of .10. The trial court found defendant guilty of driving after revocation in a bench trial, but did not enter, until five weeks post trial, any findings on the charge. Defendant sought review contending that the trial court's failure to make a general finding within seven days of trial as required by Minn. R. Crim. P. 26.01 compelled dismissal of the charge. The court affirmed the conviction holding that an appellate court would not reverse a conviction for a technical error unless the accused had been prejudiced through the impairment of substantial rights essential to a fair trial. There was no constitutional guarantee that a convicted prisoner would be placed in any particular prison.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of driving with an alcohol concentration of .10 and driving after revocation.

 

1264 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Olson


No. C6-90-831


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


466 N.W.2d 44; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 137



February 12, 1991, Decided  
February 19, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Olson, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 373 (Minn., Apr. 18, 1991)
Reversed by State v. Olson, 482 N.W.2d 212, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 58 (Minn., 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Renville County; Hon. James E. Zeug, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the District Court, Renville County (Minnesota), which convicted him of possession of marijuana in the second degree and denied his postverdict motions.


OVERVIEW: An agricultural agent who was investigating a weed complaint entered a farmhouse. The agent observed marijuana scattered about the house. A deputy unsuccessfully attempted to contact someone at the farm on several occasions. During surveillance, the authorities found defendant and a friend disking weeds with a tractor. A background check on defendant revealed an outstanding warrant for failure to appear on a driving after suspension violation. Subsequently, the officers served the arrest warrant on defendant. When he answered the door at the farmhouse, he was informed that he was under arrest pursuant to the warrant. He was informed that if he wished to re-enter the house to recover any of his belongings, the officers had to accompany him. The officers claimed that defendant consented. In plain view in the house, officers observed what appeared to be a relatively large marijuana processing operation. Nearly 150 pounds of marijuana was confiscated. Defendant was convicted of possession of marijuana in the second degree. On review, the court affirmed. The court stated that, based on the officers' testimony, defendant consented to the search of the premises.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Ohrtman


No. C3-90-1872


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


466 N.W.2d 1; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 128



February 5, 1991  
February 12, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Blue Earth County; Hon. James C. Harten, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of an order from the District Court, Blue Earth County (Minnesota), which dismissed a complaint charging defendant with fourth-degree criminal sexual conduct, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.345, subd. 1(h) (1990), with a church member defendant was counseling.


OVERVIEW: A female church member sought marriage counseling from defendant, a church pastor. During the counseling session, the church member alleged that defendant requested a back rub and lifted his shirt, then after the church member rubbed defendant's back, defendant hugged the church member, compressing her breasts against defendant's chest. The church member also alleged the defendant had an erection during the hug. Defendant was charged with fourth-degree criminal sexual conduct and sought a dismissal of the charge. The trial court dismissed the charge and found that the statute did not apply to consensual hugging. The State sought review. The court found that defendant's actions were inappropriate, unprofessional, and exploitative, that only the legislature could define the crime of criminal sexual conduct, that consent was irrelevant because it was no defense to criminal sexual conduct between a counselor and counselee, and that hugging did not qualify as a sexual touch prohibited by Minn. Stat. § 609.345, subd. 1(h) (1990).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal.

 

1266 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Anderson v. Lofstrom


No. C4-90-1489


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 44



January 14, 1991, Decided  
January 22, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. Mary L. Klas, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant client sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Ramsey County (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment to respondent attorney in the client's action against the attorney arising from the attorney's representation of the client in his post divorce decree motions.


OVERVIEW: The client and his first wife divorced. Under the terms of the divorce, the client received all right, title, and interest in and to the marital homestead on the condition that he pay his ex-wife half of the value of the home or sell the home and give her half the proceeds. The client failed to comply and the divorce court transferred rights in the homestead to the ex-wife, who immediately sold the homestead. The client commenced an action against his attorney, who was awarded summary judgment. On appeal, the court held that the client had notice of the attorney's motions and the possible outcome of the hearing should he fail to respond. Because the client did not produce the necessary additional evidence, the trial court properly granted summary judgment to the attorney. Although the client blamed the attorney for the loss of his homestead, the client clearly and willingly stipulated to the decree of dissolution, which contained the provisions relating to disposition of the homestead and his failure to cooperate resulted in the court ordered transfer of title to his ex-wife and the forced vacation of the property upon sale.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which granted summary judgment to the attorney.

 

1267 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Bruwelheide v. Garvey


No. C8-90-1320


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


465 N.W.2d 96; 1991 Minn. App. LEXIS 42



January 11, 1991, Decided  
January 22, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Bruwelheide v. Garvey, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 479 (Minn., Mar. 15, 1991)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Dakota County; Hon. Michael V. Sovis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injury victim challenged a judgment from the District Court, Dakota County (Minnesota), which found in favor of the victim in his personal injury action against respondent tortfeasors but reduced the jury award for past wage loss by the amount of the victim's paid suck leave as a collateral source under Minn. Stat. § 548.36 (1988).


OVERVIEW: The victim was injured when he tripped over logs that had piled up on a sidewalk in front of the tortfeasors' property. As a result, the victim lost 47 days of work. During this time, he received sick leave pay from his employer. In the victim's personal injury action, the jury returned a special verdict in favor of the victim and awarded him lost wages. However, the trial court deducted the victim's sick leave pay as a collateral source under § 548.36. On appeal by the victim, the court reversed, holding that the sick leave pay was not a collateral source. Section § 548.36(1)(4) specifically referred to disability pay rather than sick leave pay. Disability pay was usually calculated from the amount of a yearly salary and did not increase unless the overall salary increased. However, sick leave pay was calculated from the amount of time worked. Also, in the victim's case, he was given bonus sick leave for not using his days, which he could exchange for cash. Section 548.36(1)(4) also specified a wage continuation plan rather than sick leave. Because the victim's sick leave could be cashed-out on retirement, it was a benefit rather than a wage continuation plan.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Berge


No. C8-90-1219


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


464 N.W.2d 595; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 1325



December 27, 1990, Decided  
January 8, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Berge, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 455 (Minn., Mar. 15, 1991)
Affirmed by State v. Berge, 474 N.W.2d 828, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 248 (Minn., 1991)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Rice County; Hon. William A. Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court, Rice County (Minnesota), which found him guilty of driving under the influence pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 169.121, subd. 1(a) (1988). The trial court accepted as the strongest available evidence of guilt defendant's refusal to submit to a breathalyzer test, and defendant contended that the evidence was improperly admitted against him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was caught speeding by a deputy sheriff. The sheriff detected the odor of alcohol and other indicia of intoxication and performed a variety of field sobriety tests on defendant. Defendant failed the tests. Defendant refused to submit to a blood alcohol test. The State stipulated that its strongest evidence was defendant's refusal to submit to the test. The trial court held that defendant's refusal was admissible into evidence and found defendant guilty. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that: (1) Minn. Stat. § 169.121 provided that evidence of the refusal to take the test was admissible; (2) § 169.121, subd. 2(b), passed constitutional muster under the federal constitution; and (3) since the federal and state constitutions protecting compelled self-incrimination were coextensive, § 169.121, subd. 2(b), was not unconstitutional under the state constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment to find defendant guilty of driving under the influence.

Dorso Trailer Sales, Inc. v. American Body & Trailer, Inc.


No. C6-90-1381


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


464 N.W.2d 551; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 1294



December 24, 1990, Decided  
December 31, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Dorso Trailer Sales v. Am. Body & Trailer, Inc., 1991 Minn. LEXIS 431 (Minn., Mar. 15, 1991)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Dorso Trailer Sales, Inc. v. American Body & Trailer, Inc., 482 N.W.2d 771, 1992 Minn. LEXIS 74 (Minn., 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. Bertrand Poritsky, Judge.
Dorso Trailer Sales, Inc. v. American Body & Trailer, Inc., 372 N.W.2d 412, 1985 Minn. App. LEXIS 4458 (Minn. Ct. App., 1985)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Minn. R. Civ. P. 60.02, the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota) vacated an earlier judgment for respondent franchisor in appellant franchisee's breach of contract action. However, the trial court subsequently granted the franchisor's motion to dismiss the franchisee's first action on res judicata grounds. The franchisee sought review.


OVERVIEW: When the franchisor terminated the parties' agreement, the franchisee filed its first breach of contract action, which eventually resulted in a judgment for the franchisor because good cause apparently was not required to terminate a franchise agreement. After the franchisee learned of the existence of Minn. Stat. § 80E, which required good cause to terminate a franchise agreement with a licensed new motor vehicle dealer, the trial court vacated the earlier judgment pursuant to Minn. R. Civ. P. 60.02(a), (f). However, the trial court subsequently dismissed the franchisee's first and second actions on res judicata grounds. Both sides appealed. The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded, holding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in vacating the earlier judgment because the franchisor's attorney's failure to disclose adverse law was an affirmative misrepresentation that "misled" the trial court. However, the trial court erred in dismissing the franchisee's first action on res judicata grounds after the earlier judgment was vacated under Rule 60.02. Finally, the court held that Minn. Stat. § 80E was not unconstitutional as applied to the franchisor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's vacating of an earlier judgment in favor of the franchisor, but reversed and remanded the trial court's dismissal of the franchisee's first action on res judicata grounds.

 

1270 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. White


No. C0-90-498


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


464 N.W.2d 585; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 1312



December 18, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. White, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 366 (Minn., Mar. 15, 1991)
Writ of certiorari denied White v. Minnesota, 502 U.S. 819, 112 S. Ct. 77, 116 L. Ed. 2d 51, 1991 U.S. LEXIS 4639 (1991)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, St. Louis County; Hon. Jack J. Litman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction in the District Court, St. Louis County (Minnesota), for violation of Minn. Stat. § 617.246, which prohibited the use of minors in sexual performances. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the statute based on the unavailability of the mistake of age defense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant hired a minor to engage in a sexual performance. The minor presented an identification card falsely identifying her as her 26-year-old sister. Defendant asked the minor to repeat the information on the card and compared her signature on her W-4 form with the signature on the card. Defendant also requested the minor's social security card, which the minor said she had left at home. The trial court excluded evidence of defendant's good faith attempt to ascertain the minor's age. The court concluded that the statute was not unconstitutionally overbroad because the statute affected expressive conduct rather than speech, contained a scienter requirement for the content of the performance, and potentially deterred only a limited amount of conduct. The court noted that, by removing the mistake of age defense, the Minnesota legislature did not extend the reach of the statute into a larger area of protected first amendment conduct. The court also rejected defendant's due process challenge, finding that her attempted distinction between mistake of age from mistake of identity was legally insufficient to create such a violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Walkky v. Commissioner of Public Safety


No. C8-90-1494


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 1247



December 17, 1990, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. James D. Rogers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual sought review of an order by the District Court of Hennepin County (Minnesota), which sustained the revocation of the individual's license to drive by respondent public safety commissioner.


OVERVIEW: After a hockey game, the individual departed in his car with others. The occupants of another car complained to a police officer that one of the occupants of the individual's car caused a key scratch to their car. The police officer approached the individual's car, which was stopped n traffic. Upon questioning, the police officer observed signs of intoxication and arrested the individual for driving under the influence of alcohol. The individual refused to submit to testing and his license to drive was revoked under the implied consent law. The trial court sustained the public safety commissioner's revocation of the individual's license. In affirming the trial court's order, the court held that it was not a seizure for the police officer to talk to the individual in the individual's already stopped vehicle. Furthermore, the court held that if any seizure in fact occurred, it was justified by the police officer's investigation of the report of vandalism by the occupants of the other car.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

Woolston v. Monticello Orderly Annexation Area Bd.


No. C0-90-1389


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 1224



December 12, 1990, Decided  
December 18, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Wright County; Hon. Kim R. Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of a decision of the District Court, Wright County (Minnesota), which affirmed the decision of respondent zoning board that denied his request to rezone his property from agricultural to residential.


OVERVIEW: The landowner contended that the decision was arbitrary and capricious and was an unconstitutional taking of property. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the zoning board's reasons were supported by the facts and were related to its purpose. Hence, according to the court, the legal sufficiency and factual basis for the zoning board's decision showed that the reasons were rationally related to the promotion of public health, safety, and welfare. Further, the court held that no taking occurred because there was clearly a substantial state interest, which was to establish a program for managing the land development of the orderly annexation of land to the city. The court also held that the landowner failed to show that the rezoning denial rendered the land economically useless. Finally, the court held that the landowner purchased the land knowing restrictions might be placed on land use and that the city was in the process of implementing its comprehensive land use ordinance. According to the court, those factors diminished any claimed "investment-backed expectations."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which affirmed the zoning board's decision that denied the landowner's request to rezone his property.

Willmar v. Short-Elliott-Hendrickson, Inc.


No. C7-90-1373


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 1240



December 12, 1990, Decided  
December 18, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by City of Willmar v. Short-Elliott-Hendrickson, Inc., 1991 Minn. LEXIS 458 (Minn., Feb. 8, 1991)
Reversed by, Remanded by Willmar v. Short-Elliott-Hendrickson, Inc., 475 N.W.2d 73, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 256 (Minn., 1991)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Kandiyohi County; Hon. John C. Lindstrom, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of the summary judgment granted by the District Court, Kandiyohi County (Minnesota) in favor of respondents, a general contractor, a supplier, and a designer, based on the finding that the city's cause of action for defective design and construction of improvements to its municipal wastewater treatment plant was barred by the two-year statute of limitations of Minn. Stat. § 541.051 (1984).


OVERVIEW: Almost immediately after the plant began operations on September 1, 1982, the city began receiving complaints about offensive odors. The designer worked with the city to solve the problem until 1986, and the city commenced the action on September 30, 1987. The city contended that the trial court erred in holding that the cause of action was barred by the two-year statute of limitations of Minn. Stat. § 541.051 (1984). On review, the court held that the city should have been aware of the problem more than two years before it commenced the suit. The city was aware of the injury upon discovery of the odor problem in 1982 and reasonable minds could not disagree that the city had notice of an unsafe and defective condition by 1985. However, the trial court erred in failing to consider the issue of equitable estoppel as to whether the city reasonably relied upon the designer's representations or inducements. The four-year statute of limitations of the Uniform Commercial Code (UCC), Minn. Stat. § 336.2-725 (1990) did not apply with respect to the city's claim against the supplier because the predominant factor of the transaction was the rendition of services, not supplies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part for a determination on the issue of equitable estoppel.

Western Lake Superior Sanitary Dist. v. Orfei & Sons, Inc.


No. C3-90-589


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


463 N.W.2d 781; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 1219



December 4, 1990, Decided  
December 11, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reconsideration Denied March 15, 1991, Reported at 1991 Minn. LEXIS 58.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, St. Louis County; Hon. David S. Bouschor, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sanitary district sought review of a decision by the District Court, St. Louis County (Minnesota), which granted motions for summary judgment filed by respondents, a contractor, subcontractor, material supplier, and their successors in interest, and dismissed the district's action to recover damages caused by defective pipe on the basis that the action was barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: The sanitary district hired the contractor to design and oversee construction of a waste water system. The subcontractor was hired to install one section of pipeline, with pipe supplied by the material supplier. The pipeline was accepted as complete in 1976. In 1980, 1981, 1982, and 1985, sections of the pipeline ruptured, spilling tons of sewage into a swamp. In 1986, the district brought an action against the subcontractor and the material supplier; the contractor was added as a defendant in 1987. All three filed motions for summary judgment, which were granted by the trial court on the basis that the action was time-barred. The district sought review and the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court affirmed the summary judgment for the subcontractor because a clause in the parties' contract limited actions on it to one year. However, the court reversed the summary judgment as to the remaining respondents because the court found that when the district discovered the defect in the pipeline was a genuine issue of material fact for the jury. The court said that the district investigated several causes for the ruptures before concluding that the pipe was to blame.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of a summary judgment for the contractor and material supplier in the sanitary district's action to recover for damages caused by defective pipe. The court affirmed a grant of summary judgment to the subcontractor based on a provision in the subcontract.

 

1275 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ronmo, Inc.


No. C7-90-1065


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 1200



November 26, 1990, Decided  
December 4, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Norwest Bank Camden, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 370 (Minn., Feb. 6, 1991)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Stephen D. Swanson, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bank sought review of an order from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent State of Minnesota, awarding the State $ 37,242.10 as reimbursement for an overpayment in a condemnation action under Minn. Stat. § 117.155.


OVERVIEW: The State brought condemnation proceedings against two pieces of property subject to over $ 500,000 in mortgages held by the bank. There was an overpayment to the property owner and the bank. Thereafter, the State sued the property owner and the bank to recover the $ 71,937.60 overpayment. The trial court granted summary judgment against the bank for $ 37,242.10, nearly 52 percent of the overpayment. The trial court also granted default judgment against the property owner for $ 34,841.88, just over 48 percent of the overpayment. The bank appealed. The court concluded that the trial court did not err in determining the bank was a recipient within the meaning of Minn. Stat. § 117.155 (1988) and therefore owed the State a proportionate amount of the award. Section 117.155 allowed the condemnation petitioner to recover excess payments from any respondent that received partial payments. The bank argued that § 117.155 unconstitutionally impaired its contract with the property owner and violated substantive principles of due process. The court disagreed. There was no substantial impairment of the contract. The bank had sufficient process to protect its interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's entry of summary judgment for the State in its action against the property owner and the bank that sought reimbursement for an overpayment in a condemnation action.

 

1276 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Sands v. Production Credit Ass'n


No. C9-90-1116


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 1020



October 17, 1990, Decided  
October 23, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal form District Court, Watonwan County; Hon. David Teigum, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff buyers appealed a judgment from the District Court, Watonwan County, Minnesota, that granted summary judgment to respondent credit company. The buyers argued that the credit company was obligated to give them the right of first refusal before it redeemed their foreclosed property purchased by a bank pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 500.24, subd. 6 (1988). The buyers' motion for declaratory judgment and motion to remove the judge were denied.


OVERVIEW: The buyers executed a mortgage in favor of the credit company on two tracts. Tract One was subject to a first mortgage in favor of the bank. When the buyers defaulted on the bank mortgage, the bank foreclosed its mortgage and purchased Tract One. The credit company filed a notice of intent to redeem. After the buyers' statutory redemption period expired, the credit company redeemed Tract One from the bank. The bank did not notify the buyers of the redemption. The trial court held that the buyers were not entitled to rights of first refusal from the credit company. The court agreed and held that Minn. Stat. § 500.24, subd. 6 (Supp. 1987) did not require rights of first refusal for redemption by a junior creditor. The buyers' failure to redeem within 12 months of the bank's foreclosure cancelled the credit company's mortgage. A contrary holding would have extinguished the credit company's valid interests. The buyers' claim that the credit company fraudulently prepared the mortgage had no merit. The trial court properly refused to render a declaratory judgment that the bank could no longer seek a deficiency judgment. The buyers' motion to remove the judge was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the credit company was affirmed.

 

1277 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Application of Morrison County Ice Racing Ass'n etc.


No. C1-90-431


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 1044



October 15, 1990, Decided  
October 23, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to Department of Natural Resources.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator association complained, by writ of certiorari, of an order by respondent Commissioner of the Department of Natural Resources (DNR) (Minnesota), which upheld respondent Morrison County Sheriff's decision denying the association's request for an ice racing permit.


OVERVIEW: The standard enunciated by the Commissioner, that the applicant must demonstrate that ice racing on any particular body of water could be conducted without significant detriment to the public welfare or the natural resources of that body of water, was a proper restatement of existing law requiring consideration of the public welfare and natural resources. The Commissioner's decision to deny an ice racing permit was supported by substantial evidence and was not arbitrary or capricious. Ice racing interfered with the historic use of the lake for ice fishing and the DNR's management of the lake for recreational fishing. It also was objectionable to a majority of local landowners and interfered with their use and enjoyment of their property. Ice racing on Green Prairie Fish Lake in the past had resulted in debris and fluid spills on the lake, and the Commissioner concluded it was unreasonable to accept the risks of pollution of the lake and significant detriment to the natural resources and public welfare. In light of the Commissioner's expertise in this area and the court's narrow standard of review, the court declined to substitute its judgment for that of the Commissioner.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.
