Drewes v. First Nat'l Bank


No. C0-90-663


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


461 N.W.2d 389; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 1007



October 9, 1990, Decided  
October 16, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Drewes v. First Nat'l Bank of Detroit Lakes, 1990 Minn. LEXIS 848 (Minn., Dec. 20, 1990)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Becker County; Hon. William E. Walker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtors challenged a decision from the District Court in Becker County (Minnesota), which denied their motion for a new trial after granting partial summary judgment in favor of respondent creditor in a breach of oral contract claim.


OVERVIEW: The debtors contended that the creditor agreed lower its interest rate on an existing loan if the debtors borrowed additional money. When the creditor refused to lend the debtors any additional funds, they filed an action for breach of an oral contract. The trial court determined that the action was barred by Minn. Stat. § 513.33 (1988), which prohibited the debtors from filing an action on a credit agreement that was not reduced to writing. After judgment was entered for the creditor, the debtors filed a motion for a new trial. The debtors alleged that § 513.33 was an unconstitutional impairment of a contract. In affirming, the court determined that the statute was a substantial impairment because it eliminated the debtors' remedies. However, the statute was not unconstitutional because it demonstrated a significant and legitimate purpose behind the legislation, and the impairment was reasonable and appropriate to serve the public purpose. The statute had a significant purpose in preventing fraud in credit claims. Moreover, the statute was reasonable because it did not require the repayment of any funds or disrupt any settled and completed financial arrangements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the partial summary judgment granted in favor of the creditor on the debtors' breach of oral contract claim.

McDonnell v. Commissioner of Public Safety


Nos. C6-90-53, C7-90-224, C1-90-249, C5-90-478, C0-90-842


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


460 N.W.2d 363; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 962



September 26, 1990, Decided  
October 2, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Driver, 1990 Minn. LEXIS 781 (Minn., Nov. 9, 1990)
Superseded by McDonnell v. Commissioner of Pub. Safety, 473 N.W.2d 848, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 127 (Minn., 1991)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Carver, Chisago & Dakota County; Hon. Duane R. Harves (C6-90-53); Hon. Thomas M. Murphy (C7-90-224 & C0-90-842); Hon. Philip T. Kanning (C1-90-249); Hon. Linn Slattengren (C5-90-478).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from five judgments entered separately in favor of defendants by the District Courts for Carver, Chisago, and Dakota Counties (Minnesota), which found that Minnesota's criminal refusal statute and complied consent advisory, Minn. Stat. §§ 169.121(1)(a), and 169.123(2)(b) (1989) were unconstitutional. The appeals were combined for purposes of oral argument.


OVERVIEW: The drivers were stopped by police for speeding or erratic driving and asked to take a breath test after being read the implied consent advisory pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 169.123(2)(b) (1989). The advisory notified drivers that testing was required and that the driver may be subjected to certain penalties if testing was refused. Minn. Stat. §§ 169.121(1)(a) (1989) provided that the refusal to submit to testing was a gross misdemeanor if the driver had certain prior license revocations. The trial courts found that the consent advisory statute and the criminal refusal statute were unconstitutional. However, on appeal, the court held that the statutes were constitutionally valid. The court held that the Sixth Amendment right to counsel did not attach at the time a driver was given the advisory because formal judicial proceedings had not begun; the right against self-incrimination did not apply under the state or federal constitutions with regard to a driver's refusal to allow testing; the language of the implied consent advisory was reasonable, not unconstitutionally vague or misleading; and the criminal refusal provisions did not violate equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court orders dismissing criminal charges for refusing testing or rescinding driver's license revocations in each of the separate cases and the cases were remanded for trial or other proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

 

1281 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Search


No. C2-90-891


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 929



September 14, 1990, Decided  
September 25, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Search, 1990 Minn. LEXIS 892 (Minn., Nov. 28, 1990)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Search, 472 N.W.2d 850, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 191 (Minn., 1991)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Dakota County; Hon. William F. Thuet, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the District Court, Dakota County (Minnesota), which suppressed evidence taken in a search of a car in which respondent was riding.


OVERVIEW: Police investigating a possible robbery were refused entry to a closet in respondent's home. After waiting for respondent to leave, and observing him leave with a duffel bag, the police stopped a car driven by respondent's girlfriend. The car was registered to respondent. The police stopped respondent and patted him down and placed him in the police car. They searched the duffel bag, which respondent placed in the trunk, and found the stolen items described by the robbery victim. After the items were found, respondent stated that his dad made him do it. The trial court granted respondent's motion to suppress evidence obtained as a result of the search of the duffel bag in the trunk and to suppress the statements. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the search of the duffel bag was not made pursuant to a lawful stop and search because once respondent was in the custody of police and restrained, the contents of the bag posed no danger to the police. As a result, the fruits of the initial, illegal, warrantless search, and respondent's statement were properly suppressed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court, which suppressed the evidence taken from respondent as a result of the illegal, warrantless search and suppressed the statements made by respondent after these items were discovered.

 

1282 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Georgia ex rel. Brooks v. Braswell


No. C4-90-570


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


460 N.W.2d 344; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 902



September 5, 1990, Decided  
September 11, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. Mary L. Klas, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant presumed father challenged a judgment from the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which held that Minn. Stat. § 257.57, subd. 1(b) (Supp. 1989), which extended the limitations period for challenging paternity, violated the federal constitutional guarantee of equal protection and the prohibition against special legislation in Minn. Const. art. XII, § 1.


OVERVIEW: Nine years after the parties' marriage was dissolved, the mother brought an action for child support. The trial court denied the presumed father's motion for blood tests to determine paternity because the statute of limitations to declare nonpaternity then in effect, Minn. Stat. § 257.57, subd. 1(b) (1986), barred his claim. The statute was later amended to extend the limitations period for a presumed father who was divorced after service by publication and did not know of the child's existence at the time of dissolution. On appeal of a judgment holding that the amended statute was unconstitutional, the court reversed and remanded. The statute did not violate the equal protection clause of the federal constitution. It did not grant more favorable treatment to legitimate children than to illegitimate children, a quasi-suspect classification. The court found a rational basis for distinguishing between presumed fathers served notice of their dissolution by publication and those personally served. The statute was not special legislation in violation of Minn. Const. art. XII, § 1. The statute embraced all presumed fathers served by publication and its distinction was not arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for further proceedings. On remand, the trial court was directed to appoint a guardian ad litem for the minor child.

 

1283 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Baker v. American Family Mut. Ins. Co.


No. CX-90-346


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


460 N.W.2d 86; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 899



August 30, 1990, Decided  
September 11, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Baker v. Am. Family Mut. Ins. Co., 1990 Minn. LEXIS 794 (Minn., Nov. 9, 1990)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Clay County; Hon. Homer A. Saetre, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of a decision of the District Court, Clay County (Minnesota), which denied its motion for judgment on the pleadings, or for summary judgment, and held that the Minnesota Assigned Claims Bureau was responsible for automobile-related deaths occurring outside the state and that the assigned claims plan covered the death of the mother of respondent minor pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 65B.64, subd. 3.


OVERVIEW: The minor's mother was driving her uninsured car in North Dakota when she became stuck in a ditch in subzero temperatures. She was later found dead of exposure and hypothermia in an unheated shed on nearby farm. The minor, through a guardian, submitted a claim to the bureau for survivor's economic loss benefits and funeral expenses. These claims were referred to the insurer, who denied the claims. After denying the insurer's motions, the trial court entered judgment for the minor. The insurer sought review, and the court found no error. The court held that the minor, as a claims plan claimant, had a plan of reparation security and was therefore an "insured" under § 65B.43. Further, the court held that the finding that the minor was an insured was consistent with the breadth of the No-Fault Act's policy and intent, under Minn. Stat. § 65B.42 (1986), with the specific "gap closing" policy addressed by the claims plan, and with the claims plan's explicit refusal to preclude the participation of minor children. Therefore, the court held that the insurer was obligated to provide survivor's economic loss benefits and funeral expense benefits through the assigned claims plan.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the findings of the trial court.

 

1284 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Metropolitan Sports Facilities Com. v. General Mills, Inc.


No. C1-90-123


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


460 N.W.2d 625; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 868



August 27, 1990, Decided  
September 4, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Metro. Sports Facilities Comm'n v. Gen. Mills, Inc., 1990 Minn. LEXIS 772 (Minn., Oct. 31, 1990)
Affirmed by Metropolitan Sports Facilities Com. v. General Mills, Inc., 470 N.W.2d 118, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 126 (Minn., 1991)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Deborah Hedlund, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which held the company's ticket purchase agreement with respondent Metropolitan Sports Facilities Commission remained in effect after the repeal of Minn. Stat. § 473.568 (repeal 1984). The company had entered into the agreement in order to satisfy § 473.568's requirements, thereby assuring the local telecast of professional football games.


OVERVIEW: Section 473.568 required 90 percent of the tickets to be sold before a football game would be televised. However, the National Football League (NFL) required 100 percent to be sold. To ensure that a game only 90 percent sold out would be televised despite the NFL's 100 percent policy, the company agreed to buy all unsold tickets. This agreement depended upon § 473.568's validity except in the case of a repeal based upon the agreement's continued effectiveness. When § 473.568 was eventually repealed, the repeal was based upon the continued effectiveness of ticket purchase agreements. Thereafter, the company refused to abide by the agreement, and the Commission obtained a judgment upholding the agreement. Upon review, the court held § 473.568's existence was not a condition precedent because the agreement had provided for a conditional repeal. The court also held the repealer was constitutional under Minn. Const. art. IV, § 17 because the repealer's title had embraced one subject. Finally, the court held that even if the repeal had frustrated the company's purpose, the doctrine of frustration of purpose was inapplicable because the repeal had been contemplated by the parties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that held the company's ticket purchase agreement, which had been entered into in order to satisfy certain statutory requirements, remained in effect despite the statute's repeal.

 

1285 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Omdahl v. Hadler


No. C5-90-612


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


459 N.W.2d 355; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 841



August 15, 1990, Decided  
August 21, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Marshall County; Hon. Larry G. Jorgenson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Commissioner of the Department of Agriculture and others (Commissioner), challenged the decision of the District Court, Marshall County (Minnesota) that granted summary judgment in favor respondents, property owner and others (property owners), in the property owner's action alleging that the Grasshopper Control Law (Law), Minn. Stat. §§ 18.0223-18.0226, violated his constitutional due process and equal protection rights.


OVERVIEW: The property owner argued that the Law violated his due process rights because it permitted the Commissioner to spray his land and then enter the cost to spray as a tax upon his property without affording him a hearing. He also argued that the Law violated his equal protection rights because the Law only applied in grasshopper control zones. The court reversed the judgment, finding that in balancing the property owner's interest in avoiding payment for unnecessary spraying against the government's interest in recovery of its costs in dealing with an emergency situation, the post-deprivation remedies provided by Minn. Stat. chs. 278 and 279 were adequate to meet the requirements of due process. The court reasoned that mere postponement of a hearing until after seizure of the property was not a denial of due process if the opportunity given for the ultimate judicial determination of the liability was adequate. The court found no violation of the property owner's rights to equal protection, explaining that geographical distinctions alone did not violate equal protection as long as they had a rational basis.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

1286 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Turner v. IDS Fin. Servs.


No. C3-90-267


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


459 N.W.2d 143; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 805; 60 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1330



August 8, 1990, Decided  
August 14, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Turner v. IDS Fin. Servs., 1990 Minn. LEXIS 804 (Minn., Oct. 22, 1990)
Reversed by Turner v. IDS Fin. Servs., 471 N.W.2d 105, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 149 (Minn., 1991)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. James D. Rogers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged the decision of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota) entered in favor of appellee, former employee, from the denial of the employer's motion for summary judgment, on statute of limitation grounds, on the employee's claim of discriminatory discharge from employment.


OVERVIEW: The employee brought a claim of discrimination based on religious beliefs, age discrimination, breach of contract, defamation, and intentional infliction of emotional distress after he was discharged from his employment. The trial court denied the employer's summary judgment motion on the claims of religious and age discrimination under the Minnesota Human Rights Act (MHRA). Appeal was taken. The court rejected the employer's claim that the statutory limitations period of Minn. Stat. § 363.06, subd. 3 should begin to run on the date an employee received notice of a future termination. The court based its decision on the plain language of the MHRA, which stated that it was an unfair employment practice to discharge an employee based on impermissible considerations such as age or religion. The court noted that when a claim of discriminatory discharge was made, the most logical date on which to start the limitations period was the date of discharge. Thus, the court found that the occurrence of the practice language of Minn. Stat. section 363.06, subd. 3 referred to the actual discharge date, and not the date on which an employee received notice of a future discharge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the employer's motion for summary judgment on statute of limitation grounds on the employee's claim of discriminatory discharge from employment.

Chock v. Commissioner of Public Safety


No. C1-89-2111


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


458 N.W.2d 692; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 766



July 25, 1990, Decided  
July 31, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Anoka County; Hon. Spencer J. Sokolowski, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review of a decision of the District Court, Anoka County (Minnesota), which sustained respondent Commissioner of Public Safety's revocation of the driver's license pursuant to the implied consent law after the driver was arrested for driving while under the influence. The driver contended that a traffic stop pursuant to a sobriety checkpoint roadblock was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The driver's vehicle was stopped pursuant to a sobriety checkpoint roadblock, and he was arrested for driving while under the influence. His driver's license was revoked pursuant to the implied consent law, and the trial court sustained the revocation. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that the driver's Fourth Amendment rights were not violated when he was stopped pursuant to the roadblock. The court balanced the public interest in battling drunk drivers against the driver's right to personal security free from arbitrary interference. The court found the roadblock met constitutional requirements because it was conducted pursuant to guidelines, the officers did not employ any discretion as to which vehicles to stop, and the detention was brief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order sustaining the revocation of the driver's license.

Willette v. Mayo Foundation


No. C1-89-2299


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


458 N.W.2d 120; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 650



June 22, 1990, Decided  
July 3, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Willette v. Mayo Found., 1990 Minn. LEXIS 753 (Minn., Sept. 14, 1990)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Olmsted County; Hon. Joseph F. Wieners, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant medical center challenged the refusal of the District Court of Olmsted County (Minnesota) to dismiss, on statute of limitations grounds, the medical malpractice lawsuit of respondent patient and respondent patient's spouse.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was sued for medical malpractice by respondents. Respondents claimed that appellant had misdiagnosed a cancerous tumor, and that they had discovered that mistreatment after appellant's physicians had stopped their treatments. Appellant moved to dismiss respondents' lawsuit, citing the statute of limitations. Appellant's claim was that the statute of limitations for medical malpractice began to run once their treatment of respondent patient halted; respondents countered that the statute of limitations only began to run once they discovered appellant's malpractice. The judge assigned the case denied appellant's dismissal motion, and an appeal was taken. On appeal, the court reversed. It held that appellant's view of the law was correct; the statute of limitations ran beginning on the date appellant's stopped treating respondent patient. As the time limit set by the statute of limitations for medical malpractice claims had lapsed, appellant's dismissal motion should have been granted.


OUTCOME: The judgment below was reversed.

Olson v. Blaeser


No. C8-90-121


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


458 N.W.2d 113; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 609



June 13, 1990, Decided  
June 19, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Crow Wing County; Hon. Clinton W. Wyant, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant passenger sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Crow Wing County (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment to respondents, the City of Fifty Lakes and the City of Fifty Lakes Municipal Liquor Store, in the passenger's dramshop action to recover damages for injuries he suffered in an auto accident.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted summary judgment for the City based on the passenger's failure to comply with the 120-day notice of claim provision of Minn. Stat. § 340A.802, subd. 2. The passenger sought review, contending that the City had actual notice of his claim within the 120-day period. Alternatively, he argued the notice of claim provision violated the equal protection clauses of the Minnesota and United States Constitutions. On appeal, the court upheld the judgment. The court ruled that the facts available to the City following the accident were insufficient to put it on actual notice of the passenger's claim. The court found that the accident did not occur on the premises of the City's liquor store and did not involve a municipal vehicle. The court held that although the driver in the car that the passenger was not riding in worked for the city at the liquor store, she was off-duty at the time of the accident and driving a private vehicle. The court concluded that § 340A.802, subd. 2, was not unconstitutional under rational basis scrutiny because it had legitimate purposes which the legislature could reasonably have believed were being promoted by a challenged classification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Radloff v. First American Nat'l Bank, N.A.


No. C4-89-2264


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


455 N.W.2d 490; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 466



 May 8, 1990, Decided  
May 15, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Review Denied July 13, 1990. Reported at 1990 Minn. LEXIS 319.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Morrison County; Hon. Roger M. Klaphake, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the order of the District Court, Morrison County (Minnesota) that granted partial summary judgment against appellants on the basis that any cause of action they had arising from pesticide spraying was barred by Minn. Stat. § 541.07(8).


OVERVIEW: Appellants brought a claim against respondent more than two years after pesticide spraying ruined one of their crops. Appellants contended that their claims against the bank were not barred by § 541.07(8) because the pesticide spraying was part of a continuing tort that tolled the limitations period until the tort was complete. Upon review, the court found that the acts alleged by appellants were not continuous in nature, but separate, unrelated acts. As such, application of the continuous wrong doctrine was inappropriate. Moreover, the court determined that the bank was not covered by § 541.07(8) since it contracted for or hired pesticide services. As such, the statute was inapplicable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the order that rejected the continuos wrong doctrine but reversed that part of the order which held that the claim was barred by the statute of limitations for pesticide spraying.

Erickson v. American Honda Motor Co.


No. C7-89-1674


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


455 N.W.2d 74; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 445; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P12,459



 April 30, 1990, Decided  
May 8, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied, July 13, 1990.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Anoka County; Hon. Spencer J. Sokolowski, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a personal injury action, appellants, a victim and his family, sought review of the judgment of the District Court, Anoka County (Minnesota) that calculated prejudgment interest on only a portion of the award in their favor. Respondent dealer sought review of the trial court's judgment that denied its motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict.


OVERVIEW: The victim, a 12-year-old boy, was seriously injured when he fell off of an all-terrain vehicle (ATV) that had been purchased from the dealer. A jury found that the dealer negligently failed to warn of the dangers of the ATV, and the trial court awarded damages in favor of the victim and his family. The trial court calculated prejudgment interest on only a portion of the award, however, because the dealer had made a settlement offer. In directing a modification of the prejudgment interest award, the court held that the offer was incomplete under Minn. Stat. § 549.09 because it did not include a release of the family's obligation, accepted in an earlier partial settlement, to indemnify for a claim of the dealer against the manufacturer. The court further held that the dealer was not entitled to judgment notwithstanding the verdict because the evidence sustained a finding that the dealer knew or had reason to know of the dangers of operating the ATV. It further found that the warnings that the dealer provided fell short of those required by the manufacturer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment calculating prejudgment interest on only a portion of the jury's award, and it affirmed the trial court's denial of the dealer's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict.

Friedman v. Comm'r of Public Safety


No. C9-89-1708


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


455 N.W.2d 93; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 441



 April 27, 1990, Decided  
May 8, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Granted, July 6, 1990.
Reversed by Friedman v. Comm'r of Pub. Safety, 473 N.W.2d 828, 1991 Minn. LEXIS 128 (Minn., 1991)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Robert H. Lynn, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Hennepin County (Minnesota), which sustained the revocation of her driver's license for one year after she was arrested for driving while under the influence and she refused to take a breath test pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 169.123(2)(a) (1988).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the revocation procedure under § 169.123 was not constitutional under Minn. Const. art. I, §§ 6 and 7. She stated that she did not understand the implied consent advisory because of the words the arresting officer used, although she did not deny that he read her the implied consent advisory three separate times. Upon review, the court found that the decision to submit to chemical testing was not a "critical stage" that invoked defendant's right to counsel under the federal constitution, and she asserted no unique factors within the implied consent scheme that would dictate a higher standard of protection to her right to counsel under the state constitution than under the federal constitution. The court found no compelling reason to hold that the evidence of defendant's refusal to take a chemical test would constitute a violation of her privilege against self-incrimination under the state constitution. The trial court's conclusion that defendant's refusal to take the test was unreasonable was not clearly erroneous. The officer made an effort to explain her obligations to her.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that sustained the revocation of defendant's driver's license for one year after she was arrested for driving while under the influence and she refused to take a breath test.

Horvath v. Liquid Controls Corp.


No. C2-89-1890


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


455 N.W.2d 60; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 450



 April 27, 1990, Decided  
May 8, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied, July 13, 1990.
Review denied by, Request denied by Horvath v. Liquid Controls Corp., 1990 Minn. LEXIS 678 (Minn., July 13, 1990)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Roseau County; Hon. Russell A. Anderson, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant trustee for the heirs of the deceased sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Roseau County (Minnesota) that entered summary judgment in favor of respondent corporation after finding that the trustee's wrongful death action was barred by the 10-year statute of repose of Minn. Stat. § 541.051, subd. 1 (1988).


OVERVIEW: The deceased died after being overcome by anhydrous ammonia fumes. His heirs received workers compensation benefits. The trustee then brought the wrongful death action. The trial court denied the trustee's motion to amend and entered summary judgment in favor of the corporation. The court affirmed the finding that the 10-year statute of repose barred the wrongful death action because the facility was completed more than 10 years before the fatal accident. The court reversed the judgment that found that there was no undertaking of an ongoing duty to use due care in advising the corporation and its employees how to safely operate the facility. Although the claim arising out of an improvement to real property was barred by the statute of repose, a separate and distinct obligation to use due care existed in providing safety information. Thus, the trustee should have been allowed to amend her complaint to add claims for negligence in providing safety information after substantial completion of the facility, and to allege fraud in providing safety information that could operate to toll the operation of the statute. The cause was remanded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding that the statute of repose barred the wrongful death action, but reversed and remanded the judgment that denied the trustee's request to amend.

Ruzic v. Commissioner of Public Safety


No. C8-89-2087


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


455 N.W.2d 89; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 454



 April 26, 1990, Decided  
May 8, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Ruzic v. Comm'r of Pub. Safety, 1990 Minn. LEXIS 709 (Minn., June 26, 1990)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. William S. Posten, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which sustained respondent Commissioner of Public Safety's revocation of his driver's license under the implied consent law, Minn. Stat. § 169.123, subd. 4 (1988). The driver argued the trial court erred in holding a bulldozer, which appellant was driving on private property, was a "motor vehicle" within the meaning of Minn. Stat. § 169.123.


OVERVIEW: A police officer was dispatched to investigate a complaint about loud construction noise coming from a privately owned vacant lot. The officer discovered the driver operating a bulldozer on the lot. While questioning the driver, the officer detected an odor of alcohol, and eventually arrested the driver for DWI. The driver failed the Intoxilyzer test and his driver's license was revoked under the implied consent law. He argued his operation of a bulldozer on private property was specifically excluded from the implied consent law because the bulldozer could not be driven legally on a highway, it ran on tracks, and it was being operated on private property. The court disagreed and noted that the implied consent law had not restricted its definition of vehicles to those that could only have been legally driven upon a highway. The court noted that while the bulldozer ran on movable tracks, Minn. Stat. § 169.01, subd. 2 excepted only devices used exclusively on stationary tracks from the definition of vehicle. The court concluded that it was well established that the implied consent law applied to activity on private as well as public property.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1295 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Willenbring


No. C4-89-2037


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


454 N.W.2d 268; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 349



April 17, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for review denied May 30, 1990.
Review denied by State v. Willenbring, 1990 Minn. LEXIS 726 (Minn., May 30, 1990)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Stearns County, District Court, Hon. Bernard E. Boland, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered in the negative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the charges against him pending in the Stearns County District Court (Minnesota) for a violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.344(1)(d) (1988), which prohibited sexual intercourse with a mentally impaired person. He asserted that § 609.344(1)(d) was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The trial court denied the motion and certified the question to the court as important.


OVERVIEW: Defendant met his victim at the apartment of a mutual acquaintance. He had asked his friend to find him a willing sexual partner. He noticed that the victim seemed mentally handicapped. They had sexual intercourse twice. The victim later stated that she had told defendant that she did not want to have intercourse, but that she acquiesced. Her psychologist, who had worked with her for four years, testified that the victim had an I.Q. of 68 with an adoptive living composite level of a 13-year-old. He stated that she was mentally handicapped and classified as a vulnerable adult. Defendant's motion to dismiss asserted that § 609.344(1)(d) did not provide a consistent frame of reference for determining what conduct was proscribed in a manner that did not encourage arbitrary enforcement. The court held that the statute had a presumption of constitutional validity. It upheld the constitutionality of § 609.344(1)(d) because it required defendant to "know or have reason to know" of the victim's mental impairment. Defendant admitted that he knew the victim suffered from a mental disability. The facts were sufficient to put defendant on notice as to the victim's capacity.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question in the negative.

 

1296 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Edina v. Dreher


No. C7-89-1920


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


454 N.W.2d 621; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 369



 April 17, 1990, Decided  
April 24, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for review denied June 15, 1990.
Review denied by, Request denied by City of Edina v. Dreher, 1990 Minn. LEXIS 691 (Minn., June 15, 1990)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Hennepin County District Court, Hon. James D. Rogers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction by the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) on a citation by appellee city for violation of Edina City, Minn., Ordinance No. 312 § 29(j) (1981) for keeping a dog that disturbed the peace and quiet of persons in a given vicinity as unconstitutionally vague. Defendant claimed deprivation of his due process rights.


OVERVIEW: After receipt of a warning, a city police officer issued a citation to defendant for the barking of his dog in violation of § 29(j). The police department dispatched the police officer to defendant's neighborhood upon the complaint of neighbors, the officer listened from his car for the dog's barking, and based what he heard, issued the citation. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court. The court found that § 29(j), as applied to defendant, violated his due process rights and was void for vagueness because it did not provide an objective standard against which defendant could measure the noise level of his dog's barking. Defendant met his burden of proof beyond reasonable doubt that § 29(j) violated the United States Constitution and the Minnesota Constitution because it lacked specificity as to his own behavior, failed to give notice of the prohibited behavior, and did not discourage arbitrary and discriminatory law enforcement. The city weakened its case against defendant through its failure to call defendant's neighbors as witnesses and relied on the testimony of the police officer; the police officer's annoyance level was the standard under § 29(j).


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for violation of the city's ordinance.

 

1297 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Schmitz v. Stransky


No. C2-89-1789


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


454 N.W.2d 455; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 390



 April 16, 1990, Decided  
April 24, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for review denied June 25, 1990.
Review denied by Schmitz v. Stransky, 1990 Minn. LEXIS 676 (Minn., June 25, 1990)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Rice County District Court, Hon. Bernard E. Borene, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review from a decision of the Rice County District Court (Minnesota) that refused to award her a new trial in her paternity action against respondent alleged father. The mother asserted that the court erred when it refused to permit evidence of the alleged father's past convictions. The alleged father challenged the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 257.69.


OVERVIEW: A mother unsuccessfully brought a paternity action against an alleged father. The trial court refused to grant the mother a new trial, but the court reversed and remanded this decision because it held that the trial court erred when it refused to admit evidence of the alleged father's past robbery conviction for impeachment purposes. Under Minn. R. Evid. 609(a)(1), evidence of a witness's prior convictions were admissible for impeachment purposes if the crime involved dishonesty. Robbery involved dishonesty for purposes of R. 609(a). The court rejected the alleged father's assertion that Minn. Stat. § 257.69, the child custody statute, was unconstitutional under principles of equal protection. Section 257.69 was rationally related to a legitimate government purpose, uniformly applied to parents, enacted genuine distinctions, and created a relevant classification. The court noted that § 257.69 benefited custodial parents regardless of gender and did not violate the Minnesota Human Rights Act, Minn. Stat. § 363.03(4). Also, the trial court properly ordered the alleged father to reimburse the county for attorney fees because counsel was properly appointed him under § 257.69.


OUTCOME: The court found that the mother was entitled to a new trial.

 

1298 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Bennett v. Bursack


Nos. C3-89-1400, CX-89-1572


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 392



April 16, 1990, Decided  
April 24, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Bennett v. Bursack, 1990 Minn. LEXIS 593 (Minn., June 25, 1990)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bar challenged an order of the trial court (Minnesota), which denied the bar's motion for a new trial following an adverse verdict in a dram shop action under Minn. Stat. § 340A.801 brought by respondents, trustee and widower, to recover against a bar that had illegally sold liquor to the driver of a car that struck the widower's vehicle, killing his wife.


OVERVIEW: The widower was seriously injured and his wife was killed in a two-car accident. The widower and trustee for the wife's heirs brought claims against the driver of the other car, who was intoxicated at the time, and two bars that had provided liquor to the driver or her boyfriend. Following a trial, the jury found that the second had bar illegally sold liquor to the driver, contributing to her intoxication. The jury allocated fault as 70 percent to the second driver, 30 percent to the second bar, and zero percent to the first bar. The trial court denied the second bar's motion for JNOV or a new trial. The second bar appealed and challenged the trial court's application of Minn. Stat. § 340A.801 (Supp. 1985), the sufficiency of the evidence as to the first bar, and the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 604.02, subd. 1 (1986). The court affirmed and held that the trial court properly applied Minn. Stat. § 340A.801 because the statute included the right to sue for pecuniary loss. The jury's finding that no "sale" of beer occurred at the first bar was not contrary to the evidence because the driver's boyfriend testified that he stole the beer and had no intention of paying for it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the verdict and judgment in favor of the trustee and widower.

County of Pine v. Petersen


No. C3-89-1994


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


453 N.W.2d 718; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 317



 March 26, 1990, Decided  
April 3, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for review denied May 30, 1990.
Review denied by County of Pine v. Petersen, 1990 Minn. LEXIS 638 (Minn., May 30, 1990)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Pine County District Court, Hon. James R. Clifford, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Pine County (Minnesota), which entered a money judgment against the father to reimburse respondent county for public assistance previously furnished to respondent wife and the parties' child and which entered an order for future support contributions in the county's parent contribution proceedings under Minn. Stat. § 256.87 (1988).


OVERVIEW: The father contended that the trial court erred in making no finding on his reasonable monthly expenses when it determined the father's obligation. The county argued that the trial court was only required to determine the father's net income as defined for child support guideline purposes under Minn. Stat. § 518.551, subd. 5(a) (1988). The court reversed the judgment and remanded for additional trial court findings, holding that the trial court erred in failing to consider the father's expenses. Because Minn. Stat. § 256.87 required application of the child support law under Minn. Stat. § 518.551, the court concluded that further trial court findings were needed to determine the father's contributions under Minn. Stat. § 256.87. The court found that the father's affidavit clearly put before the trial court a claim of reasonable expenses destroying his ability to pay support and that, on remand, the trial court was required to determine the merit of his claim as a matter of fact.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for additional trial court findings.

 

1300 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State by Humphrey v. Alexander


No. C8-89-1957


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 289



March 21, 1990, Decided  
March 27, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of an order of the trial court (Minnesota), which granted respondent State of Minnesota's motion to enjoin the landowner's denial of access to his property pursuant to condemnation proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The State entered into condemnation proceedings with the landowner pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 268.027 and Minn. Stat. ch. 117. The landowner refused to permit any inspection by the State in order to appraise the property and the trial court granted the State's motion to enjoin the landowner's denial of access to his property. Upon the landowner's appeal, the court affirmed the order, holding that the trial court properly enforced the State's right to appraise the landowner's property pursuant to the laws of eminent domain. Minn. Stat. § 117.041 provided that for the purpose of making surveys and examinations relative to any proceedings under this chapter, it should be lawful to enter upon any land, doing no unnecessary damage. Moreover, the court held that although the Minnesota statutes did not specifically authorize the trial court to enjoin the landowner's denial of access under the circumstances, such a specific statutory grant was not necessary for the trial court to grant injunctive relief. The order fell within the trial court's inherent power to supervise the procedures over which it had jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which granted the State's motion to enjoin the landowner's denial of access to his property pursuant to condemnation proceedings.

 

1301 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


American Dog Owners Ass'n v. Minneapolis


No. C7-89-1741


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


453 N.W.2d 69; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 284



 March 19, 1990, Decided  
March 27, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Hennepin County District Court, Hon. Deborah Hedlund, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant dog association and appellee City of Minneapolis sought review of judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which denied the dog association's motion for attorney fees and which granted a summary judgment that Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 64.120(b)(1) and (2) was unconstitutionally overbroad.


OVERVIEW: The dog association initiated an action pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 that alleged that Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 64.120(b)(1) and (2) did not afford the procedural due process required by U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The dog association also claimed that Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 64.110 was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The lower court granted the dog association summary judgment, holding that Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 64.120(b)(1) and (2) violated procedural due process. The dog association then brought a motion for attorney fees, pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988, which the lower court denied. The dog association appealed the denial of the attorney fees and the City appealed the decision that Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 64.120(b)(1) and (2) was unconstitutional. On review, the court reversed and remanded. The court stated that the application of the four factors used by the United State Supreme Court to determine whether the procedures of a statute were constitutional demonstrated that § 64.120(b)(1) and (2) comported with the requirements of due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 64.120(b)(1) and (2) was unconstitutional and the denial of attorney fees to the dog association and remanded.

 

1302 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


K.E. v. Hoffman


No. C3-89-697


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


452 N.W.2d 509; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 248



 March 7, 1990, Decided  
March 13, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by K.E. v. Hoffman, 1990 Minn. LEXIS 454 (Minn., May 7, 1990)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Hennepin County District Court, Hon. Steven Z. Lange, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former student appealed from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment to respondent teacher and school district in an action alleging that the teacher sexually abused him and that the school district was vicariously liable for the teacher's actions. The prior student also alleged that the teacher failed to provide proper counseling and supervision.


OVERVIEW: Respondents argued that the trial court's application of Minn. Stat. § 541.073 (Supp. 1989) § 541.073 deprived them of due process of law by reviving the former student's time-barred sexual abuse claim. The court found that the legislature did not impair respondents' due process rights by enacting § 541.073, which lifted the limitations bar and revived the former student's claim against them. The court rejected respondents' contention that retroactive application of § 541.073 was unconstitutional because it worked a special hardship upon them. Where, as here, the statute had a reasonable relation to the state's legitimate purpose of affording sexual abuse victims a remedy, respondents' due process rights were not violated. Because § 541.073 retroactively applied in this case, a question arose regarding when the former student knew or should have known that the alleged abuse was the cause of his injuries. Since this was a question of fact which the trial court did not consider, the trial court improperly granted summary judgment to the respondents and the court remanded the case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to respondents and remanded the case for a trial on the merits.

 

1303 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


No. C1-89-1167


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


451 N.W.2d 886; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 204



 February 21, 1990, Decided  
February 27, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Hennepin County District Court, Hon. Myron S. Greenberg, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of felony and gross misdemeanor malicious punishment of a child, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.377 (1986).


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of malicious punishment causing substantial bodily harm to an eight-year-old child (felony) and causing substantial emotional harm to a six-year-old child (gross misdemeanor). The court did not agree with defendant that the statute as applied was unconstitutional or that the evidentiary rulings were incorrect. The term "substantial emotional harm" had a commonly accepted quantitative meaning. A person of ordinary intelligence could understand the degree of injury that was prohibited by the statute. Minn. Stat. § 609.377 (1986) was sufficiently definite to allow defendant to determine with reasonable certainty that his physical abuse of the children fell within the range of the conduct disapproved. The evidence showed severe and cruel physical punishments administered with belts, cords, sticks and cigarettes. The psychologist testified as to the effect on the child, corroborated by the foster parent. The trial court properly allowed expert testimony on the behavioral characteristics of physically abused children and whether that abuse caused emotional harm to the six-year-old child. The evidence was sufficient to support the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions.

 

1304 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Swenson v. Lafayette Lumber Co.


No. C1-89-1587


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 178



February 13, 1990, Decided  
February 20, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Swenson v. Lafayette Lumber Co., 1990 Minn. LEXIS 617 (Minn., Apr. 13, 1990)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, husband and wife, sought review of the summary judgment entered by the trial court (Minnesota) in their suit against respondent builders, alleging breach of contract and negligent design of a barn. Appellants asserted that the trial court applied the wrong statute of limitations and erred in concluding that their suit was time-barred.


OVERVIEW: The trial court concluded that appellants' cause of action accrued when they became aware that the barn's ventilation system was not functioning properly, and that their suit more than six years later, was barred by Minn. Stat. § 541.05 (1978), which provided a six-year limitations period. On appeal the court affirmed agreeing with the reasoning of the trial court. The court also found that the appellants' action was barred by Minn. Stat. § 541.051 (1988), a two-year statute of limitations on improvements to real property, which expressly stated that an action accrued upon discovery of the injury. Although appellants' action was pending at the time the statute went into effect, the enabling clause of the amendment stated that it applied to all matters pending. The court found that the law relating to the statute of limitations on improvements to real property was in a state of flux during that period; thus, appellants lost no vested right when the legislature amended § 541.051. The court agreed with respondents' claim that a retroactive application of § 541.051 would not be unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court judgment was affirmed.

 

1305 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Borgen


No. C0-89-1922


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 194



February 13, 1990, Decided  
February 20, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Borgen, 1990 Minn. LEXIS 635 (Minn., Apr. 13, 1990)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Borgen, 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 203 (Minn. Ct. App., Feb. 22, 1989)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the trial court (Minnesota), which on remand, gave him a 70 month-presumptive sentence for his first degree intrafamilial sexual abuse conviction, held that the custody point was not assignable to his criminal history score, but found that a misdemeanor point was assignable.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's sentencing worksheet for his sexual abuse conviction gave him a criminal history score of three based on a prior felony conviction, a custody status point, and a misdemeanor point. The original sentencing court gave him a 70-month presumptive sentence and a criminal history score of two based on the custody point and the prior felony conviction. On remand, the trial court confirmed the presumptive sentence, but found that the custody point was not assignable because appellant was not in custody when he committed the sexual abuse offense. The trial court held that a misdemeanor point was assignable because appellant was sentenced for three misdemeanors prior to his sentence for his sexual abuse charge. The court affirmed, holding that the sentence was not an abuse of discretion. Although it misread the sentencing transcript, the trial court was free to review the criminal history score. The trial court was not limited to deciding the custody status point and it could constitutionally correct appellant's sentence as long as the sentence was not increased. The trial court was not bound by the erroneous determination that the misdemeanor point did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which on remand, confirmed appellant's presumptive sentence for his sexual abuse conviction, but held that a misdemeanor point rather than a custody status point was assignable to his criminal history score.

In re Conservatorship of Bauer


No. C7-89-1559


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


451 N.W.2d 347; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 164



 February 7, 1990, Decided  
February 13, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Hennepin County, District Court, Hon. Melvin J. Peterson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant conservator sought review of the judgment of the Hennepin County, District Court (Minnesota), which directed the conservator to reimburse respondent Department of Human Services for the conservatee's cost of care at the state mental hospital for the period following completion of the conservatee's criminal sentence.


OVERVIEW: The conservatee was convicted and sentenced to prison for murder. On appeal, the conviction was reversed due to the conservatee's mental condition. On remand, the trial court stayed further proceedings and civilly committed him to the mental hospital. Eight years later, the conservatee pleaded guilty to manslaughter and was sentenced to 43 months, which he had already served during the pendency of his appeal, although he remained committed civilly. The trial court ordered reimbursement for his treatment costs for the period of civil confinement after the completion of his criminal sentence. On appeal, the conservator argued that the Minn. Stat. § 246.50, subd. 5 (1988) was unconstitutional in differentiating between civil and criminal patients. In affirming, the court held that criminals were committed partly for the protection of the public, which was a rational basis for distinction between the two classes of patients. Thus, the court held that while the conservatee was criminally confined, reimbursement was not required, but thereafter his commitment continued civilly, for which period treatment costs were subject to reimbursement under § 246.50, subd. 5.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1307 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Paulson v. Lapa, Inc.


No. C8-89-1313


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


450 N.W.2d 374; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 96



 January 17, 1990, Decided  
January 23, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Motion denied by Paulson v. Lapa, Inc., 1990 Minn. LEXIS 552 (Minn., Mar. 22, 1990)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Swift County District Court, Hon. Keith C. Davison, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the widow of a decedent, brought a dram shop action against appellant club for damages resulting from the death of her husband in a one-car automobile accident. The percentage of fault attributable to the club for decedent's injuries was 50 percent and 50 percent to the decedent. The Swift County District Court (Minnesota) entered judgment in favor of the widow and her young sons. The club appealed.


OVERVIEW: The wife also sought review of the trial court's imputation of the negligence of decedent to the surviving family members. On appeal, the court affirmed the jury's award of damages against the club and held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in rejecting the club's proposed jury instruction regarding the dram shop's obligation to determine the extent of decedent's intoxication. The trial court was correct in refusing to reduce the jury's award for loss of support damages by the percentage of decedent's fault. The court reversed the trial court, however, on the issue of reducing the amount awarded to the non-negligent dependents for pecuniary damage by the percentage of decedent's comparative fault. Viewing the charge to the jury as a whole, it appeared that the instructions given did convey to the jury a clear and correct understanding of the law. Only the pecuniary loss award was governed by the comparative fault statute. The wife and the surviving children were innocent third parties who did nothing to contribute to the decedent's death. Thus, under the plain language of the comparative fault statute, their damages were not subject to reduction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in part, reversed in part, and remanded the action.

 

1308 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Henke v. Dunham


No. C5-89-1429


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


450 N.W.2d 595; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 103



 January 16, 1990, Decided  
January 23, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Henke v. Dunham, 1990 Minn. LEXIS 602 (Minn., Mar. 22, 1990)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Ramsey County District Court, Hon. George O. Peterson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a patient and her spouse, challenged an order of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which entered a final judgment, dismissing their medical malpractice action against respondent radiologists for failure to timely comply with Minn. Stat. § 145.682 (1988).


OVERVIEW: The patient and her spouse brought a medical malpractice action against the clinic and the radiologists. The first trial court granted the clinic's motion to dismiss the complaint with prejudice for failure to comply with the discovery requirements of Minn. Stat. § 145.682. A second trial court denied a radiologist's motion to dismiss and granted the patient's motion to extend the time for compliance. Under a writ of prohibition, the first trial court refused to grant an extension and entered judgment against the patient, who sought review. The court reversed, finding that (1) dismissal with prejudice was an excessive punishment because the patient's neglect was excusable; (2) there was no showing that the clinic would be substantially prejudiced if an extension of time were granted; (3) because the second trial court granted an extension and denied a radiologist's motion to dismiss, it was unfair to require the remaining defendant to bear the entire burden of defense; and (4) Minn. Stat. § 145.682 complied with the constitutional requirements of furthering the legitimate state interest of discouraging meritless medical malpractice claims.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Dutton


No. C5-89-801


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


450 N.W.2d 189; 1990 Minn. App. LEXIS 33



 January 9, 1990, Decided  
January 16, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Brown County District Court, Hon. Noah S. Rosenbloom, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his judgment of conviction from the Brown County District Court (Minnesota) for psychotherapist-patient criminal sexual conduct in violation of Minn. Stat. §§ 609.344, subds. 1(i), 1(j), 609.345, subds. 1(i), 1(j) (1986).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a pastor who agreed to counsel a church member for low self-esteem, grief from her daughter's death, premenstrual syndrome, and emotional issues. Although she expressed that she was not seeking counseling for sexual issues, defendant persisted in "working" with her on her sexuality. Several sexual encounters occurred and defendant was eventually prosecuted and convicted on felony charges. On appeal, the court concluded that: (1) the evidence was sufficient to support a finding of emotional dependency, defined as a situation where the therapist knows the patient is unable to withhold consent to having sexual contact, based on the admission of over 32 cards and letters where the member literally signed over control of her life to defendant; (2) expert testimony on the nature of dependent personality disorder was relevant and properly admitted; (3) admission of a check given to defendant by the member was relevant to the degree of influence he had over her; and (4) defendant could not challenge the constitutionality of the criminal statutes on vagueness grounds because he knew, and had informed the member, that his conduct was a felony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

In re Welfare of J. K.


No. C6-89-970


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 1358



December 21, 1989, Decided  
January 2, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Welfare of J.K., 1990 Minn. LEXIS 531 (Minn., Mar. 8, 1990)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a decision of the Hennepin County Juvenile Court (Minnesota), which ordered that a minor child be placed with a neutral foster family and denied the mother's motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: After more than two years after a juvenile protection petition was filed, the trial court ordered the mother's child placed with a neutral foster family. On appeal, the mother alleged that the length of time between the filing of the petition and the entry of amended findings violated her due process rights. Stating that a parent's rights had to be balanced against the best interests of the child when child protection was at issue, the court concluded that the mother failed to show that her ability to present her case and defend against the allegations of the petition was prejudiced by the delay in bringing the case to trial and the lack of continuous trial proceedings. The court also rejected the mother's claim that the petition did not provide fair notice of the claims and the grounds on which they were based. The petition listed nine types of physical abuse, two types of sexual abuse, four instances in which the mother was suspected of threatening the children and their fathers, and that the children were dependent and neglected as defined in Minn. Stat. § 260.015, subd. 6(d) and subd. 10(b), (c) and (f) (1986). Finally, the trial court's findings supported its determination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the juvenile court.

1312 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Welfare of D.J.V.


No. C3-89-1090


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 1323



December 19, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor sought review of a decision of the trial court (Minnesota), which adjudicated him delinquent on a disorderly conduct charge for his involvement in a school fight when he was 14 years old.


OVERVIEW: After he was adjudicated delinquent for his involvement in a fight at school, the minor appealed and contended that the trial court abused its discretion by imposing a disposition of residential placement. The court held that although the minor had completed the residential work program, the issue of his disposition was not moot because it was capable of repetition, yet evaded review. The court noted that in reviewing juvenile delinquency cases, it examined the trial court's disposition orders to determine if they were necessary to the rehabilitation of the child. The minor argued that all of the evidence, other than his own admission, was inadmissible hearsay. However, the court held that in juvenile disposition hearings, the trial court was allowed to receive any information that was relevant to the disposition of the cause including reliable hearsay and opinions. The court noted that the other evidence admitted by the trial court pertained to the minor's behavior before and after the fight, was properly admitted, and was relevant to his rehabilitation. The court affirmed the disposition ordered by the trial court because it found that it was supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

1313 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Weber-Connelly, Naegele, Inc.


No. C4-89-1082


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


448 N.W.2d 380; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 1273



 November 29, 1989, Decided  
December 5, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Dakota County District Court, Hon. Raymond Pavlak, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of an order from Dakota County District Court (Minnesota), which granted an award of just compensation for the taking of respondent property owner's 13 outdoor advertising structures pursuant to the Minnesota Outdoor Advertising Control Act, Minn. Stat. ch. 173 (1988). The State contended that the trial court erred in awarding compensation for lost rental income using a gross rent or gross annual multiplier.


OVERVIEW: The owner had billboard structures that the State condemned. The trial court found that the taking was necessary for a public purpose. After viewing the premises and hearing testimony from two appraisers, the fair market value was calculated using the cost approach to valuation. The State maintained that the method of valuation dictated by the common law of eminent domain was the cost approach. The court upheld the judgment of the lower court. The valuation was based on the testimony of both parties' witnesses that the owner possessed the right to rent the structures. Although the State was not required to compensate for the rights taken, Minn. Stat. § 173.17 permitted compensation for lost rental income. The conclusion that rental income was compensable was consistent with the common law of eminent domain, and it was irrelevant that the billboards were personal property because Chapter 173 clearly permitted compensation for personal property interests. The State's appraiser categorized the income as business income but acknowledged that if the billboards could not be relocated, an award of business income was appropriate. That the billboards could not be relocated was unrefuted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award granted to the property owner.

 

1314 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Conservatorship of Edelman


No. C3-89-683


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


448 N.W.2d 542; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 1274



 November 29, 1989, Decided  
December 5, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Hennepin County District Court, Hon. Melvin J. Peterson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient appealed from the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which ordered her committed to a residential care facility due to her inability to provide for her own health and safety, claiming that the trial court erred in appointing her a conservator, but not a conservator to her estate.


OVERVIEW: The patient was committed to a residential care facility due to her inability to provide for her own health and safety. A petition to establish a conservatorship of the patient and estate was subsequently filed. The trial court appointed a conservator of the person, but refused to appoint a conservator of the estate, and an appeal was taken. The court held that because the patient was diagnosed as paranoid and delusional, the appointment of the conservator was the least restrictive means available for the patient's protection. The court also determined that the appointment of the conservator did not violate the patient's privacy rights because the patient had not refused to take her medication. Finally, the court concluded that the trial court correctly refused to appoint a conservator over the patient's estate because the evidence showed that the patient was competent to control her own financial affairs and therefore the appointment of a conservator was not found by clear and convincing evidence. The court upheld the trial court and denied the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.
