1316 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


R.S. v. State


No. C6-89-824


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


447 N.W.2d 205; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 1147



 October 24, 1989, Decided  
October 31, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, Request granted R.S. v. State, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 904 (Minn., Dec. 29, 1989)
Reversed by R.S. v. State, 459 N.W.2d 680, 1990 Minn. LEXIS 273 (Minn., 1990)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Ramsey County District Court, Hon. Thomas E. Brennan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of the decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondents, State and Hennepin County, and dismissed the father's declaratory judgment action requesting an interpretation and determination of the constitutionality of the Reporting of Maltreatment of Minors Act (Act), Minn. Stat. § 626.556.


OVERVIEW: Hennepin County Community Child Protection Services (HCCPS) received an anonymous call regarding the daughter. The caller described certain behavior, but did not allege that the daughter had been the victim of sexual abuse, and neither alleged nor hinted that either the father or the mother might have been involved if any abuse were to be found. HCCPS investigated the incident, put failed to follow the statutory procedures set out in the act. Instead, HCCPS interviewed the daughter at school, without giving written notice to school officials as provided by the Act. Because there was no indication that the parents were suspected of abusing the daughter, they should have been contacted prior to the daughter's interview. The had standing and had presented the courts with a justiciable controversy. Absent an allegation that parents were or may have been involved in abuse, parents were to be contacted prior to the first interview with the child. The court denied the father's requests to declare the Act unconstitutional, to require an assessment of the parental rights in individual investigations, and to declare that anonymous, uncorroborated calls were not reports under the Act.


OUTCOME: The court granted the father's request to order the County to follow the mandates of the Act, but found the Act constitutional and otherwise affirmed the lower court's decision.

 

1317 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State by Cooper v. French


No. C2-89-1064


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 1152



October 24, 1989, Decided  
October 31, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. French, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 898 (Minn., Dec. 15, 1989)
Reversed by State by Cooper v. French, 460 N.W.2d 2, 1990 Minn. LEXIS 287 (Minn., 1990)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator landlord sought a writ of certiorari from the final order of an administrative law judge that denied the landlord's motion for a trial de novo. Respondent State of Minnesota, by the Commissioner, Department of Human Rights, claimed that the landlord discriminated against his lessee in violation of Minn. Stat. § 363.03, subd. 2(1)(a) (1988), when he refused to rent property to her because she lived with a man to whom she was not married.


OVERVIEW: The landlord, who was a member of an evangelical church, rented a home to a lessee. Subsequently, he sought to terminate her lease. The lessee filed a charge of discrimination against him. The State claimed that the landlord violated Minn. Stat. § 363.03, subd. 2(1)(a) (1988), when he refused to rent to her because she lived with a man to whom she was not married. An administrative law judge (ALJ) granted the State's request for partial summary judgment on the issue of liability. On writ of certiorari from the ALJ's final order, the court held that the ALJ correctly concluded that the landlord's actions constituted a violation of the Human Rights Act (Minnesota). The court held that it was obliged to follow precedents that had extended the protection of the Act to unmarried individuals living together. The court held that the Act was not unconstitutional for failure to provide for jury trials. When the legislature created new rights and remedies unknown to common law, it could withhold the right to jury trial. The court held that the landlord's right to practice his religion was subject to reasonable government regulations if the government had an overriding compelling interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the administrative law judge's final order.

 

1318 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lundberg


No. C4-89-157


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 1149



October 23, 1989, Decided  
October 31, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the trial court (Minnesota), which convicted him of obstructing legal process in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.50 (1988) and disorderly conduct under Minn. Stat. § 609.72, subd. 1 (1988).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after engaging in a loud confrontation with police after defendant's brother was arrested. On appeal from his convictions, defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to convict under either charge. In affirming, the court ruled that evaluation of the sufficiency of the evidence to support the convictions required the court to view the evidence in the light most favorable to the State and assume that the jury believed the State's witnesses and disbelieved any contrary evidence. The court noted that the credibility of the witnesses and the resolution of conflicting testimony was for the jury to determine. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction for obstructing legal process under Minn. Stat. § 609.50 (1988) when it showed that defendant physically obstructed or interfered with the police officer in the performance of his duties. The court also held that the evidence showed that defendant's repeated refusal to leave the scene, his tone of voice, loudness, agitated demeanor, and use of abusive language did in fact disturb the peace as that offense was defined under Minn. Stat. § 609.72, subd. 1(3).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1319 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Minnesota Ins. Guaranty Asso. v. St. Paul Risk Services, Inc.


No. C2-89-576


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 1155



October 23, 1989, Decided  
October 31, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Minn. Ins. Guar. Ass'n v. St. Paul Risk Servs., 1990 Minn. LEXIS 437 (Minn., Jan. 12, 1990)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a workers' compensation plan and its claims administrator, sought review of a judgment entered by the Dakota County District Court (Minnesota), which granted a motion for summary judgment by respondents, a trucking corporation and the Minnesota Insurance Guaranty Association (MIGA). The injured employee had filed suit against the trucking corporation and appellants intervened, claiming a right to indemnity and to subrogation.


OVERVIEW: The employee sustained injuries on the job when his vehicle was struck by one owned by the trucking corporation. Appellants made payments to the employee, who then filed suit against the trucking corporation. When its liability insurer was declared insolvent, the trucking corporation sought coverage against appellants' subrogation claim from the MIGA, which admitted coverage in 1987. In 1988, however, the Minnesota Insurance Guaranty Act was amended to exclude certain subrogation claims. Respondents then sought a declaratory judgment that appellants' subrogation claim was unenforceable pursuant to the amendments to Minn. Stat. § 60C-09. The district court granted their motion for summary judgment. The court affirmed, finding that appellants did not have a vested right in their subrogation claim against MIGA because they had not obtained a final judgment against respondents. The trial court correctly ruled that pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 60C.09, subd. 2, appellants' claim for indemnity or contribution against MIGA was barred. The court held that § 60C.09, subd. 2, was not unconstitutional because it was rationally related to the achievement of a legitimate government purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1320 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Rockford


No. C4-89-742


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 1118



October 16, 1989, Decided  
October 24, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Resolution of the City of Rockford, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 864 (Minn., Nov. 22, 1989)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator railroad company sought review of a decision of the Minnesota Department of Transportation (MnDOT), which granted respondent city authority to install a public crossing over railroad tracks.


OVERVIEW: Half the population of the city lived in an area which was bounded by a river on one side and the railroad company's tracks on the other. The sole connecting point to the outside was a 24-foot wide road that ran under the tracks. Although the underpass was adequate to handle routine traffic, it would not have permitted prompt evacuation in an emergency. The court held that substantial evidence supported MnDOT's decision that the proposed public crossing was the safest and most practical location. Any access that did not cross the tracks would lead across the river, requiring a costly bridge and damaging the environment. Such access would have led away from the city's business district, would have required emergency vehicles to drive much further, and would have been of diminished value to citizens in an emergency. Although MnDOT had previously denied a similar proposal, that decision did not establish a precedent because it denied the petition without prejudice. MnDOT's determination was not unconstitutional because the crossing was necessary to protect public safety. Because Minn. Stat. § 219.072 (1988) did not apply retroactively, the cost of the crossing could not be allocated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed MnDOT's decision.

 

1321 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Mortenson v. State


No. CX-89-485


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


446 N.W.2d 674; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 1106



 October 5, 1989, Decided  
October 17, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Dakota County District Court, Hon. Gerald W. Kalina, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the decision of the Dakota County District Court (Minnesota), which ordered a jury trial to establish the appraised current market value of an easement that the Commission of Transportation sought to convey to respondent trustees, the owners of the underlying fee.


OVERVIEW: The State acquired an easement over property in an eminent domain proceeding. The trustees acquired fee title to the property encumbered by the State's easement. The trustees contacted the Department and expressed an interest in purchasing the easement. The State had the property appraised by an independent appraiser. The State offered the easement to the trustees at the price given by the appraiser, but the trustees commenced the action against the State. The issue was whether the trial court erred in concluding that a jury trial was necessary to establish the appraised current market value of the easement. The court determined that the legislature intended to create a limited right in favor of the fee owner. The court explained that holding a jury trial at the offer stage of the conveyance process could have resulted in a duplication of effort if the underlying fee owners rejected the jury's determination of value and then later the Commission decided to condemn the fee. The court concluded that the only right Minn. Stat. § 161.43 created in favor of the fee owner was the right to receive an offer for the sale of an easement at an appraised value.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which ordered a jury trial to establish the appraised current market value of an easement the Commission sought to convey to the trustees.

State v. Reese


Nos. C6-88-2613, C1-89-374


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


446 N.W.2d 173; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 1063



 September 26, 1989, Decided  
October 3, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for review denied November 15, 1989.
Review denied by State v. Reese, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 577 (Minn., Nov. 15, 1989)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Freeborn County District Court, Hon. Thomas R. Butler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Freeborn County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of drug and paraphernalia possession in violation of Minn. Stat. §§ 152.09, 152.15, 152.02, 151.37, 151.29, 152.092; of the unlawful possession of hypodermic needles under Minn. Stat. §§ 151.40, 151.29; and of the unlawful possession of brass knuckles and that denied his motion for an acquittal, or for a new trial, or to vacate his convictions.


OVERVIEW: The district court convicted defendant of multiple counts of possessing drugs, paraphernalia, hypodermic needles, and brass knuckles and denied his motion for an acquittal, or for a new trial, or to vacate his convictions. The court affirmed the paraphernalia, hypodermic needles, brass knuckles, and the drug possession convictions except for his misdemeanor and petty misdemeanor convictions, which it ordered the trial court to vacate on remand. The court reasoned that probable cause existed for the warrant to search defendant's house, noting that the warrant was partially based on a presumably credible witness's personal knowledge and the corroboration of his testimony. The court also held that defendant's sentence was improper under Minn. Stat. § 609.035 (1988) because his convictions arose from the same course of criminal conduct. The court further found that defendant was properly convicted of both the needles and the paraphernalia charges due to the ample evidence that he possessed the needles and other forms of paraphernalia. The court also determined that limiting the use of certain evidence and issuing a curative instruction allowed the admission of challenged evidence.


OUTCOME: The court partially affirmed and partially reversed defendant's convictions for the possession of drugs and paraphernalia and remanded the action.

 

1323 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Karney v. Banovetz


No. C7-89-430


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 1035



September 18, 1989, Decided  
September 26, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Karney v. Banovetz, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 807 (Minn., Nov. 22, 1989)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband appealed from a decision of the trial court (Minnesota), which terminated the husband's child support obligation to respondent wife, reserved the issue of future child support, and denied forgiveness of child support arrearages.


OVERVIEW: The wife and the husband agreed to transfer custody of the parties' child to the husband. The husband was awarded custody of the child, but his motion for child support was reserved. The court rejected the husband's claim that Minn. Stat. § 518.64, subd. 2 was unconstitutional as a violation of separation of powers. The statute did not keep the court from modifying support or applying judicial discretion to current support requirements based on the facts of each case. Instead, the statute limited the time period to which the modification applied, and therefore did not impair the judicial function. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in reserving future support. The wife's only income was from her spouse and she had not been employed for ten years because she had stayed home to raise children. Under the circumstances, the wife's decision to limit her income was made in good faith. The husband was not a victim of sexual discrimination under Minn. Stat. § 363.03, subd. 4(1) (1988). There was no evidence to show that the courts discriminated by treating differently, based on sex, custodial parents who have limited their incomes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Swenson v. Fifty Lakes


No. C8-89-923


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 957



September 5, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, residents of a city and neighboring landowners, sought review of the judgment of the trial court (Minnesota), which dismissed their petition challenging respondent city's decision to grant respondent property owner a conditional use permit to establish a campground on his property, which was located within the city limits of the city.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed a petition filed by the residents of a city and neighboring landowners challenging the city's decision to grant the property owner a conditional use permit to establish a campground on his property. The city had adopted a county ordinance that set forth the requirements for campground developments. The residents of the city and the neighboring landowners argued that the city had also adopted an amendment to that ordinance, which prohibited a campground such as the landowner's within one-eighth of a mile of a residence without the written approval of the resident. On appeal, the court determined that the city had not adopted the amendment. The court also found that the conditional use permit by the city was not unreasonable, arbitrary, or capricious. The court pointed out that community opposition to a landowner's desire to use his property for a particular purpose was not a legally sufficient reason for denying the conditional use permit. Because the opponents failed to meet their burden of proof that the reasons for the city's determination were legally insufficient or without factual basis, the trial court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1325 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fan


No. CX-88-2467


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


445 N.W.2d 243; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 964



 August 29, 1989, Decided  
September 5, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied October 31, 1989.
Review denied by, Request denied by State v. Suifong Fan, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 464 (Minn., Oct. 31, 1989)
Writ of certiorari denied Fan v. Minnesota, 494 U.S. 1030, 110 S. Ct. 1480, 108 L. Ed. 2d 617, 1990 U.S. LEXIS 1526 (1990)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Ramsey County District Court, Hon. J. Thomas Moot, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota) for employing and permitting a 14-year-old to engage in a sexual performance in violation of Minn. Stat. § 617.246, subd. 2 (1986). Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the statute, contending that the statute was facially overbroad and unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant owned and operated a bar that featured nude dancers. Defendant hired a 14-year-old to dance for the patrons in a sexually explicit manner and the evidence supported the jury's determination that the child engaged in a sexual performance as defined in Minn. Stat. § 617.246, subd. 1. Defendant brought post-trial motions challenging the constitutionality of the statute and the court's preclusion of a fact defense based on mistake of age. Defendant contended that the statute's definition of sexual performance would prohibit protectible First Amendment expression. The court held that although it was marginally possible that the statute could reach a valid First Amendment application, the statute did not substantially prohibit constitutionally protected expression. The court also held that the term "lewd exhibition of genitals" reasonably gave notice that it was illegal to employ a fourteen year old girl to perform the acts described. The statute gave adequate warning of the proscribed conduct and marked boundaries sufficiently distinct to administer and enforce the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court and defendant's convictions for employing a 14-year-old to engage in a sexual performance at his bar. The court upheld the constitutionality of the state statute under which defendant was convicted.

In re Estate of Edhlund


No. C6-89-385


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


444 N.W.2d 861; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 970



 August 29, 1989, Decided  
September 5, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Blue Earth District Court, Hon. James C. Harten, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant estate personal representative sought review of the judgment of the Blue Earth District Court (Minnesota), which found that the 1987 amendment to Minn. Stat. § 256B.15 was not a retroactive application of law as applied to respondent county's claim for a medical assistance.


OVERVIEW: A husband and wife made a joint application for medical assistance in 1982. The wife received medical assistance from 1982 until 1986. The husband received medical assistance from 1982 until his death in 1986. The husband left no estate. The wife, who died in 1988, neither applied for nor received medical assistance benefits after 1986. Prior to August 1987, Minn. Stat. § 256B.15 (Supp. 1987) allowed a claim against the estate of a person who had received medical assistance at the death of the person if single. However, if there was a surviving spouse, the claim could not be made against the estate of the recipient spouse. In 1987, the statute was amended to allow claims against the estate of a person for medical assistance benefits received by that person or the person's predeceased spouse. In 1988, the county filed a medical assistance claim against the wife's estate. The trial court applied the 1987 amendment to the county's claim. On appeal, the court determined that the trial court's application of the amendment was error because an examination of the 1987 amendment and its legislative history failed to indicate any legislative intent to apply the amendment retroactively.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and remanded.

State v. Lanam


No. C8-89-95


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


444 N.W.2d 882; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 963



 August 25, 1989, Decided  
September 5, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Nobles County District Court, Hon. Jeffrey L. Flynn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Nobles County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of first degree criminal sexual conduct in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.342, subd. 1(a), (e)(i) (1988).


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of first degree criminal sexual conduct in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.342, subd. 1(a), (e)(i) (1988). Defendant was convicted of abusing the four-year-old son of a friend. The child, who was ruled incompetent, identified the perpetrator by defendant's first name. Defendant suggested the child was referring to the friend's former boyfriend, who also had the same first name. The child was removed from the mother's home following a finding of neglect. The evidence that defendant, rather than the former boyfriend, committed the acts consisted of out-of-court statements made by the child to the child's foster mother. On appeal, the court determined that the trial court had not abused its discretion in admitting the incompetent child's out-of-court statements identifying defendant because the circumstances showing reliability outweighed doubts created by the finding of incompetency. The court also found that the admission of the statements did not deny defendant the right of confrontation. Therefore, the court found that defendant's challenge to the sufficiency of the evidence was without merit. Accordingly, defendant's conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Lynch v. Minneapolis


No. C9-89-218


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 952



August 23, 1989, Decided  
August 29, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the trial court (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment for respondents, the five police officers and the city, on all claims, even those on which summary judgment had not been sought. Appellant had asserted three state law claims (battery, assault, and intentional infliction of emotional distress) and three claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 against the city and all officers.


OVERVIEW: Appellant also asserted a conspiracy claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1985 against all respondents. Appellant asserted two additional 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims (negligent training and deliberate indifference to violation of constitutional rights) against the city. The claims arose from a confrontation between appellant and the police officers during the arrest of appellant's nephew. The city and two of the officers sought summary judgment on all counts against them. The remaining officers sought summary judgment on all counts against them except those relating to assault, battery, and excessive force. On appeal, the court held that: (1) where appellant alleged physical injury as a result of the officers' conduct and submitted medical evidence to support her claim and where two witnesses corroborated her story, the record disclosed genuine issues of material fact on the battery and assault claims; (2) the amount of force used by the officers and its reasonableness was a triable issue under appellant's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim; and (3) where appellant did not identify any specific inadequacy in the city's police training program, summary judgment was proper on the negligent training claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's summary judgment for the city on the claims of negligent training, deliberate indifference to constitutional rights, conspiracy to interfere with civil rights, and intentional infliction of emotional distress. The court reversed the summary judgment for the three officers on the battery and assault claims and the summary judgment for all five officers on the excessive force claim. The court remanded for trial.

Johnson v. Morris


No. C8-88-2614


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


445 N.W.2d 563; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 947



 August 22, 1989, Decided  
August 29, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Granted October 19, 1989.
Review granted by Johnson v. Morris, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 570 (Minn., Oct. 19, 1989)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Johnson v. Morris, 453 N.W.2d 31, 1990 Minn. LEXIS 86 (Minn., 1990)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Jackson County; Hon. Harvey A. Holtan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver challenged the grant of summary judgment by the District Court, Jackson County (Minnesota) for respondents, police officers and their governmental employers, on the driver's action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and under Minnesota common law. The driver argued that the trial court erred because reasonable officers would have known that the initial stop, arrest, and detention violated his constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: The first police officer stopped the driver and asked to see his license. The driver refused and drove away. A chase ensued. A second and third police officer were radioed for assistance. The third officer fired a round into the driver's right front tire and then into his right rear tire. The vehicle was moving at 30 miles per hour. The driver stopped and was arrested. The driver filed a § 1983 action and made various state tort law claims, against all three officers and their governmental employers. The trial court granted summary judgment for all respondents on all claims. The court found that the issues were whether the trial court properly granted summary judgment for: 1) the officers individually on claims brought under § 1983; 2) the governmental entities on claims brought under § 1983; and 3) for all respondents on tort claims brought under Minnesota common law. The court affirmed in part. The initial stop was not a clear violation of constitutional rights. A reasonable officer could have concluded that there was probable cause for the arrest. The court reversed upon the jury question as to whether the third officer's use of force, the gunshots, created § 1983 liability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision for respondents in part, reversed it in part, and remanded the driver's cause of action. The court reversed as to the third police officer regarding both the driver's § 1983 claim and the state tort law claim.

 

1330 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dockman


No. C1-89-214


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 934



August 16, 1989, Decided  
August 22, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Dockman, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 771 (Minn., Sept. 21, 1989)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the trial court (Minnesota), which convicted defendant of criminal sexual conduct in the first degree pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 609.342, subd. 1(a) (1988), and sentenced him to 162 months, a triple departure from the presumptive sentence of 54 months.


OVERVIEW: The five-year-old victim attended day care on the first floor of an individual's home. Defendant rented a room on the third floor. The victim told her mother that defendant had engaged in sexual acts with her, forcing her to so some of the acts. A physical examination supported these claims. The victim's testimony at trial was consistent with statements made to her mother. The trial court's jury instructions, which stated that defendant would be allowed to call witnesses, did not suggest that defendant was required to call witnesses or that a failure to introduce testimony, was an indication of guilt. The trial court did not err in ruling that evidence of defendant's prior conviction for criminal sexual conduct could have been used for impeachment purposes. Credibility was a central issue, and impeachment by the conviction would have aided the jury in determining who to believe. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant to a triple departure. The victim's particular vulnerability due to her very young age supported the trial court's departure. Multiple forms of penetration made defendant's crime more serious than the typical sexual assault.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Imlay v. Lake Crystal


No. CX-88-2551


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


444 N.W.2d 594; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 933



 August 11, 1989, Decided  
August 22, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Granted. As Amended August 24, 1989.
Review granted by, Motion granted by Imlay v. City of Lake Crystal, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 486 (Minn., Oct. 25, 1989)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Imlay v. Lake Crystal, 453 N.W.2d 326, 1990 Minn. LEXIS 90 (Minn., 1990)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Blue Earth County District Court, Hon. Harvey A. Holtan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and  [**2] remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff personal injury victims sought review of a judgment of the Blue Earth County District Court (Minnesota), which entered a money judgment against defendant city in an action brought under the Dram Shop Act after the victims were hit by an uninsured motorist. The court deducted collateral sources, calculated interest, and found that the city did not waive municipal immunity.


OVERVIEW: The victims were hit by an uninsured motorist while riding a motorcycle and were seriously injured. The victims brought suit against the city under the Dram Shop Act for serving the uninsured motorist liquor. The trial court reduced the verdict by deducting collateral sources. On review, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court found that the trial court correctly determined that the city's purchase of insurance was not a waiver of Minn. Stat. § 604.02's limit on liability. Minn. Stat. § 466.15 (1988) did not apply to lawsuits commenced under the Dram Shop Act. The court also found that the deduction of uninsured motorist benefits as a collateral source was not unconstitutional. The city's maximum liability was 40 percent of the judgment after deduction of collateral sources. However, post-verdict interest could be added to that figure. In view of the compensatory nature of pre-verdict interest, the trial court erred in assessing it, and it was reversed. Because the trial court's interest award did not provide separate figures for pre-verdict and post-verdict interest, the case was remanded for a determination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the collateral source deductions, reversed the trial court's calculation of interest, and remanded for separate figures for pre-verdict and post-verdict interest so that the money judgment against the city and in favor of the victims would be correct.

 

1332 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Atkinson


No. C7-89-959


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


443 N.W.2d 864; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 901



 August 9, 1989, Decided  
August 15, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Atkinson, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 896 (Minn., Oct. 13, 1989)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Hennepin County District Court, Hon. Patricia L. Belois, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which, on the petition of respondent Hennepin County, involuntarily committed him to a regional treatment center and concluded that Minn. Stat. § 253B.04, subd. 1 (1988) did not deny equal protection to minor children 16 years of age and older. The statute was defended by observer Minnesota Department of Human Services.


OVERVIEW: At the hearing on the County's petition, the patient's mother requested that the patient be informally admitted to the regional center. However, § 253B.04, subd. 1 provided that only children under age 16 could be admitted on parental consent. Consent by an appointed guardian was prohibited by Minn. Stat. § 525.56, subd. 3(1) (1988). The patient was 17 years old and unable to communicate due to his mental retardation. The trial court, therefore, ordered involuntary commitment. On appeal, the patient's counsel argued that application of Minn. Stat. § 253B.04, subd. 1 (1988) was an unconstitutional violation of the patient's equal protection rights and that the regional center improperly refused to admit the patient informally. In affirming, the court refused to consider the claim against the center, which was not a party. The court ruled that a legislative classification was upheld if the classification was rationally related to a legitimate state interest and that § 253B.04, subd. 1 promoted a legislative purpose of conferring upon a child 16 years of age or older the right to request informal admission and to object to imposition of treatment on parental authorization.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1333 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kuball


No. CX-89-115


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 912



August 8, 1989, Decided  
August 15, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Motion granted by State v. Kuball, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 796 (Minn., Oct. 13, 1989)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of a trial court (Minnesota), which convicted him of driving with an expired driver's license, in violation of Minn. Stat. §§ 171.27 and 171.241 (1988); driving with an expired motor vehicle registration, in violation of Minn. Stat. §§ 168.09 and 168.10 (1988); and driving without insurance, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 65B.67, subd. 3 (1988).


OVERVIEW: At trial, defendant admitted all allegations in the complaint. On appeal, defendant argued that: 1) the State broke the law in arresting and prosecuting him; 2) the trial court erred in refusing to send questions of law to the jury; and 3) the State's requirements of insurance, vehicle registration, and having a driver's license unconstitutionally infringed upon his right to travel. The court disagreed. A police officer had a reasonable basis for stopping defendant's motor vehicle. The officer had noticed that defendant's license plate displayed only a partial registration sticker, and a computer check of the vehicle plates revealed that the registration had expired. Defendant's allegations that the trial court was prejudiced against him and that the trial court and the prosecutor engaged in a conspiracy against him were wholly unfounded. The trial court properly decided all questions of law, and there were no fact issues for the jury to resolve because defendant admitted the facts underlying the charges in the complaint. Defendant failed to meet his burden of showing that the challenged statutes were unconstitutional. Operating a motor vehicle was a privilege, not a right.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1334 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tilden


No. C6-88-2305


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 898



August 7, 1989, Decided, August 15, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Tilden, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 401 (Minn., Oct. 13, 1989)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of a trial court (Minnesota), which found him guilty of possession of marijuana with intent to sell and possession of marijuana without tax stamps on the package.


OVERVIEW: The warrant affidavit stated that a property owner had a garage on his premises out of which he did mechanical and body work on vehicles and that he had access to many vehicles located in his yard. It further stated that the owner would be getting a large quantity of marijuana on a specific date and that the marijuana would be for sale later that afternoon. The court held that the warrant was not intended to cover automobiles arriving on the premises during the search. When the police began their search mid-afternoon, they apparently thought that the delivery had already been made and had no reason to search vehicles arriving on the premises while they were carrying out their search. The court concluded, however, that the totality of the circumstances established sufficient probable cause to justify a warrantless search of defendant's vehicle when it arrived. Having searched the premises, the officers knew the delivery had not yet occurred, the officers recognized defendant's name from previous drug investigations, and defendant wanted badly to get back to his vehicle. Based on this chain of events, in view of the mobility of defendant's vehicle, went beyond a mere suspicion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1335 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Westinghouse Credit Corp. v. J. Reiter Sales, Inc.


No. C5-88-2618


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


443 N.W.2d 837; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 890



 August 1, 1989, Decided  
August 8, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Hennepin County District Court, Hon. Peter J. Lindberg, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guarantor sought review of a decision from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), ordering that the guarantor's right and title to and interest in a deferred compensation plan be assigned to respondent creditor.


OVERVIEW: The guarantor personally guaranteed a $ 92,334 debt owed to respondent creditor by the guarantor's business, which defaulted. The trial court assigned the creditor the rights to the guarantor's unfunded deferred compensation plan, which totaled $ 141,991. The trial court refused to assign the creditor any rights to the guarantor's fixed fund and equity retirement funds. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not err in determining that the unqualified, unfunded deferred compensation plan was not an asset exempt from assignment under Minn. Stat. § 550.37, subd. 24 (1986). The funds in the deferred compensation plan were used by the guarantor's employer for its benefit, not placed into a trust fund. The deferred compensation plan was nothing more than an unsecured promise by the guarantor's employer to pay him retirement installments from funds that might or might not be available. The trial court properly assigned the entire amount of deferred compensation to the creditor, even though it exceeded the amount of the judgment, because the creditor would receive nothing until the guarantor retired, at which time it could collect only the amount of the debt plus interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Reinsurance Asso. of Minnesota v. Dunbar Kapple, Inc.


No. C2-89-464


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


443 N.W.2d 242; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 863



 July 26, 1989, Decided  
August 1, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Dodge County District Court, Hon. Bernard E. Borene, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of the judgment of the Dodge County District Court (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment to respondent manufacturer in the insurer's suit seeking contribution and indemnity for amounts the insurer had paid to an injured employee pursuant to the insurer's compensation liability policy insuring the employer.


OVERVIEW: The insurer filed suit against the manufacturer seeking contribution and indemnity for amounts the insurer had paid to an injured employee pursuant to the insurer's workers' compensation liability policy insuring the employer. The insurer alleged that the manufacturer had negligently designed and manufactured the machinery upon which the employee was injured. Because the manufacturer's liability insurer was insolvent at the time of the action, the trial court entered summary judgment dismissing the insurer's claim pursuant to Illinois and Minnesota statutes providing that a subrogee insurer could assert no claim for indemnity or contribution against a person whose liability insurer was insolvent. The insurer appealed and the court affirmed. The court found that 73 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 1065.84-3(b)(v) and Minn. Stat. § 60C.09, subd. 2 (1988) barred the insurer's suit for indemnity and contribution from the manufacturer. The court found that sound public policy consideration supported the rule that an insured of an insolvent insurer could not be liable for payments made by a third-party.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the manufacturer.

 

1337 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Clough v. Ertz


No. C3-89-280


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


442 N.W.2d 798; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 731



 June 21, 1989, Decided  
June 27, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Chisago County District Court, Hon. J.B. Gunderson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police chief brought an action against respondents, the mayor and city council members, arising from the termination of his employment. The Chisago County District Court (Minnesota) granted respondents' motion for summary judgment on the police chief's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 First Amendment violation claim, breach of employment contract claim, Minn. Stat. § 181.932, subd. 1 claim, and defamation claim. The police chief appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the mayor confronted the chief regarding a friend's arrest for driving while intoxicated (DWI), the chief contacted a county attorney and an investigation was initiated. Without discussing the incident with the council members, the chief secretly taped a conversation with the mayor regarding the mayor's policy to arrest only non-residents and belligerent drunks for DWI. He then issued a memorandum regarding the policy. After learning of the memorandum, the council members terminated the chief's employment due to his inability to work through or with the council and perform his duties. The court held that questions of fact existed as to whether the chief's protected free speech was a motivating factor in his termination and whether the council members demonstrated that they would have fired the chief anyway. Under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, the council members could incur liability for a single unlawful termination. For similar reasons, there were questions of fact as to the breach of contract and the Minn. Stat. § 181.932, subd. 1 whistle-blower claim. The defamation claim failed as a qualified privilege was established. The publication occurred as part of a work performance review.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment to respondents on all claims except the defamation claim and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Schmitz


No. C5-88-2182


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 748



June 16, 1989, Decided  
June 27, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the trial court (Minnesota), which convicted him of two counts of first degree burglary and attempted second degree criminal sexual conduct.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of first degree burglary and attempted second degree criminal sexual conduct. Defendant appealed his conviction, contending denial of his right to a fair trial when the prosecutor encouraged the jury to hold defendant accountable to promote a productive, law-abiding society. The court held that the prosecutor's statements did not constitute misconduct. However, because defendant also did not object to the remark at trial and did not ask for any curative instructions, the issue was not preserved for review and it was presumed that the defense found nothing improper in the argument. The court also noted that the jury was instructed several times to decide the case based on the evidence. The court also held that evidence seized as a result of defendant's consent to a search of his trailer by police officers was admissible under the plain view exception. The court also held that use of defendant's prior convictions that were within a three-year period was allowable for impeachment purposes. The trial court judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment against defendant.

 

1339 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Thorp v. Price Bros. Co.


No. C5-88-2604


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


441 N.W.2d 817; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 717



 June 8, 1989, Decided  
June 20, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied August 15, 1989.
Review denied by Thorp v. Price Bros. Co., 1989 Minn. LEXIS 569 (Minn., Aug. 15, 1989)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Wright County District Court, Hon. Gary J. Meyer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged an order from the Wright County District Court (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment to respondents, equipment designers and an installer, in the employee's action seeking recovery for an injury allegedly caused by defective equipment at his place of employment. The district court ruled that the two-year statute of limitations, Minn. Stat. § 541.051, had run on the employee's action.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured while working on a concrete molding machine and conveyor system. The equipment had been designed and installed by respondents. The employee was unable to return to work and was allegedly unable to access the plant until more than one year had passed. The employee alleged that at the time he and his attorney inspected the plant equipment, he discovered the defective and unsafe condition that caused his injury. The employee did not file his action until more than two years had passed since the date of the accident. In affirming the lower court's entry of summary judgment for respondents, the court ruled that § 541.051's two-year statute of limitations had run on the employee's claim because the equipment was "improvement to real property" under the statute. The limitations period was triggered by the discovery of the injury, not the discovery of the unsafe condition or improvement. Because the action was filed more than two years after the injury accrued, the action was barred. The court ruled that application of an amendment to the law did not violate the employee's due process rights because his claims would have been barred under the prior law as well.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from the lower court.

State v. Krejci


No. C6-88-1297


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


441 N.W.2d 510; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 672



Decided, June 6, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Krejci, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 699 (Minn., July 27, 1989)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by State v. Krejci, 458 N.W.2d 407, 1990 Minn. LEXIS 224 (Minn., 1990)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Delila F. Pierce, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of conviction of first degree assault by the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota). Defendant claimed that his rights under Minn. Const. art. I, §6 were violated when his trial was held in Hennepin County and that his Sixth Amendment rights were violated by the prosecution as his waiver to counsel and to a jury trial were not knowingly and intelligently made.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to the trial court's conviction of defendant in Hennepin County for the offense of assault, defendant appealed arguing that Minn. Stat. § 627.15 was unconstitutional as applied in his case because Hennepin County was an improper venue for defendant's trial. Defendant also argued that he did not knowingly and intelligently waive his right to counsel and that he did not voluntarily waive his right to a jury trial. Defendant contended that Hennepin County was the improper venue because all of the elements of the first-degree assault occurred in Renville County. Reversing the trial court's judgment, the court held that since both the physical act and the injury took place in Renville County, the essential elements of first degree assault took place in Renville County. Therefore, prosecuting defendant in Hennepin County violated Minn. Const. art. I, § 6. The court further noted that defendant's Sixth Amendment right to counsel was not violated as defendant was informed of the nature and the seriousness of the charges, the allowable punishments, and the benefit of the plea bargain. Lastly, the court concluded that defendant voluntarily waived his right to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's judgment of conviction.

State v. Ellis


No. C4-88-2416


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


441 N.W.2d 134; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 651



 May 23, 1989, Decided  
May 30, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied July 12, 1989.
Review denied by State v. Ellis, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 453 (Minn., July 12, 1989)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Hennepin County, District Court, Hon. Harry S. Crump, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Hennepin County, District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of the petty misdemeanor of failure to comply with a city building inspector's rental property repair order in violation of the Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances 87.90(f).


OVERVIEW: The repair order directed defendant to repair or replace broken or missing window glass and screens on rental property that he owned. Defendant did not comply, but instead informed the inspector that the tenant had contracted to perform the repairs. The parties stipulated that there had been no broken or missing windows or screens at the time defendant entered into the lease. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, rejecting his argument that because of the lease he was no longer in control of the property and thus could not be held responsible for violations of the housing code that occurred on the premises during the lease term. The court agreed with the trial court that defendant did allow another to occupy a building that did not comply with the building code, in violation of the ordinance. The court also held that defendant had not met his burden of proving that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it was too vague or overbroad, the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction, and Minn. Stat. § 504.18 subds.1, 2 did not permit the landlord to transfer to his tenant the ultimate responsibility for complying with the housing code.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1342 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Holscher v. State


No. C1-89-309


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 587



May 10, 1989, Decided  
May 16, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Holscher v. State, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 845 (Minn., July 12, 1989)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a denial of his postconviction relief petition by a trial court (Minnesota), which held that an unconstitutional jury instruction in his murder trial 29 years earlier would not have caused confusion as to the State's retention of the burden of persuasion to prove intent and that his delay in bringing the petition was an alternative ground for denying relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed an 11-year-old girl by striking her in the head with a gun. After 29 years had elapsed from the date of conviction, defendant filed his petition for postconviction relief. Defendant's delay in bringing the petition was an appropriate factor to consider in determining whether or not to grant relief. The length of time was significant enough to support the affirmance of the denial of postconviction relief. Defendant argued that an unconstitutional jury instruction was continuing to disadvantage him by being used to justify his current statutory maximum sentence for kidnapping and criminal sexual conduct. Defendant was charged with first-degree murder but convicted of only third-degree murder, which, under the statute of conviction, former Minn. Stat. § 619.10 (1957), did not include intent to kill as an element. Because the crime of conviction did not include intent to kill as an element, the jury that convicted defendant of third-degree murder was not confused or misled by the language in the instructions regarding intent to kill. Therefore, the instruction was in no way prejudicial to defendant, and any error would have been harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Christensen


No. C1-88-2065


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


439 N.W.2d 389; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 555



 April 27, 1989, Decided  
May 9, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied, June 9, 1989.
Review denied by State v. Christensen, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 427 (Minn., June 9, 1989)
Writ of certiorari denied Christensen v. Minnesota, 493 U.S. 936, 110 S. Ct. 329, 107 L. Ed. 2d 319, 1989 U.S. LEXIS 5114 (1989)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Hennepin District Court, Hon. Sean J. Rice, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged the decision of the District Court of the Hennepin (Minnesota), which dismissed the possessing drug paraphernalia charge, a misdemeanor offense, filed against defendant on the ground that Minn. Stat. § 152.093 (1986) was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The charge against defendant stemmed from her operation and ownership of a retail store. The store sold posters, tobacco, records, and items allegedly useful for ingestion of both legal and illegal substances. Pursuant to a warrant, police seized cocaine kits and other items. The issue on appeal was whether Minn. Stat. §§ 152.093 and 152.01, subd. 18 were unconstitutionally vague on their face. The court concluded the trial court found vague only that portion of the definitional statute, which read, drug paraphernalia means all equipment which are used primarily in certain activities. Minn. Stat. § 152.01, subd. 18. According to the court, the trial court's holding imposed a more exact and precise standard than required by constitutional law. In the court's view, a person of ordinary intelligence would know what type of object was referred to in the statute, thus the statute provided the constitutionally required notice. Also, the court held that the statutes required the prosecution to prove the person charged knowingly or intentionally delivered drug paraphernalia, thus avoiding an improper prosecution due to the criminal intent of a retail purchaser.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision and remanded the cause to the trial court.

State v. Dyer

Court of Appeals of Minnesota


438 N.W.2d 716; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 476

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Hennepin County District Court, Hon. Thomas H. Carey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of unlawful possession and sale of various controlled substances.


OVERVIEW: An undercover officer made several purchases of narcotics from an individual who lived at a certain address. Subsequently, the individual was arrested. The officer received a search warrant for the apartment unit where drugs were purchased. The unit was in the basement of the building. The warrant authorized the officer to enter the lower unit of the building. Upon entering, the officers announced that they were conducting a narcotics search. Defendant was convicted of unlawful possession and sale of various controlled substances. On review, defendant argued that the search was invalid. The court affirmed. The court determined that the warrant was sufficiently particular to satisfy the requirements of state and federal constitutions; the no-knock provision did not render the warrant constitutionally infirm; there was probable cause to issue the warrant, and the warrant was not overbroad.

OVERVIEW: Defendant and three adolescents were cruising the streets in a car. During this time, two tire-slashing incidents occurred in the parking lot of a local establishment. Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed. The order that defendant pay defense costs was reversed and remanded for a hearing as required by precedent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. The part of the order requiring payment of defense costs was reversed and remanded for a hearing.

State v. Mercherson


No. C4-88-2075


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


438 N.W.2d 707; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 487



 April 19, 1989, Decided  
April 25, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Robert K. Levy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State and defendant sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which ruled that Hennepin, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 385.170 (1976) was unconstitutionally overbroad.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a search warrant, officers entered a building and searched an apartment that defendant occupied. Cocaine, drug paraphernalia, and cash were seized. Defendant was charged with violation of Hennepin, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 385.170 (1976). At trial, defendant moved to have the charge against him dropped or the evidence suppressed, because there was no probable cause to support the search warrant or, in the alternative, to dismiss the charge because § 385.170 was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague. The lower court denied the motion to suppress. The lower court dismissed the charge on the ground that § 385.170 was unconstitutionally overbroad; it prohibited all people from living in, working at, or visiting a building where illegal activity occurred, and no stated interest was served in making such a broad prohibition. The lower court ruled that § 385.170 was not vague because it was understandable to a person of common intelligence. On review, the court affirmed. The court ruled that § 385.170 was unconstitutional on its face, because it infringed on a substantial amount of constitutionally protected conduct, and allowed arbitrary enforcement of its provisions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that the applicable statute was unconstitutionally overbroad.
