Graupmann v. Rental Equipment & Sales Co.


No. C9-88-2377


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


438 N.W.2d 711; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 489



 April 18, 1989, Decided  
April 25, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Lajune T. Lange, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff victim and his wife sought review of an order from the District Court of Hennepin County (Minnesota), which, in an action for personal injuries against defendant rental company for injuries received when a truck rented from the rental company ran over the victim, granted summary judgment for the rental company and dismissed the complaint with prejudice on the grounds of res judicata. The rental company requested attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The first action filed by the victim and his wife was dismissed when no certificate of readiness or motion to continue was filed. Counsel for the victim and his wife filed a motion to vacate that dismissal. The district judge denied the motion and ordered that the judgment of dismissal be with prejudice. Another motion to vacate was filed and denied. The victim and his wife's appeal was dismissed by the court. They then filed another action against the rental company, which was dismissed. On review the court found no error in granting summary judgment. The court noted that under Minn. R. Civ. P. 41.02(1) (1988) the district court could, on its own motion, dismiss an action for failure to prosecute or to comply with the rules of civil procedure or any order of the court. Unless the district court in its order for dismissal specified otherwise, a dismissal under Rule 41.02 operated as an adjudication on the merits. A judgment on the merits constituted an absolute bar to a second action for the same cause of action and was conclusive between parties and privies. The court denied the request for appellate attorney fees on the grounds that bad faith was not shown.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's grant of summary judgment.

 

1349 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Aderman v. County of Washington


No. C2-88-2348


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 437



April 11, 1989, Decided  
April 18, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Aderman v. County of Washington, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 394 (Minn., June 21, 1989)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county employees, sought review of a decision of the District Court (Minnesota), which granted respondent county summary judgment, ruling that the county was authorized to eliminate promised medical insurance benefits after retirement.


OVERVIEW: Prior to January 1, 1985, the county personnel regulations provided its employees and their spouses with lifetime medical insurance coverage. On August 14, 1984, the county cut the benefit by imposing caps and by mandating that retirees take advantage of Medicare if they were eligible. In 1988, the legislature passed 1988 Minn. Laws ch. 605, §§ 7, 13, which validated contracts for post-retirement health insurance benefits that precluded commitments for permanent benefits. The county employees filed suit based on estoppel and constitutional property rights, challenging the county's termination of permanent health insurance benefits. The trial court granted the county summary judgment, ruling that the 1988 legislation was to be applied retroactively. The court reversed and remanded, holding that only 1988 Minn. Laws ch. 605, § 13 was expressly applied retroactively to August 1, 1986; otherwise, most sections in 1988 Minn. Laws ch. 605 became effective on April 25, 1988. Minnesota laws were presumed to have no retroactive effect unless clearly and manifestly intended by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the summary judgment grant to the county in the suit challenging the elimination of medical insurance benefits after retirement.

 

1350 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Minnesota State Patrol Troopers Ass'n on behalf of Pince v. State, Dep't of Public Safety


No. C1-88-2292


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


437 N.W.2d 670; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 356; 132 L.R.R.M. 2370; 132 L.R.R.M. 2371



March 28, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Minn. State Patrol Troopers Ass'n v. State, Dep't of Pub. Safety, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 403 (Minn., May 24, 1989)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Ramsey County District Court, Hon. Allan R. Markert, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Minnesota State Patrol Troopers Association sought review of an order from the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which entered confirmed an arbitration award entered in favor of respondents, state, Department of Public Safety, and related parties, in the Association's grievance on behalf of state trooper who had been discharged.


OVERVIEW: The state trooper was discharged based on numerous acts of harassment against his supervisor. The Association represented the state trooper in his appeal from the discharge and the parties submitted their case to arbitration. The arbitrator held that the discharge was for just cause and supported by all the evidence. On the Association's appeal from the arbitrator's decision, the district court denied its motion to vacate and confirmed the award. On further appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the search warrant obtained to search the state trooper's home lacked probable cause and the evidence offered at the arbitration hearing should have been suppressed. The court held, however, that absent the evidence that should have been suppressed, sufficient evidence remained to warrant the arbitrator's decision that the state trooper's discharge was based on just cause. The court further held that its power to vacate the arbitration award was strictly limited to the grounds listed in Minn. Stat. § 572.19(1) and because the record reflected no evidence of corruption, fraud, partiality or misconduct by the arbitrator his decision had to be affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order confirming the arbitrator's award in favor of respondents in the Association's suit challenging the state trooper's discharge.

 

1351 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Montano


No. C2-89-352


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


437 N.W.2d 772; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 389



 March 28, 1989, Decided  
April 4, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Ramsey County District Court, Hon. Edward S. Wilson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Petition for discretionary review denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought discretionary review of a decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which denied his challenge to the constitutionality of the Minnesota prostitution laws, which were found at Minn. Stat. §§ 609.321-.324 (1988).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the statutes were a substantially overbroad intrusion into freedom of expression. Defendant was a temporary resident who was charged with engaging in prostitution. Defendant claimed that he would be in danger of deportation if he were convicted of that crime, even if his direct appeal were still pending. The court denied the petition for discretionary review. The court noted that the Immigration and Naturalization Service could not consider a conviction, for purposes of deportation, until it was "final." According to the court, the determination of finality was not a matter of state law, but was a question of federal immigration law. The court further noted that under federal immigration law, a conviction was not considered final until all procedures for direct appeal had been exhausted. Thus, the court held that defendant had not shown a compelling reasons for granting pre-trial discretionary review. In addition, the court noted that it would declare a statute unconstitutional only when absolutely necessary, and then with extreme caution.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's petition for discretionary review.

 

1352 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


St. Paul Cos. v. Hatch


No. C5-88-2392


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


437 N.W.2d 666; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 340



 March 22, 1989, Decided  
March 28, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by St. Paul Cos. v. Hatch, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 380 (Minn., May 18, 1989)
Reversed by St. Paul Cos. v. Hatch, 449 N.W.2d 130, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 314 (Minn., 1989)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Ramsey County District Court, Hon. Gordon Shumaker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and appeal reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance company challenged a judgment from the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which granted the motion filed by respondent, an acquiring insurance company, to dismiss appellant's petition for review of an order of the Commissioner of the Department of Commerce on the ground that the statute providing for de novo review, Minn. Stat. § 60D.12, subd. 1 (1986), was unconstitutional and not severable.


OVERVIEW: Respondent applied to the Commissioner for approval to purchase 10 percent or more of the voting stock of appellant. After an administrative hearing, its application was approved with certain conditions. Appellant petitioned for review in the district court. The district court granted respondent's motion to dismiss on the ground that § 60D.12, subd. 1, which provided for de novo review, was unconstitutional and not severable. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that the principle functions of the Commissioner were protective, supervisory, and regulatory. These functions were the kind performed by the executive branch in the exercise of its police power. Delegating this function to the judiciary through de novo review of the Commissioner's decision violated the separation of powers clause of Minn. Const. art. III, § 1. The language of the statute providing for de novo review could not be severed because the remaining provisions, standing alone, would be incomplete and could not be applied in accordance with legislative intent. The court accepted jurisdiction over an appeal on the merits and reinstated a previously discharged writ of certiorari and notice of review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's determination the statute providing for de novo review was unconstitutional and not severable but accepted jurisdiction over an appeal on the merits and reinstated the appeal.

 

1353 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. My Mechanic, Inc.


No. C3-88-1550


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 295



March 15, 1989, Decided  
March 21, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an automobile repair shop, sought review of a judgment from the trial court (Minnesota), which found that defendant had violated Minnetonka, Minn., Zoning Ordinance § 300.30, subd. (1)(g)(21) (1985), a misdemeanor offense, by displaying a temporary sign without a permit.


OVERVIEW: The City notified defendant that its conduct in displaying around an intersection several moveable signs advertising its business violated city ordinances and that the signs had to be removed. Defendant requested a variance to display a temporary sign, but the request was denied. Defendant accumulated four citations for violating § 300.30, subd. (1)(g)(21). The trial court found that defendant's actions violated the ordinance. On appeal, the court affirmed. The ordinance was not void for vagueness. The ordinance required a permit to display a temporary sign, and the term "temporary sign" was defined in such a way that the ordinary person would consider defendant's signs to have been temporary. The ordinance did not violate defendant's right to freedom of speech. The commercial speech involved was lawful and not misleading, but the City demonstrated a governmental interest in limiting the use of temporary signs. Pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 462.357 (1984), the City could enact sign control ordinances under its general zoning powers, which included the power to promote aesthetic values. The ordinance reached no further than necessary to serve the governmental interest of aesthetics.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1354 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Rutledge v. Commissioner of Jobs & Training


No. C2-88-2236


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 298



March 13, 1989, Decided  
March 21, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged a judgment of the Department of Jobs and Training (Minnesota), finding that he was not eligible for unemployment compensation because he was pursuing a claim for temporary total and permanent partial disability workers' compensation benefits. The Department found that if he received both, he would collect more than his unemployment compensation entitlement.


OVERVIEW: The employee contended that the Department's finding violated his equal protection and due process guarantees because Minn. Stat. § 268.08, subd. 3(3) (1986) barred those seeking remuneration from an alternate source from unemployment compensation benefits if the amount received would exceed the unemployment compensation entitlement. The court rejected the employee's claim, holding that the plain language of the statute was to be given effect because the wisdom of the law or its adequacy to accomplish a desired purpose was for the legislature and not the courts to consider. Further, the court held that the legislative classification was not unconstitutional because it bore a reasonable relationship to the objective of the legislation: to protect the unemployment compensation fund from depletion of funds that could not be reimbursed. Finally the court rejected the employee's claim that § 268.08, subd. 3(3) interfered with his attorney-client privilege because the communication with his attorney relative to the workers' compensation claim was not privileged communication.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding of the Department.

 

1355 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


E.S.P., Inc. v. Midway Nat'l Bank


No. C5-88-1940


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


437 N.W.2d 71; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 275; 8 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. 2d (Callaghan) 112



 March 6, 1989, Decided  
March 14, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by E.S.P., Inc. v. Midway Nat'l Bank of St. Paul, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 647 (Minn., Apr. 24, 1989)
Vacated by, Remanded by E.S.P., Inc. v. Midway Nat'l Bank, 447 N.W.2d 882, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 288 (Minn., 1989)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Ramsey County District Court, Otis H. Godfrey, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) granting summary judgment for respondents on the basis that appellant's breach of warranty claim under Minn. Stat. § 336.4-207 (1986) was barred by the statute of limitations found in Minn. Stat. § 541.05 (1986).


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that its action was an action for indemnity seeking payment for all sums for which appellant might be found liable and that such a claim did not accrue for statute of limitations purposes until the party seeking indemnification had been damaged by paying more than its fair share of the obligation. Appellant claimed that since it had not yet paid more than its fair share of any obligation, its action was not barred by Minn. Stat. § 541.05. The court held that appellant's cause of action arose as a breach of warranty under the Uniform Commercial Code and was in the nature of an implied contract action. Accordingly, since appellant paid the check on February 6, 1981, under Minn. Stat. § 541.05, it had until February 6, 1987 to bring suit against respondent. It failed to do so, and accordingly, its action against respondent was barred.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting summary in favor of respondents on the basis that appellant's breach of warranty claim was barred by the statute of limitations was affirmed because appellant failed to bring its cause of action within the six-year statute of limitations period.

 

1356 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Shenkman v. Duluth


No. C8-88-1320


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 239



March 1, 1989, Decided  
March 7, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developer sought review of a decision of the District Court (Minnesota), which entered judgment in favor of respondent city in a suit alleging that the city's act of rezoning a property was arbitrary, capricious, and unreasonable, and the action amounted to an unconstitutional taking without due process of law.


OVERVIEW: Over the course of a decade the developer purchased several parcels of undeveloped land and formed a contiguous 79-acre tract of land that was near a highway. The developer intended to build a large shopping complex, which at that time was the highest and best use of the property. The city council imposed a building moratorium ordinance that affected the developer's land. Later an ordinance was passed that rezoned the majority of the developer's land from commercial to suburban. The developer filed suit alleging that the city's act of rezoning the property was arbitrary, capricious, and unreasonable, and the action amounted to an unconstitutional taking without due process of law. The court entered judgment in favor of the city. The court affirmed, holding that the value of the property was identical before and after enactment of the city's ordinance. A valid rezoning did not give rise to an action for damages simply because the land in question could be more valuable for some other purpose. There was no taking unless all reasonable uses of the property had been proscribed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the city in the action alleging an unconstitutional taking due to the city's rezoning of land.

 

1357 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Hay v. Andover


No. C7-88-1213


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


436 N.W.2d 800; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 246



 February 27, 1989, Decided  
March 7, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Anoka County District Court, Hon. Esther M. Tomljanovich, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owners sought review of a judgment of the Anoka County District Court (Minnesota), which denied their claims against respondent city for taking, violation of due process, violation of equal protection, and violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed the trial court's judgment on the issue of laches. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects. The court ruled that the owners' claim of a property interest in a special use permit was not private property and not subject to the constitutional provision of taking. The property interest in the special use permit was a government entitlement or benefit. The court ruled that any taking claim for the underlying real estate was not ripe for adjudication. The owners had not attempted to obtain a variance which would have allowed them to use their property in some manner other than a mobile home park. The court ruled that the city had a rational basis for denying sewer access at the time of the application. Thus, there was no violation of due process or equal protection or 42 U.S.C. § 1983. On the issue of laches, the court ruled that the owners' delay in bringing the action did not bar their claim. It would have been premature for them to petition the city because any attempt would have been futile, and because circumstances had changed. The owners' property was within close range of the city sewer line.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment as to the issue of laches. The owners' claims were not barred by laches. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

 

1358 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Ackerman v. American Family Mut. Ins. Co.


No. C4-88-1802


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


435 N.W.2d 835; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 171



 February 14, 1989, Decided  
February 21, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Hennepin County District Court, Hon. Steven Z. Lange, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a trustee for heirs of a deceased employee, appealed the judgment by the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) in favor of defendants, a co-employee and an insurer, which declared the co-employee was not grossly negligent in plaintiff's claim for underinsured motorist benefits against the insurer based on the wrongful death claim against the co-employee. Plaintiff alleged Minn. Stat. § 176.061, subd. 5(c) (1986) did not apply.


OVERVIEW: The deceased was killed when the co-employee struck him at work. There was no allegation of intentional injury. Plaintiff contended that the co-employee was grossly negligent in causing the deceased's death and that her damages exceeded the liability limits of the co-employee's auto insurance policy. The insurer contended that the co-employee was not grossly negligent. On appeal, the court held under § 176.061, subd. (5)(c) a co-employee working for the same employer was not liable for a personal injury incurred by another employee unless the injury resulted from gross negligence or was intentionally inflicted by the co-employee. The court rejected plaintiff's argument that the deceased's death did not arise out of and in the course of his employment and that simple negligence was insufficient to sustain the action against the insurer. The court held that because the right for plaintiff to recover was grounded in the wrongful death statute, Minn. Stat. § 573.02 (1986), and that right would not be protected by Minn. Const. art. I, § 8. Thus the court concluded that plaintiff failed to meet her burden in challenging the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 176.061(5)(c) (1986).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1359 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Zachman v. Kunin


No. C8-88-1608


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 75



January 24, 1989, Decided  
January 31, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Zachman v. Kunin, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 623 (Minn., Mar. 29, 1989)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee, a housekeeper, sought review of a judgment of a trial court (Minnesota), which granted respondent employers' motion for summary judgment regarding the employee's action under Minn. Stat. § 347.22 (1986) for injuries sustained when she was attacked by the employees' dog. The trial court concluded that the employee's exclusive remedy was under the Workers' Compensation Act, according to Minn. Stat. § 176.031 (1988).


OVERVIEW: The employee brought her action under Minn. Stat. § 347.22 (1986), which imposed absolute liability on a dog owner for an unprovoked attack by the dog. The employers' dog bit her when she came to work at their house. On appeal from the adverse summary judgment, the employee urged the court to adopt the "dual persona" exception to the rule that her exclusive remedy was under the Workers' Compensation Act. Affirming the judgment, the court held that the employers' identity as owners of a dog was not so completely independent from and unrelated to their status as in-home employers that the court had to recognize the persona as separate for purposes of applying workers' compensation laws. The employee's remedy for the work-related injury was through the workers' compensation insurance provided by the employers'. The court also rejected the employee's contention that the Act, as applied, violated Minn. Const. art. I, § 8 because it barred a tort action for permanent disfigurement without providing an adequate substitute remedy. And because the exclusive remedy provision applied equally to employees covered by the Act, it also not violate the guarantees of equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting summary judgment for the employers.

 

1360 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


United Steelworkers of America, Local 6115 v. Quadna Mountain Corp.


No. C5-88-1405


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


435 N.W.2d 120; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 98



 January 24, 1989, Decided  
January 31, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by United Steelworkers of Am., Local 6115 v. Quadna Mt. Corp., 1989 Minn. LEXIS 661 (Minn., Mar. 29, 1989)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Aitkin District Court, Hon. John A. Spellacy, Judge.
United Steelworkers of America, Local 6115 v. Quadna Mountain Corp., 418 N.W.2d 723, 1988 Minn. LEXIS 21 (Minn., 1988)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of a judgment from the Aitkin District Court (Minnesota), which granted the motion for summary judgment filed by respondents, tortfeasors, their primary insurer, and their excess insurer, in the employer's workers' compensation subrogation suit.


OVERVIEW: An employee was injured and he filed suit against the third-party tortfeasors and their primary insurer. In settling that suit, the employee agreed to indemnify them. The employer then filed a workers' compensation subrogation suit against the same parties and entered into a settlement with them, with the employer agreeing to indemnify all of the settling parties and the injured employee. The employer then brought the tortfeasors' excess insurer into its suit. The trial court granted respondents' motion for summary judgment based upon circular indemnity. Upon review the court affirmed the summary judgment, holding that the employer's subrogation interest was not jeopardized by the employee's indemnification agreement. The court held that the suit against the excess insurer was dismissed because the employer entered into a settlement agreement which created circular indemnity. The court held that the excess insurer was not foreclosed from asserting the indemnity agreement because it did not authorize, nor was it a party to the employer's settlement with the tortfeasors and their primary insurer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment which had been granted in favor of respondents in the employer's workers' compensation subrogation suit.

 

1361 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Kuehn v. American Federation of State, etc., Council No. 65


No. C2-88-1779


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


435 N.W.2d 130; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 93



 January 23, 1989, Decided  
January 31, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Kuehn v. Am. Fedn. of State, County & Mun. Emples., 1989 Minn. LEXIS 697 (Minn., Apr. 18, 1989)
Writ of certiorari denied Kuehn v. Council No. 65, American Federation of State, etc., 493 U.S. 849, 110 S. Ct. 145, 107 L. Ed. 2d 104, 1989 U.S. LEXIS 4354 (1989)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Public Employment Relations Board.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator, an employee who was not a union member, appealed a determination of the Public Employment Relations Board (Minnesota) (PERB), which upheld the decision of the Bureau of Mediation Services (BMS) that the "fair share fees" taken from the employee's paycheck pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 179A.06, subd. 3, for respondent union's services were proper.


OVERVIEW: The employee was notified that he was subject to the fees. He requested a detailed breakdown of the union's expenditures that were the basis for the fees. The employee filed a challenge to the assessment with the BMS. BMS found that the union's initial notice was inadequate but that the corrective measures from Minn. R. 5510.140 cured the defect and that the employee was subject to the fees. On appeal, the employee asserted that the fees violated his association rights under the First and Fourteenth Amendments because he was not aware of the basis for the fee prior to paying it. The court held that recent amendments provided for constitutionally adequate notice. The union had properly carried its burden of proving that the fees imposed under Minn. Stat. § 179A.06, subd. 3 were reasonable and the burden had not been impermissibly shifted to the employee. Section 179A.06, subd. 3 was constitutional. The calculation of the employee's fees was made in accordance with § 179A.06. The court affirmed that the employee received a prompt hearing and decision. The evidence supported the conclusion of BMS that the fees could be used by the union to pay other organizations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the PERB order that upheld the BMS decision that the fees imposed on the employee were proper. The court held that the statute that provided for the fair share fees was constitutional.

 

1362 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Anderson v. State


No. C3-88-1421


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


435 N.W.2d 74; 1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 52



 January 17, 1989, Decided  
January 24, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeals from Stevens County District Court, Hon. Keith C. Davison, Judge. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sellers of farm real estate sought review of the decision of the Stevens County District Court (Minnesota), which granted judgment for respondents, the State and the Commissioner of the Department of Agriculture, and held that repeal of the tax exclusion for seller-sponsored loans under the Family Farm Security Act was not an unconstitutional impairment of a contractual obligation and promissory estoppel did not apply.


OVERVIEW: The sellers participated in seller-sponsored loans. At the time that the loans were made, the sellers qualified under the Act for a state guarantee of the outstanding balance of each of the loans in the event of buyer default. The State, as guarantor, was a third-party to the underlying contract for deed between each buyer and seller. At the time the loans were made, Minn. Stat. § 41.58, subd. 3, provided for an exclusion from gross income of sellers of the interest on seller-sponsored loans under the family farm security program. The exclusion was repealed, and the sellers challenged the repeal. The court affirmed the trial court's decision determining that repeal of the tax exclusion was not an unconstitutional impairment of a contractual obligation, and that the doctrine of promissory estoppel did not apply to the parties' transactions. The court held that increasing taxation or adding a new tax did not impair the obligation of a contract. Although the exemption was part of the contract, so was the law with reference to the state's power of taxation, and the risk of an additional tax was one of the usual hazards of business enterprise.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

 

1363 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Application of Minnesota Dep't of Transp.


No. C5-88-1470


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1989 Minn. App. LEXIS 18



January 3, 1989, Decided  
January 10, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Minn. DOT, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 738 (Minn., Mar. 17, 1989)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landowner sought review of the decisions of respondent pollution board that denied him a contested hearing and that granted respondent department of transportation a variance from the State noise pollution standards.


OVERVIEW: The department of transportation planned to widen a road that fronted the landowner's property. studies were commissioned to investigate the effects of the widening upon state noise pollution control standards. Several options were derived and the department chose the option that complied with the standards except for the morning rush hour time. The landowner requested a contested hearing with the pollution board which denied the request and granted the department's request for a variance from the standards to accommodate the morning rush hour. The court held that because the department and the pollution board agreed that other alternatives would have more fully complied with the noise standards, there was no material issue of fact to justify a contested hearing under Minn. R. 7001.0130, subpt. 1 (1987). In affirming the decision the court held that because the landowner was one of 382 that were affected by the noise variance he did not demonstrate a substantial invasion of his property rights to compel condemnation proceedings under Minn. Const. art. I, § 13.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of a contested hearing and affirmed the variance.

 

1364 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. Itasca County


No. C2-88-1720


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 1297



December 29, 1988, Decided  
January 10, 1989, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Martin v. Itasca County, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 769 (Minn., Mar. 17, 1989)
Reversed by, Remanded by Martin v. Itasca County, 448 N.W.2d 368, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 295 (Minn., 1989)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a county employee, filed suit against respondent county, alleging a denial of due process when the county adopted a policy requiring the employee to take an unpaid leave of absence to run for a county office. The trial court (Minnesota) granted summary judgment to the county. The employee appealed, and the county sought review of other issues.


OVERVIEW: The employee, who was the county's civil defense director, announced his candidacy for county commissioner. Subsequently, the Board of Commissioners adopted a policy requiring all county employees seeking federal, state, or county office to take an unpaid leave of absence during the campaign. After a similar policy was held unconstitutional in another case, the employee filed suit. Reversing the grant of summary judgment, the court held that the other case was indistinguishable and that the county's announcement of its new policy denied the employee due process of law. The court held that recourse to the county's grievance policy would have been futile, and that a two-year statute of limitations did not apply. Finally, the defense of qualified immunity did not apply because the employee's claim was a contract claim against the county, not against the commissioners as individuals.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment to the county and held that the county's policy deprived the employee of wages and benefits without due process.

 

1365 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Watson


No. CX-88-573


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


433 N.W.2d 110; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 1222



 December 6, 1988, Decided  
December 13, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Watson, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 348 (Minn., Feb. 10, 1989)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, McLeod County; Hon. John M. Fitzgerald, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions in the District Court, McLeod County (Minnesota), for two counts of theft, one count of diversion of charitable gambling funds, and one count of conspiracy.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the Minnesota Charitable Gambling statute, specifically Minn. Stat. §§ 349.15, 349.12, subd. 11 (1986), was unconstitutionally vague, that the evidence presented at trial was insufficient, and that the trial court committed prejudicial evidentiary errors that warranted a new trial. The court affirmed, holding that: (1) the gambling statute was not unconstitutionally vague and was sufficiently specific and understandable so that defendant should have known that his conduct was illegal; (2) the evidence was sufficient to support the verdict because there was sufficient circumstantial evidence for the jury to infer that defendant was using gambling proceeds for other than lawful purposes and also to prove that his organization did not manage the gambling operation according to the statute and that he was able to circumvent the law and use charitable gambling proceeds for his own purposes; (3) it could not be a lawful purpose under § 349.15 if a gambling operation was managed by an ineligible organization; and (4) the trial court rulings were not so prejudicial, nor did they so materially affect defendant's substantial rights, as to warrant a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

1366 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ellis


No. C8-88-670


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 1183



November 28, 1988, Decided  
December 6, 1988, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of a Minnesota trial court, which convicted him of possession of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: An informant gave police a tip about a drug dealer. The police followed up on the tip and observed defendant in what was believed to be the beginning of a drug transaction. Defendant and his vehicle were searched, and cocaine was found in defendant's vehicle. Defendant was arrested and subsequently found guilty of possession of cocaine. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The police officer's corroboration of much of the informant's information, as well as the on-the-scene assessment by the police officer, provided probable cause to arrest defendant. Defendant's contention that the informant was connected to the underworld and was, therefore, unreliable, was without foundation. The record as a whole supported the conclusion that the police had reasonable grounds to believe that defendant's vehicle contained drugs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1367 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hyland


No. C1-88-767


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


431 N.W.2d 868; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 1141



 November 15, 1988, Decided  
November 22, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. Allan R. Markert, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which convicted him of illegally parking commercial vehicles on a residential street in violation of St. Paul, Minn., Legislative Code § 157.04(13)b.


OVERVIEW: Within a month of the effective date of § 157.04(13)b, defendant was ticketed for violating it. He received seven citations, and after his motion for dismissal based on discriminatory enforcement was denied without a hearing he was convicted on a stipulation. In affirming the conviction the court held that the ordinance did not violate the due process or equal protection clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court held that the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague because any indefiniteness in the ordinance as to whether it applied to the registered owner of the vehicle or the person who parked it did not affect defendant, who was both the owner and person who parked the vehicle. The court also held that the parking ordinance was a reasonable exercise of a city's police powers. The court then held that the trial court correctly ruled that defendant failed to prove discriminatory enforcement of the ordinance in violation of equal protection. Furthermore the court held that defendant had not made a threshold showing of discriminatory enforcement so the trial court correctly disposed of this issue without a hearing and refused to receive evidence bearing on it at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of illegally parking commercial vehicles on a residential street.

 

1368 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Moore


No. C3-88-1015


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


431 N.W.2d 565; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 1102



 November 8, 1988, Decided  
November 15, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Steven Lange, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Minnesota sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Hennepin County (Minnesota), which granted defendant's motion to have Minn. Stat. § 152.15, subd. 1(1)(i) (Supp. 1987) declared void for vagueness because the statute used the undefined term "cocaine base."


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with possessing with an intent to distribute a controlled substance containing three or more grams of cocaine base in violation of Minn. Stat. § 152.15, subd. 1(1)(i) (Supp. 1987). Defendant brought a motion, pursuant to Minn. R. Crim. P. 17.06, subd. 2(2)(c), to have § 152.15, subd. 1(1)(i) declared unconstitutional. The trial court granted defendant's motion because the statute used the undefined term "cocaine base." The State challenged the trial court's judgment on appeal. The trial court's judgment was reversed. The court found that the term "cocaine base" was not so vague as to render § 152.15, subd. 1(1)(i) constitutionally infirm. The court found that a person of average intelligence would understand that "cocaine base," the possession and sale of which evokes a greater criminal penalty than the possession and sale of the same quantity of other forms of cocaine, means pure cocaine in its undiluted chemical form. Accordingly, the court found that the statute defined the offense for which the criminal penalty attached with sufficient definiteness that ordinary people could understand what conduct was prohibited.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed.

 

1369 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Oswalt v. County of Ramsey


No. C3-88-866


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 1111



November 8, 1988, Decided  
November 15, 1988, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Oswalt v. County of Ramsey, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 503 (Minn., Jan. 13, 1989)


PRIOR HISTORY: Oswalt v. County of Ramsey, 371 N.W.2d 241, 1985 Minn. App. LEXIS 4396 (Minn. Ct. App., 1985)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of a judgment of the trial court (Minnesota), which awarded him compensation from respondent city for the taking of his property by subtracting damages he had already received from the county and the unpaid balance of a mortgage from the value of the property at the time of the taking. The trial court also calculated and awarded the property owner interest and attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: A city project altered the water flow of a ditch running adjacent to the owner's property and caused severe structural damage to his house. When the city refused to purchase the house, the owner defaulted on his mortgage payments, and the mortgage was foreclosed. The owner sued the city and the county. The trial court rendered judgment in favor of the owner against the county but held that there was no unconstitutional taking by the city. On appeal as to the issue of an unconstitutional taking, the appellate court reversed and remanded. The trial court determined the value of the property at the time of the taking and awarded the owner that amount less the amount the owner had already received from the county and the unpaid balance of the mortgage. On appeal, the owner challenged the trial court's decision to offset the fair market value of the property by the unpaid portion of the mortgage. The court affirmed. The court noted that the purpose of compensation was to place the owner in the same position as he would have been if the property had not been taken. The court held that since the owner never paid the balance of the mortgage, he was not entitled to compensation for it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Weisman


No. C0-88-811


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 1070



October 25, 1988, Decided  
November 1, 1988, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Weisman, 1988 Minn. LEXIS 791 (Minn., Dec. 16, 1988)
Writ of certiorari denied Weisman v. Minnesota, 489 U.S. 1080, 109 S. Ct. 1533, 103 L. Ed. 2d 838, 1989 U.S. LEXIS 1397 (1989)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from a trial court (Minnesota), which convicted him of driving with no driver's license, failure to display license plates, and speeding on a bridge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's car was pulled over for speeding. He refused to produce a driver's license or identification, so he was arrested and ultimately convicted of driving with no driver's license, failure to display license plates, and speeding on a bridge. On appeal, defendant challenged the constitutionality of the statutes under which he was convicted, but the court upheld the constitutionality of the statutes. The court rejected defendant's claim that the driver's license statute, Minn. Stat. § 171.02 (1986), infringed on his right to travel. The court further held that the state, in the public interest, had the right to require drivers to obtain a license for the privilege of operating a vehicle on the roads. The court also rejected defendant's challenge to the registration statute, Minn. Stat. § 169.79 (1986). The court held that the statute was a proper measure under which the state could regulate and supervise vehicles, their movement and control, and establish their identity in relation to the public and to any resultant damage or injury they may occasion. Finally, the court rejected defendant's vagueness challenge to Minn. Stat. § 169.01 (1986), the speeding statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

1371 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State, Dep't of Public Safety v. Elk River Ready Mix Co.


No. C5-88-1162


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


430 N.W.2d 261; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 1000



 October 7, 1988, Decided  
October 18, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Sherburne County, Hon. Robert B. Danforth, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant concrete company sought review of a judgment from District Court, Sherburne County (Minnesota), which upheld a fine imposed on the company for operating an overweight vehicle and held that Minn. Stat. §§ 169.825 and 169.871 (1986) were constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Minn. Stat. § 169.825 (1986) provided for criminal sanctions for the operation of overweight vehicles. Minn. Stat. § 169.871 (1986) provided for civil sanctions for the same transgression, and provided for the issuance of notice of an overweight report and possible penalty. The company pleaded guilty to operating an overweight vehicle. In the civil proceedings the company challenged the constitutionality of both statutes. In affirming the judgment the court rejected due process and vagueness challenges to Minn. Stat. § 169.871 (1986). The court first observed that the notice of the possibility of civil sanctions was adequate, and held moreover that due process did not require any notice at all, because there was no potential deprivation of a liberty or property interest under § 169.871. The court also held that the notice that the vehicle's "driver or another" might be civilly liable was not vague, at least as applied to the company, which had actual notice it was a target. The court also held that Minn. Stat. § 169.825 (1986), though complicated, was not vague in relation to the computation of permissible maximum gross vehicle weights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against the company.

 

1372 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Ford v. Emerson Electric Co.


No. C2-88-1118


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


430 N.W.2d 198; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 957; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P11,995



 October 4, 1988, Decided  
October 11, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Ford v. Emerson Elec. Co., 1988 Minn. LEXIS 795 (Minn., Dec. 16, 1988)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Pine County District Court, Hon. James F. Dehn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wrongful death claimant challenged the decision of the Pine County District Court (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment, on limitations grounds, to respondent water heater manufacturers, in the claimant's action that followed the deaths of her family members in a house fire.


OVERVIEW: The claimant's husband and children were killed in a house fire, which originated at the water heater in the family's home. The water heater and its components were made by the manufacturers. The claimant brought a wrongful death action against the manufacturers. The trial court granted summary judgment to the manufacturer because it found that the claimant's action was barred by the two-year statute of limitations for injuries arising from defects in improvements to real property, Minn. Stat. § 541.051. On appeal, the claimant argued that the three-year statute of limitations for wrongful death actions, Minn. Stat. § 573.02, applied. The court disagreed and affirmed. The court first held that the express language of § 541.051 and § 573.02 indicated an irreconcilable conflict between the statutes when a wrongful death action arose out of an improvement to real property. Thus, under a rule of construction, the more particular provision, which was § 541.051, the two-year provision, controlled over the general provision, which was § 573.02, the three-year provision. Because the death of the family members occurred more than two years before the action was brought, it was time-barred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the manufacturer.

State v. Sorenson


No. C9-88-225


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


430 N.W.2d 231; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 963



 October 4, 1988, Decided  
October 11, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Sorenson, 1988 Minn. LEXIS 692 (Minn., Dec. 1, 1988)
Affirmed by State v. Sorenson, 441 N.W.2d 455, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 139 (Minn., 1989)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Kittson County District Court, Hon. Donald E. Shanahan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Kittson County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of transporting a loaded, uncased firearm in a motor vehicle, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 97B.045(1) (1986).


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that Minn. Stat. § 97A.205(2) (Supp. 1987) authorized a conservation officer to enter defendant's private property without first establishing probable cause to believe that a violation of Minnesota's game laws had occurred. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that in order for defendant to have established that the conservation officer's presence on his property was an unreasonable search and was constitutionally prohibited, defendant had to first establish that he had a "constitutionally protected reasonable expectation of privacy" in the area searched. The court noted that the activities that were engaged in by the conservation officer while on defendant's property took place entirely in open fields. Consequently, according to the court, defendant's fourth amendment rights were not violated, because the special protections afforded by the fourth amendment did not extend to open fields. Further, the court held that defendant's arrest, which occurred a few hundred yards away from his cabin, was not within the cabin's curtilage.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which convicted defendant of transporting a loaded, uncased firearm in a motor vehicle.

Popp v. County of Winona


No. C2-88-695


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


430 N.W.2d 19; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 938



 September 27, 1988, Decided  
October 4, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Winona County; Hon. Lawrence T. Collins, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of a judgment from the District court, Winona County (Minnesota), which quashed an alternative writ of mandamus against respondent county that required the county to commence condemnation proceedings for the taking of the property owners' property in connection with the widening of a road, or in the alternative, show cause why the county had not done so.


OVERVIEW: The property owners' land fronted on a county road. The legal description on the property owners' warranty deed made reference an auditor's plat, which showed that the road was 66 feet wide. The plat did not state that the road had been dedicated. The county widened the road. The property owners claimed that the widening project resulted in the improper taking of their land, and filed an action for a writ of mandamus against the county. The trial court issued an alternative writ of mandamus directing the county to initiate condemnation proceedings or to show cause why it had not done so. The county chose to show cause at a hearing. The trial court ruled that the property owners were estopped from raising a condemnation claim because the deed made specific reference to the plat. The property owners claimed on appeal that the trial court did not follow the proper procedure and that it erred in quashing the alternative writ of mandamus. The court ruled that it was proper for the trial court to allow the county to show cause why it had not commenced condemnation proceedings, but that the property owners' deed established the county's claim to the land for road purposes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order quashing the writ of mandamus entered against the county in an action by the property owners to commence condemnation proceedings for the taking of the property owners' land or to show cause why the county had not commenced condemnation proceedings.

State v. Larson


No. C2-87-2503


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


429 N.W.2d 674; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 909



 September 19, 1988, Decided  
September 27, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Larson, 1988 Minn. LEXIS 759 (Minn., Nov. 8, 1988)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Ramsey County District Court, Hon. Joseph E. Salland, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment entered in the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), convicting her of driving while intoxicated (DWI) in violation of Minn. Stat. §169.121.


OVERVIEW: A deputy sheriff discovered defendant's vehicle sitting 75 feet off the road near a road sign that had been knocked down. After administering field sobriety tests, the deputy took defendant to the police station for a breath alcohol examination. The Intoxilyzer test yielded a .14 blood alcohol concentration. Defendant was charged with DWI. Between the time the officer found defendant and administration of the Intoxilyzer test, 77 minutes elapsed. At trial, defendant's counsel sought a judgment of acquittal, arguing that there was no evidence presented as to the driving time. The jury found defendant not guilty under one portion of the statute but guilty under Minn. Stat. §169.121(1)(d). On appeal, defendant asserted that expert testimony was needed to show her blood alcohol concentration at the time of operation/control because the presumption that the test would be deemed accurate at the time of violation had been removed from the statute. The court held that the jury was in the best position to assess intoxication in conjunction with the lag time between the test and operation of the car.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment.

 

1376 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Halvorson


No. C6-87-2164


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 1010



September 8, 1988, Decided  
September 20, 1988, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] This opinion will be unpublished and may not be cited except as provided by Minn. Stat. § 480A.08, subd. 3 As Amended.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Halvorson, 1988 Minn. LEXIS 642 (Minn., Nov. 23, 1988)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the trial court (Minnesota), which, following a stipulation of the facts, found him guilty of a theft offense under the mechanics lien statutes for failing to apply payments by the owners toward paying off the subcontractors in violation of Minn. Stat. § 514.02, subd. 1 (1986).


OVERVIEW: Defendant accepted payments on a remodeling contract from the owners, deposited the funds into his own account, and used the money to pay subcontractors on other jobs. He claimed that the statute was unconstitutional and that it was the corporation rather than him personally who was criminally liable because the owners' payment checks were made payable to the corporation and the statutory offense was a strict liability offense. On appeal, the court disagreed. The possibility of corporate criminal liability did not affect a corporate officer or employee's criminal liability for his own acts. The Minnesota Supreme Court had previously ruled that Minn. Stat. § 514.02, subd. 1, did not unconstitutionally authorize imprisonment for debt. The mechanics' lien statutes changed the legal relationship of contractors and landowners from a mere contract relationship to a fiduciary one. Given the fiduciary duty and the statutory requirement that the contractor know labor and material costs remained unpaid when he misapplied the proceeds, § 514.02, subd. 1, did not require intent to defraud to avoid the constitutional proscription against imprisonment for nonpayment of debt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for theft.

 

1377 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hennum


No. C5-87-1524


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


428 N.W.2d 859; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 876



 September 1, 1988, Decided  
September 13, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Granted.
Review granted by State v. Hennum, 1988 Minn. LEXIS 497 (Minn., Nov. 23, 1988)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, En banc State v. Hennum, 441 N.W.2d 793, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 153 (Minn., 1989)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wabasha County District Court, Hon. Lawrence T. Collins, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After issuing an order compelling an adverse mental examination of defendant by the State, the Wabasha County District Court (Minnesota) entered a judgment that convicted defendant of second-degree felony murder in accordance with the jury's verdict.


OVERVIEW: After her husband allegedly beat her, defendant shot and killed him as he slept. Defendant challenged her ensuing conviction for second-degree felony murder. The court reversed and remanded for a new trial, holding that the trial court's erroneous order of an adverse psychological examination was not harmless beyond a reasonable doubt because it infected much of the trial. Defendant was ordered to undergo a mental examination as a condition of allowing her expert to testify regarding battered women's syndrome. This was error because self-defense was not mentioned in Minn. R. Crim. P. 20.02 as a situation where the state may compel a defendant to undergo an adverse mental examination. Moreover, such an examination was allowable only after a defendant notified the prosecuting attorney of an intention to assert a defense of mental illness or deficiency. Here, defendant gave no such notice. Rather, defendant's only possible theory of defense was self-defense because she essentially admitted to the acts constituting felony murder. Because there was to be a new trial, defendant's other contentions regarding trial court error were moot.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded defendant's conviction for second-degree felony murder because errors accumulated as a result of the trial court's erroneous order compelling an adverse mental examination of defendant by the state.

 

1378 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Favre


No. C2-88-745


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


428 N.W.2d 828; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 867



 August 30, 1988, Decided  
September 6, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Hennepin County District Court, Hon. Pamela G. Alexander, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with driving under the influence of alcohol, driving with an alcohol concentration of .10 or more, and possession of drug paraphernalia. Over the State's objection, the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) accepted defendant's plea of guilty to reckless driving, Minn. Stat. § 169.13, subd. 1. The State appealed, and also challenged the trial court's refusal to consider its motion to amend the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The State had refused to plea-bargain because defendant had an alcohol concentration of .15, the two minors in his car had been drinking, and his record indicated at least one prior alcohol related offense. At a hearing, the trial court refused to consider the State's motion to add an additional charge, Minn. Stat. § 169.121 subd. 1(e), driving with an alcohol concentration of .10 or more, as measured within two hours of the driving. Defendant moved pursuant to Minn. R. Crim. P. 15.07 to be permitted to enter a plea of guilty to reckless driving. On appeal, the court held that a finding of manifest injustice was an abuse of discretion. The State's articulated reasons for refusing to plea bargain were not arbitrary or invidious, but in conformity with the deterrent purpose of the statute. The court also found the proposed amendment was not prejudicial. The only difference in the added offense would be the time of measurement of alcohol concentration, and defendant did not allege that the amendment would prejudice his defense. Finally, the trial court declined to hear argument on prejudice, the standard set forth in Minn. R. Crim. P. 17.05, which was an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the case for reconsideration of the State's motion.

State v. Peterson


No. C6-88-361


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 852



August 24, 1988, Decided  
August 30, 1988, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court (Minnesota) found appellant driver guilty of driving after suspension and ordered him to pay a fine. The driver moved for amended findings, but the trial court denied the motion. The driver appealed.


OVERVIEW: After paying a reinstatement fee, the driver's privileges were reinstated on April 3. The Department of Public Safety mailed the license to the driver's last known address. On the weekend of April 4 and 5, the driver moved but did not file a change of address form. The driver telephoned the Department to inquire about the whereabouts of his reinstated license and to inform them about his change of address. The Department mailed another notice of suspension to the driver's old address stating that his license and driving privileges would be suspended again, effective April 13. On April 8, the driver went to the service center, filed a change of address form, was given a temporary driver's license effective for 20 days, but was not advised that his license had been suspended again. The driver was stopped one week later and was cited for speeding and driving after suspension. The court held that it would have been unjust to hold the driver accountable for the Department's failure to check his driving record before issuing a new license or to penalize him for its administrative delay in processing his change of address. The driver did not violate Minn. Stat. § 171.24 (1986).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment.

The trial court granted the motion and the adoptive parents sought review. Good Neighbor Care Centers, Inc. v. Minnesota Dep't of Human Services


No. C5-88-612


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


428 N.W.2d 397; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 777



 August 4, 1988, Decided  
August 16, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied.
Review denied by Good Neighbor Care Ctrs., Inc. v. Minn. Dep't of Human Servs., 1988 Minn. LEXIS 719 (Minn., Oct. 19, 1988)


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to Department of Human Services.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Minnesota Department of Human Services (DHS) imposed a 20 percent reduction of medical assistance payments on relator nursing homes. The nursing homes sought review of DHS's decision.


OVERVIEW: The Minnesota Equalization Law, Minn. Stat. § 256B.48(1) (1986), required nursing homes to charge private paying residents the same rates paid for the residents receiving medical assistance. While the nursing homes were appealing the established medical assistance rates, they began charging their paying residents anticipated post-appeal rates. As a result, DHS imposed a 20 percent reduction of medical assistance payments on the nursing homes. The court held that the nursing homes' practice of charging private paying residents anticipated post-appeal rates violated the Equalization Law. Further, DHS's interpretation of the Equalization Law to preclude expedited hearings of underlying rates appeals upon service of a Notice of Agency Action was not an invalid, unpromulgated rule. Moreover, the imposition of rate reductions during the pending of an appeal did not violate procedural due process. Finally, the interpretation of the statute to preclude charging anticipated post-appeal rates did not constitute an unconstitutional taking because the nursing homes were only "legally entitled' to charge approved rates. Accordingly, the decision of DHS was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The decision of DHS, to impose a reduction of medical assistance payments on nursing homes, was affirmed.

 

1382 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Zak


No. C2-87-2436


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 669



July 18, 1988, Decided  
July 26, 1988, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the District Court (Minnesota), which upheld a jury verdict that found defendant guilty of second degree assault and reckless driving.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was in his vehicle when he observed his estranged wife's boyfriend driving a pickup truck with defendant's two boys in the truck. Defendant then commenced chasing the truck in an attempt to see his sons. Defendant rammed the back of the pickup truck, pushing the truck through some intersections. Defendant overtook the pickup truck and exited his vehicle. The wife's boyfriend was able to escape by pulling around the car in front of defendant and then driving to a law enforcement center. Defendant was charged with second degree assault and reckless driving. At the trial, the wife's boyfriend testified that the children were scared and crying. The jury convicted defendant as charged. The court affirmed, holding that assaultive intent could generally be inferred from a defendant's conduct. Defendant's reckless actions supported a finding of assaultive intent. The prosecution was authorized to ask the jury to put themselves in defendant's shoes, although arguments inviting jurors to place themselves in the shoes of the victim were improper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for second degree assault and reckless driving.

Brotzler v. County of Scott


No. C1-87-2329


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


427 N.W.2d 685; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 648



 July 11, 1988, Decided  
July 19, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for review denied September 16, 1988.
Review denied by Brotzler v. County of Scott, 1988 Minn. LEXIS 439 (Minn., Sept. 16, 1988)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Scott County District Court, Hon. Michael A. Young, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a summary judgment entered by the Scott County District Court (Minnesota), which dismissed all of his 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and state tort claims against respondents, a county, county attorneys, the Minnesota State Highway Patrol, two cities, and various law enforcement agencies and officers.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed the instant civil suit after he was acquitted on charges of theft by swindle, failure to register motor vehicles, failure to pay state motor vehicle tax, fraudulently applying for certificates of title, and other related charges. Appellant alleged civil rights violations under § 1983, together with tort claims for malicious prosecution, misrepresentation, and false arrest. On appeal, the court held that the trial court properly granted summary judgment to respondents. The attorneys were entitled to absolute prosecutorial immunity, which appellant was unable to overcome by mere allegations of bad faith, malice, or conspiracy. Similarly, appellant failed to overcome the law enforcement officers' qualified immunity. Appellant's allegations against the cities and the county under § 1983 were properly dismissed because they lacked factual support. Finally, the State Highway Patrol was an agency of the State and was not a "person" subject to suit under § 1983.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment entered by the trial court.

 

1384 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stegner


No. C7-87-2495


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 628



July 6, 1988, Decided  
July 12, 1988, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the trial court (Minnesota), which convicted him of felony theft of property with a value over $ 2500 in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.52, subd. 3(2) (1986).


OVERVIEW: After defendant was charged with theft, he chose to proceed pro se in spite of repeated warnings by the court of the dangers of doing so. Following his conviction, defendant asserted on appeal that the trial court erred in failing to appoint counsel for him and in failing to elicit a knowing and intelligent waiver of his right to counsel. The court affirmed the judgment. The court noted that the record established that defendant was intelligent, articulate, and capable of understanding the dangers of self-representation. He told the court that he would not qualify financially for appointed counsel and he was warned several times of the disadvantages of proceeding pro se. The court concluded that on the record there was a valid waiver of the right to counsel. Defendant also argued that Minn. R. Crim. P. 26.04 was unconstitutional because it deprived a pro se defendant of sufficient time to challenge his waiver by post-trial motion. The court held that ignorance of procedural rules, including time limitations, was one of the dangers of waiving the right to counsel and that defendant could not claim the rules themselves were unconstitutional because he was unaware of them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Beer Wholesalers, Inc. v. Miller Brewing Co.


No. C5-88-285


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


426 N.W.2d 438; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 597; 1988-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P68,108



 June 14, 1988  
June 21, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Beer Wholesalers, Inc. v. Miller Brewing Co., 1988 Minn. LEXIS 699 (Minn., Aug. 24, 1988)
Writ of certiorari denied Beer Wholesalers, Inc. v. Miller Brewing Co., 489 U.S. 1039, 109 S. Ct. 1173, 103 L. Ed. 2d 235, 1989 U.S. LEXIS 606 (1989)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District County District Court, Hon. William B. Christensen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant beer distributor sought review of an order of the District County District Court (Minnesota) that entered summary judgment in favor of appellee beer manufacturer in an action brought by the beer distributor against the beer manufacturer for breach of contract, tortious interference with contract, and antitrust violations.


OVERVIEW: The beer manufacturer sent the beer distributor a written notice of its intent not to renew a distributorship agreement, citing operation deficiencies. Despite the beer distributor's attempt to correct the deficiencies, the agreement expired. The beer distributor filed an action against the beer manufacturer alleging that the notice of nonrenewal constituted a modification and that the beer manufacturer's subsequent conduct breached the modified agreement. The beer distributor also asserted that the beer manufacturer tortiously interfered with its customers, and violated antitrust laws. The complaint was dismissed on summary judgment, and the beer distributor appealed. The court held that: (1) there was no evidence the beer manufacturer intended to renew the agreement if the deficiencies were cured and the notice of nonrenewal was not a modification; (2) Minn. Stat. § 325B.01-.17 (1977) did not apply retroactively to the agreement; (3) the beer distributor failed to raise any genuine issues related to its claims of breach of implied covenant of good faith and tortious interference with contract; and (4) there was no evidence of any unlawful conspiracy to coerce fixed prices.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the beer manufacturer.

 

1387 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Black v. NuAire, Inc.


No. C3-88-219


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


426 N.W.2d 203; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 599



 June 9, 1988  
June 21, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Black v. NuAire, Inc., 1988 Minn. LEXIS 694 (Minn., Aug. 24, 1988)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. John W. Borg, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant shareholder sought review of a decision of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), which entered a judgment dismissing his shareholder derivative action against respondents, corporation, directors, and employees. The shareholder challenged the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 302A.243 (1986). All parties sought review of the partial grant of attorney fees to the shareholder, and respondents appealed the denial of fees.


OVERVIEW: The shareholder initiated his derivative action, and the board of directors appointed a committee of disinterested persons, pursuant to § 302A.243, in order to review the claim. The committee found that the deferred compensation agreement claim had merit, but then it recommended the dismissal of the action after a rescission of the agreement. The trial court found that the committee was duly appointed and investigated in good faith, and it rejected the constitutional challenge to § 302A.243. The court affirmed the dismissal of the action, holding that: 1) § 302A.243 was constitutional because the procedural regulations were within the state's plenary powers; 2) the trial court's review was properly limited to whether the members were disinterested and whether the committee investigated in good faith, with a review of the merits precluded under § 302A.243; 3) because the trial court found a substantial benefit to the corporation by the recission of the compensation agreement, there was no abuse of discretion in granting attorney fees; and 4) a denial of fees under Minn. Stat. § 549.21(2) (1986) was proper, pursuant to a finding that the shareholder did not act in bad faith.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the shareholder derivative action and the grant of partial attorney fees to the shareholder.

 

1388 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


American Family Ins. v. Metropolitan Transit Com.


No. C7-87-2240


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


424 N.W.2d 825; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 558



 June 8, 1988  
June 14, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Hennepin County District Court, Hon. William S. Posten.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer brought an action against respondent Metropolitan Transit Commission (MTC) for a claim of no fault medical expenses incurred by its insured, who was injured while exiting from an MTC bus, in accordance with the Minnesota No-Fault Act, Minn. Stat. § 65B.47, subd. 1 (1984). The Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) granted summary judgment for the MTC, and the insurer sought review.


OVERVIEW: The insured, who was injured on January 28, 1986, made a claim to the MTC for no-fault medical expenses on July 11, 1986. The MTC contended that, because the legislature did not expressly state whether 1986 Minn. Laws ch. 455 § 95, the 1986 amendment to Minn. Stat. § 65B.47, subd. 1 (1984), applied prospectively to all future claims or simply to all future accidents, it intended that the amendment was to apply retroactively to accidents which occurred prior to the amendment. On review, the court reversed, holding that the trial court incorrectly ruled that the amendment applied to all no-fault claims made after its effective date, March 26, 1986. A law was not to be construed to be applied retroactively unless clearly and manifestly so intended by the legislature, and no such intent was shown in the amendment. There was nothing in the amendment's language to indicate that it was to clarify existing law or was to be applied retroactively. Further, retroactive application of the statute did not comport with basic contract law, in that an insurance policy was customarily governed by the law in effect at the time a policy was issued or a contract was made.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment for the MTC.
