Johnston v. Michael Shea & Associates


No. C6-87-2486


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


425 N.W.2d 263; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 529



 May 23, 1988  
May 31, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied July 28, 1988.
Review denied by Johnston v. Michael Shea & Assocs., 1988 Minn. LEXIS 723 (Minn., July 27, 1988)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Hennepin County District Court, Hon. Robert Schumacher, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant social worker sought review of the decision of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment to respondent county in a tort action brought by the social worker in connection with the county's investigation of sexual abuse allegations against her. The social worker also claimed the county violated her rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: The social worker was accused of sexually abusing two girls who had been referred by the county to the clinic in which she worked. When the county undertook an investigation, the social worker sued the county and the clinic. The trial court granted the county's motion for summary judgment and the social worker appealed. The court found that the manner in which the investigation was conducted was clearly discretionary and held that the county was immune from tort liability under Minn. Stat. § 466.03(6) (1986). Turning to the social worker's § 1983 claim, the court found that she had lost no property or liberty interest as a result of the county's actions because the county had no employment relationship with her. Even if the social worker had such an interest, she did not show that the county had a policy or custom that infringed on any constitutionally protected rights. The court also found that the social worker failed to show that the county's policy of investigating allegations of child abuse was the moving force behind any alleged constitutional violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the county.

 

1390 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Quinn


No. C7-88-14


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


422 N.W.2d 763; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 452



 May 3, 1988  
May 10, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Quinn, 1988 Minn. LEXIS 679 (Minn., June 29, 1988)
Reversed by, En banc State v. Quinn, 436 N.W.2d 758, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 41 (Minn., 1989)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Charles Porter, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a pretrial appeal, the State challenged an order of the District Court, Hennepin County (Minnesota), that granted defendants' motion to suppress evidence developed from a wiretap authorized by a wiretap warrant pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 626A.06 (1986) of the Minnesota Privacy of Communications Act (Act), Minn. Stat. ch. 626A (1986).


OVERVIEW: When they filed their motion, defendants were being prosecuted for receiving stolen property, conspiracy to receive stolen property, and theft by swindle. A wiretap had been placed on one of their telephones as part of a police investigation into a shoplifting and fencing operation. The wiretap warrant provided for its own termination in 10 days or when any person specified in the warrant was charged with a specified offense. The district court granted the suppression motion because the termination provision did not require interception to cease once the objective of the authorization was attained. The court affirmed its order. The trial court correctly found that the warrant did not terminate upon attainment of the authorized objective, or in any event in 10 days, as required by Minn. Stat. § 626A.06, subd. 4(h) (1986) of the Act. Strict compliance with the Act was required, and a provision for termination when a suspect was charged was not equivalent to attainment of an authorized objective. Although the nature of the operation permitted broad objectives, the warrant's termination upon a charge against a person who was not named in the warrant application was arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order.

Caucus Distributors, Inc. v. Commissioner of Commerce


No. C4-87-1952


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


422 N.W.2d 264; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 212



 April 22, 1988, Decided  
April 22, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied, June 10, 1988.
Review denied by Caucus Distribs. v. Comm'r of Commerce, 1988 Minn. LEXIS 637 (Minn., June 10, 1988)
Writ of certiorari denied Caucus Distributors, Inc. v. Minnesota Comm'r of Commerce, 488 U.S. 1006, 109 S. Ct. 786, 102 L. Ed. 2d 778, 1989 U.S. LEXIS 110 (1989)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari to Department of Commerce.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This matter came before the court on writ for certiorari to review a decision of respondent, who found that the promissory notes relators offered and sold in exchange for loans, were unlicensed securities under Minn. Stat. § 80A.14 (18). Relators argued that these were merely promissory notes.


OVERVIEW: Relators asked an elderly widow to lend money to their campaign organization. They issued her several promissory notes at attractive interest rates, and she expected to be repaid. Respondent ordered relators to cease offering or selling unfiled promissory notes without obtaining an opinion letter from the department of commerce. Portions of relators' brief and appendix were considered immaterial and stricken.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed respondent's order that the promissory notes which relators issued, constituted securities under the statute. The state securities laws, as applied to relator's fund raising activities, did not impermissibly infringe on relator's first amendment right of association.

Rambaum v. Swisher


No. C0-87-2192


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


423 N.W.2d 68; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 412



 April 19, 1988, Decided  
April 26, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Rambaum v. Swisher, 1988 Minn. LEXIS 565 (Minn., June 29, 1988)
Affirmed by Rambaum v. Swisher, 435 N.W.2d 19, 1989 Minn. LEXIS 4 (Minn., 1989)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Dakota County; Hon. Eugene Atkins, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant fraternal organization appealed the judgment of the District Court, Dakota County (Minnesota) in favor of plaintiff injured person. The injured person was seriously injured when he was struck by a car driven by defendant driver. The injured person sued the driver on a theory of negligence and defendant bar and the fraternal organization for the illegal sale of alcohol to the driver, who was an obviously intoxicated person.


OVERVIEW: The fraternal organization contended on appeal that the jury's finding that alcoholic beverage sales to non-club members was illegal was in error and that the joint and several liability statute, Minn. Stat. § 604.02(1) (1986), violated constitutional rights of equal protection. The injured person challenged the trial court's reduction of the jury award by the amount for which the injured person settled with the bar and the constitutionality of § 604.07(2) (1986), which required future damage awards reduced to present value. The court reversed, in part, the trial court's judgment reducing the injured person's recovery by the amount the injured person had settled with the bar, because a reduction of a verdict discouraged settlement of lawsuits and provided the other defendants a windfall.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, in part, the trial court's holding that the sale of alcoholic beverages to the driver by the fraternal organization and bar was illegal. The court reversed, in part, the trial court's reduction of the injured person's damages and remanded the case for determination of payments from the fraternal organization.

Wolter v. Hasse


Nos. C6-87-1953, CX-87-2426


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 375



April 12, 1988, Decided  
April 19, 1988, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION WILL BE UNPUBLISHED AND MAY NOT BE CITED EXCEPT AS PROVIDED BY MINNESOTA STATUTES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Wolter v. Haase, 1988 Minn. LEXIS 450 (Minn., June 23, 1988)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant personal injury victim sought review of a judgment from the trial court (Minnesota), which applied Minn. Stat. § 604.07 (1986), the discount statute, to his noneconomic damages in his action against respondent automobile owners. The owners sought review of the trial court's calculation of prejudgment interest and the application of the collateral source rule.


OVERVIEW: The victim was injured when a driver swerved around the owners' two vehicles, which were stopped on the edge of the road, and collided head-on with the victim's car. The victim received a jury verdict for past economic and noneconomic damages. Franke v. Farm Bureau Mut. Ins. Co.

Court of Appeals of Minnesota


421 N.W.2d 406; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 206



 March 18, 1988, Decided  
March 29, 1988, Filed

OVERVIEW: The insured was a passenger in a car that collided with a second car. Holstad v. Southwestern Porcelain


No. C0-87-2032


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


421 N.W.2d 371; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 168; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P11,721; 5 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. 2d (Callaghan) 912



 March 16, 1988, Decided  
March 22, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Holstad v. Southwestern Porcelain, Inc., 1988 Minn. LEXIS 622 (Minn., Apr. 28, 1988)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Kandiyohi County District Court, Hon. John C. Lindstrom, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant buyer filed an action against respondents, a manufacturer and a seller, for breach of express and implied warranties under the Uniform Commercial Code, negligence, and strict products liability. The Kandiyohi County District Court (Minnesota) granted summary judgment for respondents, and the buyer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The buyer purchased a prefabricated silo for use on his dairy farm that was manufactured and installed by respondents. The buyer sought to recover damages for the loss of feed and decreased milk production based on his claim that the losses resulted from his cow's eating feed which had gone bad from exposure to air entering through a tear discovered in the silo. The trial court granted summary judgment for respondents. The court affirmed the judgment. The court held that the sale and installation of the silo was predominantly a sale of goods and thus subject to the U.C.C. Since the U.C.C. warranties applied to the installation of the silo, the U.C.C. four year statute of limitations set forth in Minn. Stat. § 336.2-725 (1978), applied. There was no evidence that respondents knew or should have known about the torn air bad. Hence, the statute of limitations was not tolled, and the buyer's warranty claim was time barred. Because defendant sought damages for economic loss arising from a commercial transaction, he was barred from maintaining his tort action because there was no damage to other property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgments granted in favor of respondents on the buyer's action for breach of warranties under the U.C.C., negligence, and strict products liability.

 

1396 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Bergmann v. Melrose


No. C0-87-2046


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


420 N.W.2d 663; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 320



 March 9, 1988, Decided  
March 15, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from District Court, Stearns County; Hon. Roger Klaphake, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant holder of a liquor license challenged a judgment of the District Court, Stearns County (Minnesota), that sustained a decision of respondent city denying the holder's application to renew his liquor license because there were unpaid real estate taxes and assessments on the property and because the holder had failed to meet a condition of the license requiring him to operate a family restaurant in conjunction with his liquor store.


OVERVIEW: When the holder's license to operate a liquor store was first granted, he agreed to the condition that he would also operate a family restaurant on the premises, but no restaurant was operated during the last three years before the holder applied to renew the license. Because of a dispute between the holder and a third party, real estate taxes and special assessments on the premises went unpaid for several years. The court affirmed the judgment. It was not arbitrary, capricious, and unreasonable to condition the license on the operation of a family restaurant. The city reasonably encouraged operation of a family restaurant because it had no other such restaurant, while it had several other liquor stores. The city did not act arbitrarily and capriciously in denying the license under a city ordinance because of the unpaid taxes and assessments. The holder's equal protection rights were not violated because a condition on a liquor license was a legitimate exercise of the city's police powers and it was rational for the city to conclude that the condition might induce the operation of a family restaurant. The appeal was not frivolous, and the city was not entitled to attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

Qualle v. County of Beltrami

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of a judgment of the Beltrami County District Court (Minnesota), which reversed the county's decision to freeze respondent administrator's salary.


OVERVIEW: The administrator had been the clerk of the court for 20 years. When the Minnesota Pay Equity Act (Act), Minn. Stat. Ann. § 471.991-999 (1986), was passed, the county hired a consultant to insure compliance. Each county department head was assigned a rating for several factors relating to the position. The administrator position was assigned a level which made the administrator's salary higher than the level called for. The administrator's salary was frozen. The court refused to review the constitutional issue because the county did not raise it in a timely manner. The court held that the trial court's decision was not clearly erroneous. The court concluded that the trial court's decision was not contrary to the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Leonard v. Parrish


No. C8-87-1386


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


420 N.W.2d 629; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 305



March 8, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Ramsey County; Hon. Bertrand Poritsky, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant passenger sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which denied her motion for a new trial. The passenger was injured in a collision between a motorcycle and a car. The jury found respondents, a motorcycle driver and a car driver, negligent but reduced the passenger's recovery under Minn. Stat. § 169.974, subd. 6 because she was not wearing a helmet at the time of the accident.


OVERVIEW: In the accident, the passenger was thrown from the motorcycle and struck her head and body on a street. The passenger sustained a skull fracture and other head injuries. The parties earlier stipulated to the use of expert testimony and the burden of production on whether damages could have been reduced by the use of a helmet. Minn. Stat. § 169.974, subd. 6 (1986) allowed for a reduction of damages for damages for head injuries of a person who was not wearing protective headgear to the extent that those injuries could have been avoided by wearing protective headgear that complied with certain safety standards. Under the stipulation, the passenger agreed to forfeit the opportunity to challenge the jury's right to consider the issue. On appeal, the court affirmed the denial of the passenger's motion for a new trial. Section 169.974, subd. 6 did not violate the passenger's rights under the Minnesota or United States Constitution. The evidence supported a damage reduction under § 169.974, subd. 6. In addition, the trial court did not err in limiting certain proposed jury instructions and voir dire questions, or in performing the present-value discounting function.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the passenger's motion for a new trial.

 

1399 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Gjovik v. Breiland


No. C6-87-1807


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 308



March 8, 1988, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] This opinion will be unpublished and may not be cited except as provided by Minn. Stat. § 480A.08, subd. 3 (Supp. 1987).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual sought review of a judgment of the trial court (Minnesota), which awarded damages in the individual's action against respondents, owner and driver of a vehicle involved in an accident in which the individual was injured.


OVERVIEW: The individual's knee was injured in the accident and he alleged that he was required to have a total knee replacement one year later as a result. Respondents argued that the individual's knee injury was related to an injury seven years prior to the accident. The individual had three operations for the previous injury and was considered a likely candidate for a total knee replacement. The previous injury forced the individual to retire. The individual appealed from the trial court's award of damages as inadequate. The court held that the award of damages for past wage loss, although less than a stipulation on the record, was not given under the influence of passion or prejudice. The court further held that Minn. Stat. Ann. § 604.07 (1986), which discounted future damages, was not unconstitutional. Finally, the court held that the "collateral source" statute, Minn. Stat. Ann. § 548.36, subd. 1(2) (1986) was constitutional as applied to the individual.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1400 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Normandale Properties, Inc.


No. C3-87-2106


Court of Appeals of Minnesota


420 N.W.2d 259; 1988 Minn. App. LEXIS 316



 March 8, 1988, Decided  
March 15, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Normandale Props., 1988 Minn. LEXIS 585 (Minn., May 4, 1988)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Hennepin County; Hon. Charles A. Porter, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which dismissed charges of attempted unlawful disposal of hazardous wastes against respondent company.


OVERVIEW: An Environmental Services inspector received a report that someone was unlawfully attempting to dispose of hazardous waste at an address. He inspected the property and found 15 containers hidden under sheetrock in the dumpster. The containers had a strong solvent odor and many had the words "hazardous waste" written on them. The property was managed by the company. The inspector spoke with a company employee who said that he had put the containers in the dumpster at his boss's direction. The containers had been left by a tenant in another city. The company tried to dispose of the containers in a dumpster at another property but they were rejected by the waste hauler. The employee then put the containers where the were found. The company was charged with attempted unlawful disposal of hazardous waste. The trial court dismissed the charges on vagueness grounds. The State appealed. The court noted that a statute which did not implicate first amendment freedoms was facially void for vagueness only if it was vague in all its applications. The court held that Minn. Stat. Ann. § 115.071, subd. 2a(a) (1986) was not facially void, nor was it vague in its application to the company.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.
